et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And then the pain will cease, as we have said in the liver abscess. 
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear where the patients now die, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mouse according to the divisions of the cures we have said, and it does not profit at all, then apply three methods of cautery which are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	Of these, one method is that you make III or IV cauteries, aligning according to the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the liver cautery that we have mentioned before; 
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient often turn on his back;
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	and another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has II points, as we have shown in the shoulder dislocation;
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and lift the heart which is located near the mouse, or where the sides of the patient come towards the left, and let the elevations from which you lift the heart be according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries be according to the width of the body. 
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	After he puts the two inflamed nerves so that the heart is pierced from the other side, and then draws fire from the cautery, and thus he will have four. 
Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	And if you see, that cauterizing the whole cautery to three nerves.  
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has festered for a long time, this is worth more than the other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is of no use for dropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you cure it according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your cure does not profit at all, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the shoulder blade, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the thigh, and two behind the back on the spine, and one at the breast;  
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	and let the cauteries be very close to the species of the heart. 
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	After leave the cautery uncovered for a long time to prevent putrefaction, and do not leave the patient's care after the cautery; 
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	And healing would hasten, and both intentions would be fulfilled with the help of God. 
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	The shape of the cautery for the belly is the cleaver that we have shown before; 
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	and the one for the back should be oval-shaped, according to what has been mentioned before.  
de l’enfleure des piez	from the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsy-stricken and are full of yellow water, it is fitting that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; 
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	and apply your hand with the cautery without turning.  
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply with the point, lest you burn the surrounding flesh excessively, and let the cautery be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	Afterward, make two cauteries on each leg at the point of the knife; 
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and the other behind, midway up the leg; 
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	and let the cauteries lie long without cleaning so that it may rise. 
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	after the cure of the other cures that we have said. 
de la menoison	Of the setting
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	When a solution of the stomach comes from cold and moisture, as long as the retentive and digestive powers which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by ordinary methods; 
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	and you see the patient suffering greatly and of strong constitution, then make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said before or a stomach cautery, a circular cautery;
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	and four cauteries around the belly subtle and all the cauteries subtly pinned, and two cauteries on the hips. 
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the wrist, and a cautery on each arm, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the navel, for the cure is beneficial when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	When hemorrhoids are at the fundament, one or several, and they are old and made up of thick cold and damp corrupted humors, and they are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit, then make cauteries. 
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	III on the spine of the back, which is all behind below the armpit bit by bit in a triangle, and I the cautery below the shoulder II must. 
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	And if you think that his stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then on the face one puts a large cautery on the stomach, as it is previously said, and another on the liver, and another on the thigh with all the cauteries clavile. 
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	And let the cautery stay open for a long time. 
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing the place until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	When you cut an althelul (likely a type of bandage or dressing), if it is heated so that it seems like a razor, and then put all inflamed on the said althelul.
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	And you leave it so that both your hand and the cautery come to the beginning of the vein, so that the blood is cut.
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	Do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of swelling, cauterize each one as we have said. 
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	After the treatment of wounds, make sure they are healed.
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	And if you cauterize a large area with a large cautery, it will be more helpful. 
de plaie mal curee	of a wound poorly healed
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will describe in their place, then there comes a disease that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula comes and is aged and has putrid rotting moisture, then you must test its depth with a delicate probe, and be careful that you know the entire depth of how many parts it has.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	After heating the cautery which resembles a razor, insert it into the fistula according to the amount that the tentacle has entered, and start again with the cautery until those corrupted and rotten bodies are burned once, twice or three times depending on the amount needed. 
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	And be careful not to burn the nerves that are there, and the large veins.  
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestines, be careful of these areas, and do not cauterize except in a fleshy place, and remember that it is not a piercing.  
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	After treatment the place until it is healed, and if the wound is closed and the matter is removed for a long time, then know that the wound is completely healed.  
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	And if the matter is not removed, know that the wound is bad, and it corrupts the bone at its base. 
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	And as one of these that we will say in its place. 
de la maladie des reins	of the sickness of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	When pain from cold comes as rain, and from great windiness, and does not take solace from a woman, then it is fitting that you make a cautery on the reins on one side and the other with the pointed cautery that we have previously said. 
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	And if we cauterize them in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will do more help.  
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the back part above the bladder where the hairs begin at the hipbone, on the right and left, and let each cautery be as long as the tip of a thumb.
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	And make him fire the cautery on his back wherever you need it. 
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	Let the cautery be sharpened according to the shape previously mentioned. 
de la marris	from the marsh
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	When the matrix is cold and moist, and does not allow conception because the flowers are corrupted and their ends are delayed; 
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	and when they come, there is great pain:
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	then it is fitting to make three cauteries around the buttocks as we have said of the bladder cautery, and two cauteries on his back.
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	And let the cauteries be sharpened as we have said. 
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	When viscous moisture descends to the hip joint and for this reason it moves from its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	and the place of separation is found on two sides, it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the bone of the hip in a circle-shaped burn, and mark in front of the place around the bone as it turns, so that the bone is inside the circle. 
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	And let the cautery be such as those with which one cauterizes the stomach. 
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	And if this cautery is not present, make three large olive-wood cauteries, and let the cautery be as perfect as all the others.  
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cauterize it until it is healed. 
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When pain comes to the bone of the hip, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured by what we have said in the division and the cure is ineffective, and the illness is old: 
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	Then it is necessary that you purge the patient of gross humors with foul-smelling pills, or other good-seeming pills. 
Aprés li fai cautere;	Afterward apply the cautery; 
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	and the manner of applying the cautery is according to two methods: 
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	that is to say, together burning medicaments and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	Fire cautery is according to many methods, of which one is as follows:  
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	that you cauterize on the box of the hip three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them deep and large, and put between each cautery a space the thickness of two fingers, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped.  
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Once done, make one cautery in the middle above the head of the hip, so there are four according to this form:  
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	And if you see, if the cauterizer with a cautery makes a circle as we have said before in the dislocation of the hip; 
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	But make it in such a way that the circles encompass the whole hip, and all the flesh around the heart be burned. 
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done for sciatica, when the pain stays in the hip, and does not reach as far as the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	And if it comes up to the thigh and leg, make two cauteries there where the patient says the pain is strongest, and one cautery above the ankle four times, on the left side a prick. 
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	And let the cauteries be sharp-edged, and burn through the thickness of the flesh. 
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers of the foot or nearby, then cauterize him there where he feels the pain three times or four times with a cautery called "point". 
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	And if it is necessary, make them more; 
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a cautery with a knife-shaped or circular cautery, and take great care in all your cauteries that you do not leave it so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more pain and contraction. 
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have done cautery on the ankle of the foot, and they let it until the leg was all swollen, and the foot also, and it was pierced and corrupted all the foot.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purging of the belly from which he had death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make a cautery on one and the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the surgeons say about cautery of the hip, which is the manner: make such a tool and at its head as thick as a nail, or a little less, and it should be grooved, from one groove to the other with a space the size of a thumb's knot; 
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	and let the grooves be facing in two parts, and also be like knots, and it should have a well-made iron handle;
et c’est li forme:	And this is the form: 
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	And it should be heated until it is all red and feels hot, and then put it on the box of the bad hip, and it should be turned on the healthy side; 
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	and the cautery one time when the cautery is red hot and leave it for III days;
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	And then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; 
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the cure with ointment until it is healed. 
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	 Albucasim says that we use this cautery little because of the fear of its appearance, and we rarely see anyone who uses it; 
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	and nevertheless it is a good cautery, for whoever can endure it, and where it is applied.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The cauteries of burning medicine are such that you make an instrument with crossbars in which the edge of the door descends, and it is made of iron or steel with a long handle, and at its height there are two knobs, and between each knob there is the thickness of a finger;  
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	and they should be opened with fire and above, and joined together according to this form: 
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	Then place the box of the hip on the patient lying on his sound side, and immediately put your hand very firmly on the box of the hip; 
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Then place between the two circles of a hot awl that has been heated in the fire for one hour or so, and let the patient suffer the heat and burning sensation.  
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	For there is a biting sensation as well as from fire. 
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	And when the biting sensation has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and remove the hip awl gently, and leave it like that for three days, and apply butter until what is black from the burn is removed. 
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	And let it stay for three days so that putrefaction is drawn out;
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and this would be the last help after the treatment of ointments until it is healed 
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or leg, you must make the instrument that holds tight according to what you have done in the hip properly; 
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	and this is the way of the hot awe, and I wrote it or treated it in the treatise on the correction of medicine. 
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	where there be a small opening so that the point of a razor can enter; 
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and put that pot on top of another pot well sealed, and put alkali and lime and soft heat on top until there are two handfuls of powder and you will have prepared it well in your hand; 
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	and leave it like that until hot and thick vapor descends into the sealed pot, then take all that vapor, and pour it onto heat and alkali as before. 
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And then it will be very acute and is administered in soft work of medicine and cauteries on other members. 
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	For it performs other work like fire, and if with other medicines which one cauterizes well the hip thus turpentine and honey of sumac and chalk with soap, all these things mixed together. 
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a remedy by which a man was cured of the pain in his hip and sciatic vein, and he praised it greatly, saying that no other remedy was done, and that he was healed at one time when this remedy was done, and he bathed himself as he teaches here after.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And say in this manner that you take two drachmas of fresh green litharge and grind it very much with a bit of fat and put it on the hip and on the thigh and on the leg where the pain lies and bind it. 
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And leave it for three hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning.  
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make it enter or bathe so that its body is a little aroused, and make it enter or bed, and the pain will go away entirely and it will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a cautery of such medicines, unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat droppings, it helps a lot.
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And it must be done in this manner. 
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen cloth and soak it with old oil and put it on the hollow between the thumb and the finger which is called the fossa.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	After you take goat horns that are dry, and burn them until they are charcoal, then put them on wool, and leave them until they are extinguished. 
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	And do this again likewise, and do not cease to do so until you think by feeling that it reaches the hip, and that the pain is gone. 
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	And this manner of cautery is called "goat horn cautery". 
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or by percussion or by excessive evacuation, or by similar spread of cold matter, none of these cases are worth cautery except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is fitting that after this the patient is purged with fetid pills or other similar things, and that they are made on their back, where the pain lies, three lines marked with an inch, and in each line five cauteries or more according to the strength and quantity that the patient can endure. 
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	And let the cauteries be made according to the cautery that is called "points".
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	and if you see it, make three or four cauteries with a medium-sized fire cautery according to this form: 
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	This disease often comes to young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a tight throat when they wake up, and fear; 
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes upon the other spines.  
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you want to cauterize it, then cauterize it with a branding iron according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery properly burns each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, if you cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery making two or three lines, and the points are close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After healing the place until it is healed according to what we have said, and be careful that you do not apply the cautery in a gibbosity which is in the spasm of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When joint pains are from moistures that are spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which the doctor properly calls "gout," and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: 
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	Make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form: 
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need for you to grasp the face of the foot, if you burn it with the whole cautery we call "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains come to the knees and other joints, which happens often, then make a cautery on each knee three or four cauteries on each side, with olive oil. 
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand too long so that only the thickness of a kernel is burned. 
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend as far as the knee and back, apply the cautery that we have described in our chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the wrist two lines. 
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	And if there is any pain left in the arms, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand. 
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains come to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good governance to the patient and take medicine. 
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give it good governance and purge phlegm, it will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the fracture of the bone
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When a rupture comes in the groin and the bowels descend to the buttocks and it is recent, it is necessary that when you see it cleansed, he should not eat anything that day.
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and let him use things which loosen the belly so that the bowels descend from his belly 
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands and command him to hold his breath while the bowels are repaired and set them right at your will, and press down below the break on the bone of the shoulder blade and at all one sign that resembles half a circle above the body 
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then heat the cautery which has this shape 
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it drips pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then reset the bowels to their place 
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and have the assistant hold his hand so they do not return backwards 
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and work well on the patient's thighs and put a cushion under him and a sergeant on his thighs and another on his foot who holds his hands 
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	then put the cautery on the sign with all your hand and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone and if you do not reach it the first time start again another time until you arrive at the bone 
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	and carefully guard so that the eye does not weep when you do the cautery. 
que tu ne le brulasses;	so that you do not burn it.  
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and so that through this, the patient does not die or suffer other ills. 
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is fitting that the cauteries for children be subtle according to their age, and those for adults as large according to theirs.  
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	After three days, treat the area of the cautery with butter until the burning is removed.  
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	Afterward, treat it with other remedies until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days so that the wound heals well. 
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is fitting that his bandages be loosened gradually, so that the eye does not weep when he prepares to go into rooms. 
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, give him a well-made bandage and have him wear it for forty other days. 
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	and let him have good rest, that he work little and guard against too much drinking and eating, and too loud shouting; 
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	and when he follows this instruction he will be completely healed. 
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here afterwards the treatment of cutting in this chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Of the breaking of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When tumors come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, make a cautery with a cautery according to its quantity, and burn one-third of the core; 
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the cure according to what we have said; 
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the ancients have said that one should cauterize it with a three-angled cautery according to this form: 
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first mark the place of the incision and make a line across the width above the break, and another behind it, and hold your hand steady with the entire hot iron.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from falling or being struck, and this pain lasts a long time, and medicine does not help it, then it should be cauterized with the cautery that is called "points," and let the cautery be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and strength and its location of twists and turns and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	if it is healed from the first cautery, it is good; 
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	if not, start another cautery on top of the first one, because it is customary that it should change to the member that is closest to it, so it is necessary that you make the cauteries until the patient is healed. 
de meselerie	from surgery
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The mesentery is helped sometimes by cautery with great help, and the same disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	If you see it cauterize, take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not spread nor remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the sick person, then do V cauteries on the head: 
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	I smear the head with new [ointment], and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hairs; 
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	and two on the two horns, and one behind on the nape;
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	and I leave as long as your hand that the cauteries reach to the bone, and as long as the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape;
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	and cauterize above the mouse according to what is before it. 
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the misery is everywhere scattered; 
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and it loses visibly, then you must cauterize with those cauteries that we have said or the chief one and two cauteries on the spine of the neck and six cauteries on the spine of the back and one large one on the rump and another nearby and two on the two shoulders; 
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and two on the elbows and two on the tendons of the foot and one on each joint of the hands and feet and on the pits of the hands; 
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and beware of the nerves that are on the heel bone, so that you do not burn them;
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and never make a cautery on the bone of the elbow and one other on the bone of the stomach and one other on the liver. 
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And know that when you do more cautery, you help more, and it increases the benefit. 
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that sick people do not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because the body is already all corrupted. 
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the manner of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After healing, cover the wound with flour mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When swelling comes in a limb and is treated with medicine and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then make cauteries on the limb according to its size. 
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	And let the cauteries be a prick entering into the thickness of the flesh.  
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it with unguents until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And sometimes one makes a cautery on the hand and foot and back, at the point where the nerve moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed. 
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And nonetheless no one should interfere with it unless they know the limbs and the outlets of the nerves that move the body.  
de albaras	of alabaster
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the illness which is called "albaras" is old, and the engine of medicine is worthless, then cauterize a perfect spot with a cautery, according to the quantity of the species of the heart, until the whiteness is removed, and its color is changed. 
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	Then make a plaster of flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of dove and blood of almond, of each one part. 
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and air it in place until it is healed. 
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of a chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a chancre first appears, and you see it stopping, then cauterize it with a cautery iron that resembles a circle, encircling the entire chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And nevertheless the wise say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the ulcer;
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	and nevertheless it does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen several times; 
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	and further back it is necessary that he be cauterized around with the cautery which is called "circle," as we have said in the discourse of cauteries. 
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot move
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When someone has an ailment which is called "adubelati," and it delays in dying either because of the superfluity it causes or because of the weakness of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say, too old) and he has little blood, or because of time; 
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you wish to hasten its death:
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	then cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking. 
aprés le laisse ensi.	afterwards leave it thus.  
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce through all of the cautery, heat the cautery as follows.
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of that illness which is called "adubelati" as long as the cautery has pierced the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it burning in this way so that the course of the rot is relieved.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure by fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	There is another kind of illness which is called "corrodens," and it is nothing other than a gnawing away of the limbs, for it eats at the limbs just as fire eats at dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this ailment in a place which can suffer cautery with fire, then heat the cauteries very small and large according to what suits the place where the ailment is; 
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	After cauterizing all sides so that you eradicate all the corruption and nothing of it remains, so that everything which is corrupted is removed. 
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days and put on the wounds cauterized soft bread crumbs with oil until the burns from the fire are removed, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of wounds engendering flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good;  
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	and if not, begin the cautery again on what remains of the corrupted flesh. 
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this ailment has sometimes been cured with a hot medicinal wash in place of fire cautery;
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	but nevertheless fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already mentioned the cure with a hot medicinal wash in the division: 
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	take it when you need it. 
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Of the leeches that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that with fire a disease arises which is called "closed" according to our understanding, and it is a large evil thing which bleeds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries for this disease are according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know fire cautery, and hot iron cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Fire cautery is when you heat the cautery iron as hot as a goose feather quill and make it of good iron to the measure that it can burn the nail on all sides, and that it has delicate edges. 
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	After placing it all hot on the nail, turn your hand around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail. 
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	And leave it like that for three days until it begins to rot. 
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Then make a plaster of wild mallows ground with salt, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.  
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the place of cautery by anointing it with fat until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are converted by fire the body, and it often happens in hands and feet, then it is necessary that you administer a hot iron cautery. 
et est en teil maniere:	And it is in this manner: 
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	Take a cane of iron or steel, or a feather of an arrow, and put it on the nail and the surrounding flesh, that is to say warts.  
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	And put the cane on so that it surrounds it entirely, then apply a piece of hot coal, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand in turning so that the edge of the cane reaches the root of the nail, and the hot iron can find its way deep to the root. 
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	and let the patient suffer a bite from the hot iron for an hour; 
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	then leave it like that, and all its roots will be pulled out.  
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Then do one after another, until you remove all those that are on the body, then treat the inflammations which produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When someone trembles from cold nerves, or a quartan fever or another, it is fitting that you make them four cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; 
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and one cautery on the foot, and one on the stomach with an olive cautery;  
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	they will stop trembling, and their health will quickly recover from the cold illness. 
des pustules puans	Of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes appear by fire burns on the body, or stinking pustules, which come from corrupt large matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	it is fitting, at first when they appear, that one make a cautery on each head of the pustule:  
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	a subtle cautery from myrtle wood, in which the point is grasped by fire, or a long aristolochia root, or a lentil cautery. 
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And never apply cautery at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further in front, but the superfluity from which they come is broken, and they are healed. 
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	But it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood. 
quant li artere est copee	When an artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times there are great outpourings of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound which comes to the firebrand, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cauterization of a limb, and similar things; 
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	and it is a very grievous thing to staunch. 
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And nevertheless when this happens to anyone, if you hurry to put your index finger on the wound of the vein and press it very hard until the blood is quieted beneath your finger and no drop issues forth; 
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	Then put several small and large olive oil cauters on the fire until they are all red. 
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Then take one, large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is located, and put the cauter on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cauter on it until the blood is stopped up. 
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it leaps forward when you lift your hand from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another cautery that is in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not stop doing this one after another until the blood is stopped up. 
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	And be careful that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient;  
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	And know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well stopped up immediately, especially when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways that we have said. 
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by a strong ligature of thread, or by medicines placed on top which have the power to stop blood.
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	and let it be bound and restrained tightly. 
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who would apply a bandage tightly with cloths or put burning things on it, or other similar things, it will not help and will do harm.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if this happens to anyone and they have neither mirror nor medicine present, they should put their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press well until it is rested upon the wound and upon the vein; 
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	and do not move it but moisten it with cold water often so that it is very cold until the blood is frozen and thickened and rested; 
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	and make inquiries beforehand about those who need to cauterize and those who need medicine. 
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the cures of cutting
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and the uses and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; 
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	and I have put this chapter from the top to the bottom, and I will go in this chapter by the same way so that those who wish can find it more easily. 
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this one, it befits, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than the first of the cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter there is often evacuation of blood when opening a vein and incising an abscess and in the treatment of wounds and in the extraction of arrows and in cutting into stones and similar things 
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	where there is doubt and fear and many die. 
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	if there are some who torment themselves so much with their illness that they die easily because of the fierceness they find in their illness and its severity 
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	and from these one must have fear. 
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And there are some who give you their sense and say:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	“wait, I am cured” 
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put greater caution in your honor than in your greed, and do not act foolishly but wisely of those of whom you are certain and of whom you can take oaths.
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	and use prognosis and indication in the treatments of your patients so that health may be converted. 
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And this will help you to acquire good reputation, glory, and long remembrance. 
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and uprightness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordained this chapter in divisions by chapters, according to that which is before it or the chapter of cauteries, that I have devised from the head down to the feet, so that you may more easily find that which you shall need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	A head full of sharp pain
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	Know that this ailment often comes to children at birth, and when the midwife pulls the baby's head too forcefully; 
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	and sometimes it comes from a cause unknown.  
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this ailment except in children, and all those I have seen hastened towards death; 
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	and for this reason it seems to me better to leave such treatments to others.  
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw a child whose shoulders were full of pain, and whose head grew larger each day until it could no longer support it; 
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture gathered below the bone above the shoulder blade, between the heart and the bone; 
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and the works are such if moisture is between the flesh and bone, and the abscesses are small, that you split between the head a wide fissure; 
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and it be also as long as two fingers, while the moisture flows;
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and see this shape of a spatula: 
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more abundant and the abscess is larger, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, like this:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	And if the moisture is below the bone, and the signs that you see are the corners of the head open on each side, and the sharp pain leaps forth when you press it with your hand inside, and this is not answered by you: 
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	then it befits that you split between the head three fissures according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	Afterwards, remove the fissures with cloths and powders, and he puts wine and oil, and leaves it thus until the fifth day; 
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	then he unbinds it, and heals the wound with bandages and ointments, and leaves the head to be straightened equally, and let the patient eat dry meat free of moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed. 
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another way of incision is that you look where the size of the abscess appears, and the gathering of the point; 
car aucune fois est elle devant;	for it is never in front; 
aucune fois derrier;	never behind;  
aucune fois en destre;	never to the right; 
et aucune fois en senestre.	and never to the left. 
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Therefore cut there where the abscess appears, and the gathering of the point, and make the incision according to your power; 
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and be careful not to cut an artery; 
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and a vein flows blood so that the patient dies from the flow of blood and evacuation of moisture.  
de reume	of rheumatism
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When there occurs in someone an ailment called "catarrh" in the eyes or in the breast and the ailment is old, and the cure of medicine does not profit at all, then the last resort is cautery with which one severs the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	Therefore it is necessary, when you see them cut, for the patient to turn their head back; 
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	afterwards rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then pull the patient's neck to the whole cloth;
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	Then look where the vein flows, and the temples on each side are behind the ears, and they are filled. 
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then mark the temples with a notch, then cut one and the other with a sharp knife of two parts, until the vein reaches the bone, and this should be done across the breadth of the head. 
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see it, put the spatula below the artery and the cup above, cutting as much as it must through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if the blood flows continuously upward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery does not open to the touch, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of space of three fingers, then mark a notch and cut down to the bone; 
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	and as much blood as is needed to withdraw should be six ounces, and perhaps a bit more or less, according to what the patient can endure and the fullness of the artery.  
puis regarde la plaie:	Then look at the wound: 
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If it remains on the bone and there is a pustule, cut it so that pus does not flow in, then drain the wound and bandage it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.  
de emigrainne	from migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes, and acute catarrh, due to moisture from tears and the heat in the temples and a strong ancient humoral imbalance and similar things, and it is treated by medical remedies and all of this does him no good, then we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the manner of extracting them is such that the patient should make a fist with the hairs of his temples and listen to the artery which opens in the temple for it opens well by its beating and is less full outside than in some men who are too cold; 
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	and if it is full, the patient should tighten his neck with some cloths, then rub the place with a rough cloth and raise the place with hot water so that the artery appears clearly. 
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Then take the spatula of which this is the shape:  
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	then scrape the skin slightly until you reach the artery, then lift it up with pincers and carefully remove the membranes that are below it from each side. 
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	And if the artery is thin, turn it to the point of the hook, then cut from that part according to the quantity of the two ends.  
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not copied, it will not jump at all altogether.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And draw blood from the sixth rib to the third. 
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	And if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a strong doubled silk thread, so that decay does not come before the wound heals, and blood flows. 
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	Then cut away the excess that is between the two ties at that same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with a cautery blade down to the bone so that the flesh is cut. 
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And this is the milder operation if the patient does not have a fever and is of hot complexion. 
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For cauteries help to finish off moisture:  
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	Therefore it is of greater help against moisture. 
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	When it is necessary to extract arteries, one should fill the area with old cotton and place well-made tents on top. 
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when they are loosened, let them be treated with dry medicines that promote flesh growth, and with bandages, until they are healed. 
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	and if without cutting the artery as much as you work, hurry to cauterize it or apply vitriol to the area and hold it with your hand until the blood is stopped. 
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	and if you don't have it available, put your thumb on the area until the blood freezes, and apply cold water to the area until the bleeding stops, and extract it as needed. 
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	and the best and easiest way to extract an artery is to cauterize the vein of this two-pronged cautery, but make sure the prongs are well spaced to hold their heat longer. 
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	There should be a space of one finger width between the two blades, and then when you have marked the two spots, place the hot iron on them until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places. 
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	And let them be spaced apart between the two heads for it is not soldered together at all. 
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And this is the form of the cautery: 
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the veins that are on top of the head of a feverish person, and no cure of medicine profits them at all, and you see the face of the patient reddening, and feel their forehead pulsating like a tremor;
