et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and if they are tense and moist so that the hairs of the papers fall out, and the papers are heated and scorched by the ardor of the tears, then this cure is necessary. 
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And they called it the ancient "bruised cure," and what you do is shave the hair from the back of the head of a patient with this illness, then make three incisions on the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead; 
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	And let one of the incisions be as it should all go down the forehead by swallowing until the nose, and the others you shall make with the ribs above the papers, and beware of incising the arteries that are on the sides above the papers.  
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	And remove your hand from the continuation of the two mandibles, and let each wound be the quantity of three fingers across the joints. 
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have ready a piece of sponge and much linen for wiping the blood, then put in the spatula sharp on two sides as follows is its shape. 
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision which is above the temple to the second incision.
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	And scrape out all the flesh which is between the two incisions until all the fat which is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then pull out this spatula.  
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you put the instrument called "cultellaire" into the first crack, it is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the sharp edge towards the flesh that is burned at the heart, and the blunt side towards the bone, and push until it comes to the middle fissure.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to these parts so that the incision is continuous until you reach those that open onto the heart, and then again make another incision in the middle fissure until the other side. 
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	And then extract the blood equally, and press the place for the blood taken. 
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	Then put in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and place on it cloths softened in wine and oil and alum, and guard that no boils come there. 
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And on the third day untie the bandage, and bring a large poultice of hot water, then the ointment cure with rose oil, and other cures for which we cure wounds, until it is healed. 
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When some acute catarrh comes along customarily, and you see these things small and weak, and dim the sight, and burn the papers. 
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hairs fall out, and his head is filled with sharp pain, and the patient sneezes; 
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then know by these signs that those humors and phlegm do not come from a single vein, and the remedy for it is this. 
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you must instruct the patient to lie on his back, then make a large incision between the forehead and a second one at the width of a finger's breadth.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin at the left temple and cut to the right temple, and let the incision be down to the bone; 
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and remove your hand from the nerves of the temples that move when chewing;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is uncovered, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, and then insert between the two edges of the incision cotton wool and linen bandages;  
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then bind soft cloths soaked in wine and oil over it, and be careful not to let an abscess form there.
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	When it is removed, you must rub the bone until it starts to produce flesh, and then treat it with drying agents which will promote the growth of flesh.  
En teil maniere:	In this manner: 
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster. 
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	And administer it to these wounds to draw out the flesh. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	Everything that falls in the ears is one of four things: 
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	Either grain, or beast, or a stone from a mine or similar things such as iron.
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	Or seed, such as acorns, beans, peas; 
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Or flowing things such as water and easily flowing things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or any other object lodges in the ear that does not fit into the ear and does not grow in it, then put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, then distill some oil of violets or sesame oil, and then administer an extraction. 
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	And make it sneeze vigorously, and stop its nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool. 
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and raise the ear above. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times strength comes by this treatment.  
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	And if strength does not come, administer extraction with subtle pincers, of which this is the form: 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it jumps with strength with the pincers, that is good. 
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	If not, administer extraction with a subtle awl of small diameter.  
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	And if it does not jump with that, make a cane of iron and push the head of the cane or the hole of the ear hard, and plug what is around the cane with soft wax so that the veins cannot enter with the cane. 
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	Then the treatment will come forth strong, for many times strength comes as we have said.
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	And if it does not come forth in any manner, take glue of which one takes birds, and put some instrument that is suitable for doing so in the middle, and put a piece of cotton around.
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the hot iron on the stone or whatever it may be, and draw hard. 
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not flow out from all the things we have said, then hasten to cut the ear as if it were an abscess with hot blood, and spasm. 
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	And the manner of incision is such that you first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein and draw out blood according to the measure of his strength. Then have the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, making a small incision at the root of the ear in the fat or wherever it depends; 
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	And let the incision be shaped like a crescent moon until you reach the bone, then press the stone according to your power and suck it quickly into your mouth. 
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And continue the treatment until it is healed. 
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction.  
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if he cannot urinate, give him a thin, delicate spatula according to this form: 
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think the grain is wet from moisture of the ear until you have made many pieces of it. 
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	Then extract it with delicate pincers and a sucker, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In acute pain then when a bone is in the ear it is necessary that the patient uses a sneeze first of all, and widely fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that same ear where the pain is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps far because of it, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If not, take many stones according to the length of your finger, light and slender, and heat them a little in the fire; 
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and place one or two of them on the patient's ear, and press upon it from their feet on the other side, and strike with another stone upon the stone which is in the ear; 
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not cease to do this stone on stone until the sharp pain is entirely gone, and thus it will all be gone. 
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see it, take the joint, and put one of its heads in the ear, and grasp the other head with fire until the softer joint is burned. 
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Then redo another part of other joints until the sharpness subsides entirely, as we have said regarding stones. 
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of a beast, if it is of small size, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; 
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is of large size that one can feel it, then administer extraction with pincers;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and this is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear. 
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms embedded in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and where we treated distillations, and the treatment does not profit at all, then it is necessary that you look at the ear in the sunlight: 
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If there are any worms, take them out with fine tweezers; and if there are none, take the cane whose shape is this: 
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	Insert the smallest end into the ear according to the amount of suffering of the patient, then suck up all the cane. 
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Do this often until all the worms come out.  
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey and come out, stuff cotton around the cane as I have said in the stone. 
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	And if they do not come out as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the killing of worms, and you will find them or treat distillations.  
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if you distil your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, of which this is the shape as you see. 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And whether of silver or iron, it is three below at the small holes, and above it covers to distil. 
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	And to press within the distillation is an instrument of iron well made for it, and if you see take the razor and wrap around the point with cotton. 
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	Then it drips your oil or juice, and whatever you see of your medicines in the tube, and the tube is in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	Then put within the razor all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or comes out of the ear. 
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	And let the patient smell it within, and whether the distillation is a little heated over the fire so it is distilled in the ear. 
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born who does not have some perforation in their ears; 
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	And the same thing happens to adults through a wound or a splinter lodged in the ear, and this damage sometimes comes perfectly inside the ear so that it cannot be seen; 
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	And sometimes the hole widens because of fire, and one sees it well. 
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which comes perfectly and cannot be seen is of a healing grievance in several ways, and in this case it behoves you to put the patient's ear in the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look inside: 
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	If you see an apparent obstruction, then the work has this whole form of which this is the shape: 
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	It should be sharp and cutting in front and behind entirely flat so that it does not wound the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	If the ingrown hair is from flesh near the ear or the cartilage of the ear, hold it with fine tweezers and gently pluck it until all the hair is removed. 
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operation is performed perfectly in the ear, then take a very subtle razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then apply it to the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the ingrown hair that the patient feels pain near the ear, pierce it gently, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear. 
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	Then place a tent in the ear according to the width of the piercing, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it with rose water and powdered vitriol. 
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And if you see the ear swollen, it is necessary that you draw out the tent and insert another tent moistened with cerate made from rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed. 
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, plunge a sponge and cloths into cold water, and place them on the ear, and use other remedies that stop bleeding, which are found in treatises on distillations.
de la char des papieres	from the flesh of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This is the tool that comes from papers of the eyes when they are moist and dry, so it is fitting that you extend them with pincers and forceps, and the cup of a spatula from its roots. 
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Then put on the place crushed vitriol. 
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if without it being cut off, then cauterize with a subtle lentil-shaped cautery, and cauterize after the incision is made. 
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	And many times they repair themselves, so that nothing remains of their roots.
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return at all. 
de la gresle	of gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times come in papers of the eyes some things that resemble hail in their form and hardness, and for this reason this illness is called "hail," and it is a gathering of thick moisture in the paper above and below. 
li ovraiges est telz:	The works are such: 
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	Take care if the hail moves from one side to another, and it is a light thing to know.
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Make the donkey's skin wide then lightly scrape each part, then take it with pincers and cut. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cut it without piercing a bit of paper, do not worry about the patient.
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	And if the fissure is large, sew it together with a stitch and treat it until it heals. 
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	And if it is small, do not apply any pressure, for ointments will soon restore it and generate flesh. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the hail descends into the ear towards the upper part, turn over the paper and hold the hail with pincers, cut it and press on one side and the other.
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is removed by incision, it does not matter. 
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the hailstone is removed, wash it with warm salt water and treat the place where it entered as long as the patient is healed.  
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a grease that accumulates on cloths and papers, and it happens more to children than to adults, and it grieves their eyes greatly, and they get catarrh in the mornings and cannot look at the sun because tears rush to their eyes. 
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	And for this reason they lie down on their faces and sleep on them, with their papers under their eyebrows, so wet that the swelling and appearance are covered by the exinach which appears in the eye. 
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the bone coming out.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the way to do the work is that the patient puts his head in a healthy place; 
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	And then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that it contains, exiting from each part, then put it on top. 
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	And press with both your hands on one side and the other so that the exiting matter is gathered within the circle. 
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	Then make in the middle of the moisture a sharp incision with a knife, a slit no wider than the wound that one makes when opening a vein.  
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	And cut through the skin completely until you reach the exiting matter. 
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And in several configurations, matter will exit the incision, according to the form of a white piece of fat.  
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Then extract it all at once with a piece of clean cloth between your hands, turning your hand to the right and left until it is spread out.  
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and guard that you do not insert into the fissure so that you reach all the way to the eye, lest you bruise it. 
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the pus does not appear at the beginning of the fissure, then widen the fissure slightly until it appears. 
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then extract it as we have said, then moisten cloths in water and vinegar, and place them on the area, and bind with bandages. 
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind flaxseed and put it on to corrupt that moisture which has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the site of a hot abscess, then apply soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When hairs grow from planted paper and are aged, they harm the eyes, and bring about manners of illnesses such as accustomed tears and softening of the eyelids, as long as it is the cause of the destruction of the eyes.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	And the treatment is according to four manners:  
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	either by fire cautery, or by sharp medicine according to what is before it or chapter of cautery, and it is done either by incision and suture or by canes, according to what I will say. 
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient on your knee, then turn the paper from the eye to your left hand. 
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If it is converted, it is good; 
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, if you insert a needle along its entire length. 
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let it be below the margin of the paper where the hair grows from those hairs, and draw the thread along the top of the entire paper, and turn it to the razor; 
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then make in the part below the paper, below the added hairs, along the entire spatula, from the large tear duct to the small one. 
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	Then extract the thread and place below the paper a small tent of cotton and linen; then draw upon the paper a shape like a myrtle leaf, and in all ways it is necessary that the shape be according to the quantity you see raising the paper which is divided into parts.  
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if there is need for someone to have a large quantity of paper according to how soft the paper is; 
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	Then make all along the two lines that you have marked, and begin from large tears to small; 
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	And let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the lancet into one of the two angles of the heart, then flay it all; 
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	Then bring together the two lips with a stitch from a needle with all fine woolen thread, and wipe away the blood, and let the excess of the threads dry on the two eyebrows without using any gluing substances if you see fit to do so;
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	And if not, do not worry about it, then leave the suture and threads until three or four days;  
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	Then heal the wound without stitching with drying and constricting things, for paper comes alive at the sewing of the wound and its assembly, but stitching is slow (as the ancients say), and this is work without fear. 
et si a une autre maniere:	And if there's another way: 
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And it is that you sign the paper in a shape like the leaf of myrtle as we have told, at 3 ounces dried according to the form which is here:  
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then let him who has little strength do it equally according to the form that is here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you cannot hold the pliers and the thing is not even, take a needle where it has one thread and put it in the shape. 
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	And put one other thread behind the large tear, and the second thread behind the small one, and assemble between your two hands the threads equally. 
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift your hand equally and lift all the skin on which you have signed, as we have told, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching and cure it until it is healed. 
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; 
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	And it sometimes happens that the hairs of the paper are converted: 
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	Then you must use what we have said about incision; 
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	But the suture in one and the other is more artificial. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The cure of boils is according to this form: 
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	And that you convert the paper and insert it within according to what I have said, and then make two boils by art, and two subtle ligatures as long as the paper and the width of a spatula is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	And cut as two ends where you hold the threads; 
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	Then assemble one and the other subtly upon that which rises from the paper of the oil, and strain the two boils from the two parts they form;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and leave it like that for several days, and the skin which will be stretched will die and harden and bear, as long as it wishes by itself. 
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it is delayed, if the head has some strength, then treat it until it is healed; 
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is closed and the paper is lifted, and the hairs no longer grow; 
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and this is the shape of the two canes that you will make according to this figure and according to this quantity of length and width: 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the works are such that you take a fine needle, and put a thin silk thread through it; 
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then join the heads and tie them subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long;  
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then arrange in the chase another thin silk thread quickly, and tie the heads of the threads; 
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then put the patient's head on your lap; 
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and let it be in the sun so that the work is illuminated, for this is a subtle and delicate work, then insert the needle at full speed into the root of the hair closest to the joint, and make it pierce quickly through the skin following the natural direction of the hair. 
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then pull out the hair up to the joint and insert it into the joint if there are one or two or three or more hairs. 
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Then withdraw your hand so that all the hairs come out of the joint along with the skin following the natural direction of the hair. 
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the joint is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you will pull the joint downwards along the thread that you have ordered, until the joint comes out through the hole above and you see it with your eyes. 
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then you should treat the flesh and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows up over it; 
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from a horse's tail with it, and let it grow together with the one you are leaving it with until it is elongated and then remove it. 
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the rotting of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this illness which is called "aleacratio" or rot comes to the eye, there are two ways: 
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and the other unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs through a wound incision, or by cutting with a cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the way to treat it is that you cut the suture, and separate the lips of it, and put flax tents in it, and bind it until it heals. 
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And it is not fitting that you use things in its treatment that dry and constrict.  
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, the illness will return worse than the first. 
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	But work with softening things, such as fenugreek; 
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And rose of aquilegia or allspice and flaxseed are cooked, and ointments of diachylon melted in any of the oils, and it wraps a tent, and cures it from this. 
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasures of your cure are that you take care that it does not fuse according to the form it was before; 
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And this work that we have said is nothing more than the direction of this disease, so that it does not return according to the form it was before. 
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This sickness which is below, which is truly called "axacrati," and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	Accidents come from wounds and fissures and cauteries and similar things; 
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	And the way of working it is that you take a needle with a double thread and stick it into the flesh and make it pierce from the left tear duct to the right so that the threads come out on both sides of the flesh.
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then the flesh is cut above all the needle, and the cup at the spatula wide. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is necessary, it is good;  
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If not, take the razor and put it in the slit, and turn the paper, and make two slits or cuts on either side within the paper; 
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and let the heads of the two slits be at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make one angle so that when they are joined together, the shape is like the shape of a Greek letter “Y”; 
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	Then remove that flesh, according to the amount its sides are affected below, so as not to tear the paper, then rejoin the two separated parts and sew them with a thread of wool;  
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply the care that we have mentioned of softening medicines and bandages, until it is healed. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the ailment comes from a fissure or suture or cautery, it is fitting that you make a full incision below the hairs of the skin, and according to what has been said before. 
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	Then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said.  
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	And one must do the work according to the form of the ailment, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare all sorts of tools so that they can make the shape return to its natural form. 
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And the patients themselves, according to what is fitting for work and instruments are in several positions. 
dou soudement de la papiere	of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this suture occurs in the hands of men in such a way that the skin above is stuck with the white of an egg and cannot move or perform its natural works, then you must put the point of a razor under the skin and lift it up.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and hold them like pincers, as long as you grasp that which is airy with a subtle spatula, which is neither too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient can only suffer from the spatula being too sharp and not bleed. 
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	And let your incision, by which you scrape off the assembled skin, be slightly made so that the paper revives according to its natural form. 
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	And heal all that is assembled, and do it sometimes in the sharp saline eye, and raise it with sweet water, and with broth. 
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	Then place a tent of linen between the paper and the eye, and put woolen cloth soaked in abundance of egg on top of the eye.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	And after the third day, use warm broth and similar things until it is healed. 
de l’ungle de l’oil	from the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the nail is according to two manners: 
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	It is nervous and appears like hard fat, and another which is not nervous but appears like white frozen moisture, that when you touch it with iron and think to pinch it, you cannot. 
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	And both kinds begin toward the great tear duct and grow bit by bit until they cover the whole eye and all the light and the movement of the eye. 
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his head on a sound pillow, then he opens his eyes;  
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lift the paper to your hand, then hold the needle with small forceps and extend it above; 
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle and put a hair of horse, or cow, or ox, with strong thread;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a bit and stick it in the needle, and pierce it through with the whole needle, and tie the needle with thread and extend it above, and flay all the hair on the side of the needle that touches the caruncle and silk to the hair up to the head, then cut the rest at the root of the tear duct with a very fine spatula and small forces, and leave the flesh natural or tear duct, so that through the incision does not come the accustomed body fluids;  
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	And sometimes they have fastened the nail to the awl alone, as we said. 
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	Then, having skinned it, one takes all the spatula smooth of which this is the form: 
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and tear it, and that the kernel is not pierced. 
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	And after the incision, put a piece of silk thread into the eye, and make a collar out of silver, and leave it until the next day. 
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal what is necessary so that it may be healed.  
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot put in the needle, and the awl cannot enter, many times this kind of nail is cured by medicine. 
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And they grow as I have said in the division, and if you see it covered, work on the eye of the patient, and take a light sharp piece according to this form.  
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And lift the bone subtly, and if you see that it decreases not and the reason hastens it, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of litharge and red lead, finely ground, and keep the eye until the next day. 
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is all removed.  
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the eye, such as an abscess, then milk it, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear harms the eye greatly, suspend it at the corner, and cover part of it and not all, so that fluid does not enter. 
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill into the eye red collyrium which is made of litharge.  
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows upon the iris
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	In some men a red flesh never is born, and cover the prunes and restrain them on papers and turn them in the fire, and they resemble a rose of baluster. 
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the works are such that the patient puts his head in good health, then he works the eyes, and all the flesh with suitable needles for this, and supports it with strength; 
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then cut the first flesh, and go cutting all the way with the razor to the end, and be careful that you do not bruise the eye during the work; 
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and let the incision be along the spatula that we have said in the incision of the nail and with small force by which one removes the splinter, as the shape after this chapter demonstrates; 
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, apply oil of cypress or you distill red cochineal and similar corrosive medicines, and put hot cotton oil with a little egg white on top so that it is well assured against a hot abscess;
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if it remains there and the sock covers it, and you doubt a hot abscess, leave the eye and treat the abscess with soothing things for a hot abscess. 
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Then return to your work until it is healed, and do the same when a splinter is lodged in the eye. 
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But nevertheless, it is necessary that you relieve the treatment of each weak eye by its natural path; 
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and from accidental paths in ironwork.
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	And do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this limb is suffering from this work. 
des voines des eulz	of veins of eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Blood vessels are red veins that are covered on the eye, and tolerate their work to sight and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is therefore necessary in the first place that you look to see if the eye is weak or strong, and there is no other illness except pain. 
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	Then proceed in this manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Command the patient to put his head in a healthy position, then suspend those veins at every inch according to his wisdom, and let the inches be subtle double according to this form. 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be applied in degrees throughout the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	Then one coils those veins subtly, and wipes the blood hour after another, until you see those veins move away from the eye; 
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	And be careful that you do not prick the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you only sever those veins; 
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	And when you have done this, if you distill green and red collyrium into the eye to corrupt what remains of the humor. 
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you cannot collect all of this in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye of soothing things to ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and you are sure of a hot abscess, then start again according to this manner which is before until he is healed;
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the form of forces: 
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The one called "arissati" makes a fistula: 
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you treat it by cautery and by burning medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then cut into the abscess, where it should dwell, and draw out all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed. 
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the decay and blackness, then take all the instruments with which it is made. 
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "sharp point," and is made of iron at the front end, and is pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that this corruption is removed. 
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicines. 
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the wound is sealed, and flesh grows, and the body of the gut is sealed, and remains thus for 40 days, and it does not reopen and is not abscessed, and no bad accidents occur, know that it is healed; 
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If this is not the case, if there is no other remedy than to return the fistula to the anus opening according to this form:  
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with an iron instrument, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, take a drill according to this form, and let the head of the drill have three angles, and let the shaft be tapered down to a point as you see here: 
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and remove your hand from the oil one finger's breadth away, then turn the drill completely until it pierces the bone, and let the patient feel this by the vein that flows out if they hold their hand on their thigh; 
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the place, the matter goes to naught. 
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	This is an easier thing for the patient.  
de l’issue de l’oil	from the outflow of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eye opens entirely and there is no hindrance in the nose or decrease, then it is fitting that you bind the patient. 
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	Then the healthy one, then put on leeches or a cupping glass without iron to suck, then put on the eye a bandage made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocol, and then strain the eye, and plaster with bandages and cloths.
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	And the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough and fold each one into four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity the eye needs.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	Then strain it with a hard bandage, and start again the cupping to suck without hurting. 
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	Then remove the cupping glasses and leave the oil strained day and night, and if the ligaments soften, then you must strain it a lot. 
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then remove the ligament after a day and night, and if you see the oil recover, it is good.  
se ce non;	If not; 
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	start again the plaster and cloths and the ligament and cupping glasses until it is healed. 
dou derrompement de toile uvee	when rupture of cloth with
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When a disruption comes in the woven fabric, then open it up, and remove strips of paper as fine as grains of resin, and it is astonishing to see.
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	Then if you see it covered, the work is such that you thrust a needle into the root of the lower part up to the upper part, then thrust another needle where there is a doubled thread from the tear duct.  
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and let it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its position; 
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then take the place of the doubled thread and tie one part of the eye around it, and pull it tight, then remove the needle and put a softened linen cloth soaked in plenty of egg white on top; 
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it until the thread loosens with the eye, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; 
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and once the wound is restricted by the eye on each side with a circle of cloth, until it is healed. 
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eye has a large appearance, pierce it with a fine spatula that comes perfectly from the eye, and correct the whitish moisture and remove the eye, and it will heal quickly;  
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then remove it until it is healed. 
de la bowe de l’oil	from the hollow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease which is called “alcunnati” is nothing but a bowel assembled in the eye, resembling descending fire, and it is not fire; 
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	And the manner of performing the operation is such that you make the patient sit upright on a suitable seat, then take the head between your hands in two parts, and move it so that you see the bowel come up above your eyes; 
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then let it be fixed, and not descend, and relieve the light, and let the patient see things as he used to; 
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend below, know that it is fire, and if the descending of the bowel is not as we have said. 
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take a subtle spatula and cut on the horny membrane one spot along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the horny membrane and the cornea, as long as the bowel rises; 
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when it is drawn out, distill into the sharp hot oil mixed with honey, or hot water or fenugreek boiled and honey, then let it be cured by another cure until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	of sharp points of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have seen the resemblances of needles in the division, and what it is fitting to pierce.  
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	If in work according to health. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is fitting that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and bind his good eye tightly. 
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	Then place the paper from the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right. 
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	Then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called “almagda,” or in your left hand if the eye is right. 
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the point of the instrument near the crown through the thickness of a reed at that part of the eye where there is least tear gland. Then push the instrument which is called "almagda" skillfully, and turn your hand until it pierces through the part of the eye, and feel that the almagda enters into the empty space. 
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	And it is necessary that the measure of the almagda passage be exactly equal to the space from the pupil to the end of the black part. 
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and this is the crown of the eye;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	If you see the bone in this paper due to the clarity of the corneal veil, then put the instrument as far as where the point is, and then press it out below, one way after another. 
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If it is sharp now, the patient sees it in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	Afterwards rest a little, and if the point goes back up the second time, put force on it with the instrument, and when it is firmly fixed and does not rise, gently withdraw the almagda by turning your hand bit by bit. 
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	And then put back into it a drop of gemstone juice, and lift from it the eye within. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put a cloth or linen moistened in rose oil and plenty of egg yolk on it, and tie it with healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on a common poultice with plenty of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have their eyes too hard, then it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called “alberit”, of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And so pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not go too deep, but make the place subtle, then put in almond, as we have said; 
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	And for the completion of the work, prepare the patient a sleeping doctor approaching, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; 
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	And let it be devoid of all movements, and take light meats, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and let it be bound according to its position until the third day; 
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	Then untie it in the same dark house, and test its sight, and make it see some things, and then tie it back until the seventh day; 
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And it is not fitting that you do this in the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is fitting that you delay this, because the humor rises quickly. 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	When an abscess comes, loosen the bandage before the seventh day, and apply what dries up the abscess.  
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	And when it is appeased, loosen the bandage and put a linen cloth over it to cover for several days, and keep it in a darkened room. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	Then gradually go outside little by little, and return to your normal activities.  
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And know that no disciple should interfere in this case. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	A man from Yrach came to us who told us that in his homeland they made an almond cake which causes a sharp pain, but for all that I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients. 
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the appearances of almond shapes so that those who do not know them may recognize them. 
et soient d’arain proprement:	and let them be of good iron 
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the heads of these be of the same subtlety, and the last one in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	From the flesh comes the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Sometimes there are born or found diverse joined chariots, from which some appear like scorpions with many feet; 
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there are such that have a chariot enchanted of fox color, and if a chariot seems of good color. 
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that then of these chariots which is of good color and not enchanted, it is fitting that you make the sick person sit between your hands against the sun; 
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and open their nostrils, and put the ointment on those chariots, and draw them forth;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	for as much as you can sustain it at a subtle sharp spatula on one side, until you know that chariot is all taken out. 
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there remains any thing which one cannot take out, then work with all the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains;
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if without overcoming it, or an abscess arises, so cut it as it is necessary; 
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if they are malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize them so that the pus is dried up and all the humors are removed, then apply fresh wine vinegar. 
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If it works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy. 
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	And if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is a humor in the bone above, to which the instruments do not come to cut. 
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	Then it is necessary that you put a linen thread a little thick, and knotted with our hands, and have between each knot a space of one inch or less. 
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	And put the patient's shoulder on the thread in his nose at its bottom, and draw it while smelling as much as it comes through the nose into the mouth. 
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	And many times they do so to children at schools, and it is a light thing for whoever wants to do it. 
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	Then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and draw them out one after the other as we are who are skilled at it. 
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you know that the worms have corrupted the flesh, then draw out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before. 
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode everything that remains of the flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then insert into the nose a cane of lead for several days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, into which one distills the oils and medicines or other things 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it is made of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and conducts it as well; 
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you wish, make a closed cane, and the instrument is full to purge the head;  
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and it has a handle at the head to hold it when one heats the oil or any liquid. 
de la char sor le neis	From the flesh comes the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times there arises in the head a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large over time, so much so that it is a fearful thing to behold; 
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and for this reason, you must cut it at the beginning and remove all of it, then apply the cautery or burning medicine to the spot. 
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if one delays covering it until it is large, take care if it is hard, of dark color, with poor sensation:
