si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	Do not touch it with iron because it is a festering abscess, for when one covers it even once, great harm comes to the patient; 
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	And if the abscess is soft to the touch, not dark in color, and you see that it can be completely covered, empty the patient and cover it without fear, treating the area with drying and binding agents.  
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	Therefore, when this happens to anyone, see if the wound is fresh and full of blood; 
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bring the two edges together with stitches, and treat it until it heals. 
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	And if the edges are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of their core until they bleed, then bring the two edges together with stitches, and remove them, and sprinkle with powder of dragon's blood and ground incense. 
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put on the powders a piece of strong plaster or another soldering plaster, and leave it until it discharges by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The way to suture is that you bring the edges together: 
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	either with needles, as we have said in suturing the abdomen;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have shown you. 
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	Within the lips there often appear hard abscesses, resembling grains of millet, some smaller and some larger; 
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then you must turn back the lips and cut open each pustule, take them with pincers and remove them in each part.
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	Then apply the area after the incision with powdered vitriol, until the blood is stemmed. 
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then cover it with linen and treat the area with dry things until it is healed.  
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times there arises on the gums swollen flesh which the ancients called "albulus" 
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	it is necessary that you hold it with forceps and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood run. 
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	Then put ground vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders on the spot;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if that flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, then cut it a second time and cauterize it. 
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after the cautery,
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the shapes of the instruments for cutting. 
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes there are assembled at the head of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, crusts that are ugly and rough.
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	And sometimes the teeth are black and citron-colored and wormy, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are foul-smelling.
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his shoulders are in your lap, and hold the bones or the splinters visible, until there remains nothing; 
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and then make the blackness and the greenness, and the yellowness and the other stains, until they are cleaned; 
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes that which is at the first reason, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, one begins again on the second day and the third, until you have raised everything; 
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that teeth need various shapes of instruments for raising, according to what the work shows, for which the rasp with which one raises front teeth has other shapes than those with which one raises between teeth; 
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these shapes and others should be prepared with you. 
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you treat a tooth for its pain that you delay drawing it out as much as you can, for this ought not to be done. 
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	For it is a very noble substance so that one has no excuse for drawing it out.  
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to be treated, it is necessary that you are certain of the tooth that is painful.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Often the pain deceives the patient, and they think that it is a holy tooth, and have a good tooth drawn. 
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	And nevertheless the pain does not depart because of this, as long as the bad tooth remains, for we have often wanted to do this to these saints. 
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	And when you are well certain of the aching tooth, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth at all points, and spit forcefully to keep the gums from all sides. 
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	Then move it with your two hands or use subtle forceps at the first prick and prick, so that it is well loosened, then firmly grasp the forceps. 
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the head of the patient rest upon your thigh between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and insert it into each side gently, and move it as you did at first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the bone is pierced and gnawed, it is fitting that you fill it with cloths where the holes are; 
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you extract it subtly with tweezers so that it does not break when extracting it;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is very wise to work around the gum to loosen the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take good care that you do not break it, and a part remains, and returns to the patient by the ill will of the root greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not act like ignorant barbers who by their haste and boldness often break the carriage and do not accomplish what we have recounted; 
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but often bring great illness by the extraction of these roots that remain, or by the carriage they break, as we have often seen; 
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is drawn, wash the wound with wine or vinegar and salt;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if blood flows from it, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol to the place. 
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that doesn't work, cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the instruments with which one pulls teeth should have long points and thick handles so they do not bend when you pull the tooth. 
et ce sont les formes:	And these are the shapes:  
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be large limbs so that they do not bend in the opposite direction, and they should be made of good iron, and they should have teeth to hold the pieces.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains after pulling, you must put moistened cotton with butter on the place for one or two days until the gums are softened, then insert the tongs called "algefri," whose head resembles a bird's beak.  
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	And their inside should be made like a file and this is its shape: 
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, then you must expose the flesh around the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali," that is to say, a small plane, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	It must be strong and thick so it does not break, and if the root comes out with these, that is good. 
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If not, then help yourself with all the instruments, from which the forms come hereafter: 
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument which has two handles, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments which are in front in the manner of teeth, and of this instrument which appears like large tongs, of which here is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let these instruments be such that they cannot break, and know that many instruments are made of dense material; 
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not so sharp; 
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wisest master craftsmen discover their own instruments according to what their work and the illness show them, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to the diversity of others, so that they do not break either the chariot or the other bones, or it rots, if he seeks the instruments that suit him, as I told you, and help yourself with gestures, of which this is the form: 
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be large and well-gripping to hold the bone so that it does not escape, but can hold and remove it; 
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, so he has all these instruments: 
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth appears not according to nature, and its form is ugly, even in young women, it is necessary that you know if the density came after the tooth, and is not in its proper place, and cannot be filed or smoothed. 
adonques lou raie;	then the rasp. 
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	And if it is joined with the tooth, take this instrument whose shape is like a small beak, and is made of sharp steel. 
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the tooth must be filed little by little every day for its hardness, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file it with a part of a lime like this is the shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	And it is also like the file with which one makes needles
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	And file the tooth little by little in the hand lightly, so that it does not move until it comes out. 
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	Then the blade in the end should have no scraper, and if the steel is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, then file the sharpness until it is smooth so that it does not cut the tongue nor corrupt speech. 
quant li dent lochent	When a tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front tooth loosens, either by impact or by falling out, and the patient cannot press on what they are eating without it hurting, and you have treated them with astringent medications, and that does not work; 
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	then it is necessary to restrain it with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes. 
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	And let the wire be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	And if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the wire and bend it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the ends between the crooked teeth, if there is one or more, until you reach the sound tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	Then begin again the covering until the part where you started, and strain your hand subtly and wisely, so that it does not move. 
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	And let your bandage be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. 
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then grasp the head with a file in tongs, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy tooth, and fix it so that it does not bite the tongue; 
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	And then leave it tight as long as it can remain, and if it loosens, or the threads break, remove it with another thread;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it remains and serves thus for its entire time, this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two missing ones, as you see: 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when a tooth falls out, if it is put back in its place again and again, as we have said.
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and let no one interfere who is not wise and experienced, and at no time make the shape of a cow's bone tooth, and put it in the place where the defect is, and extract it as we have said, and let it remain and serve for a long time. 
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the band of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Never is this ligament which comes below the tongue or natural, that one is born thus; 
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by an accident of a stitched wound; 
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the works are such that you open the mouth of the patient and hold his head in your lap, and lift the tongue; 
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then grasp the nervous ligament widely, as long as the tongue is dislodged from its tenement, and if there is hardness or knot, and it is due to stitching of a wound, then he puts in the hook and grasps widely that ligament; 
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and guard that the incision not be too deep, for the artery which is beneath; 
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done so, lift the place with a sharp rose and ice, or with a sharp cold, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; 
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and let the patient chew each night, so that the gums may not stick together.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if a flow of blood comes, put ground vitriol on the place; 
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the bleeding does not stop, cauterize it with a lentil-shaped cautery, which is good for this; 
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then cure it with another remedy until it is healed,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see a scar of black or hard color that the patient does not feel, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; 
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is declining toward the armpit, and there is moisture, then he cuts the sinew, and makes an incision with a subtle scalpel, and delivers it from one side and the other. 
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the blood does not come to your work, then put ground vitriol on it until it is quenched, then return to your work until you draw out all the pus; 
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift the wound from its place and cleanse it with other remedies until it is healed.  
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes there come into the throat boils that are called "godaths," and we properly call them the two almonds, and when you cure them as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take heed: 
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if it is a hard abscess of small size and dark color, do not touch it with iron at all.  
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it at all with iron, also for the draining of blood. 
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	But leave it alone until it is dead, and then you will cut it away, where it would break on its own.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is of a white color and the root is slender, prepare the instrument to cut, but first look to see if the abscess is quiet and calm. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit facing the sun and let their chest be bare, and open the mouth and take the scalpel between your hands, and press the tongue down below with the instrument. 
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	And it should be of silver or fine steel as a knife is:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	While you press the tongue down with this instrument, and see the abscess, take the lancet and insert it into the almond, and draw it forcefully upward as much as you can.  
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and do not touch anything of the cloths with it, then put the cup on the instrument, which is its form, as it seems to have some force; 
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and both the heads are curved and one towards the other, and are very sharp, and are made of tempered iron or steel: 
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, take pliers as they are shaped like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And it is sharpened on one side, and not on the other.  
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have applied one of the almonds, apply the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, clear and easy, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with warm water, or decoctions of cooked pomegranate seeds, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; 
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then let it heal until it is healthy. 
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And if other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two almonds, apply them similarly as the two almonds were applied. 
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born inside her throat, to be exact an abscess of small size; 
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And it had almost completely closed off her entire throat, so that the woman could not exhale through the passage that was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and she would have died if she had remained like that for one or two days. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high up that it had to be pierced twice through the two nostrils of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I therefore hastened immediately and put in a small incision, then I let the pus out freely, and extracted a large amount of bowel; 
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I made another incision in the other opening of the birth, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; 
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	afterwards I put the incision into these abscesses, and cut out a part, and there only came out a small amount of blood; 
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the passage of her throat was opened up for the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and I did not stop cutting from that abscess for a long time; 
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscess would grow again, and fill the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; 
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I lanced it and cauterized it inside the throat: 
ensi demora sens croistre;	afterwards it ceased to grow; 
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I departed from those parts, and only God knows what happened after me. 
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the membrane covering the eye descends to the eye and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; 
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is below large and round, it is called "uve". 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the inflamed abscess is soothed and subtle, then you must cut it; 
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and the one which is round and assembled and not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is of a bloody or yellowish or black color, so you must avoid cutting into it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner I have described, by its color and length, you should make the patient sit facing the sun, and press their tongue against the instrument which we mentioned before. 
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then insert the cautery into the eye, and draw it underneath, and hold it with one of the two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.  
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And you should not grasp it too forcefully, only the excess that is beyond the natural limit. 
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	For if you grasp more, it will greatly harm the voice and speech. 
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of being cut, it is necessary that you use a remedy to quell their fear during cauterization.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery if it is sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And let the patient put his head in healthy ground, and then press his tongue to the instrument that we have mentioned or the chapter of cauterization, and bind it with sharp, lively thread, so that it is not too thick nor too thin. 
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And in employing the wrapping of this instrument, of which this is the form: 
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And let it have on its head a covering where one puts the medicine, as the coverings of a spoon, and put the instrument over all the medicine on the eye.  
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	And let the patient lie on his side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from his mouth into the medicine within, so that it does not descend to the throat, and make him choke. 
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye for the quantity of half an hour, until you see it soften and the bites of the medicine are calmed. 
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	And if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton with the medicine, and push the instrument all the way into the cotton in the cane above it, until the cotton catches fire on top. 
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	And do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it to dry, and bind it afterward for four or five days. 
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to moisten the cautery with the medicine again, do so, and after the cautery wipe it around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and cleanse what is around it from the medicine. 
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be washed with cold water, and let it be treated with gargles until it is healed.  
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision or cautery; 
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and lavender and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in a pot, and put water in it, and boil it; 
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot let there be an instrument placed according to this manner: 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it should be made of silver or iron, and let one of its ends be inserted into the patient's eye socket as far as the vapor rises to the eyeball through the tube, until the eyeball is mortified;  
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	then repeat often until the eyeball dries, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the arrival of a hot abscess, for many things can happen; 
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not do this except at the decline of a hot abscess.  
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, then take a cane and put an egg white inside the head, so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; 
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	For the egg white does not allow the steam to burden the mouth, and it is a good cure together with health.  
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Often a bone or fishbone, or something else, gets stuck in the throat; 
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	So it is necessary that you pull out what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing move;
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	And what you do not see and is lodged in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach; 
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	perhaps if it is extracted by vomiting; 
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of stale bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	And tie it to the sponge with thread, then transfer it. 
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	And when it arrives at the place, if it swells, then draw hard.  
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	And if it does not come easily as we have said, then take the plunging instrument according to this form: 
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily, and have the head raised upwards. 
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	And be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest it should make you unwell, nor push any bone inside. 
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	And it is better that the patient inserts the instrument, so that they know where the thing is swollen.
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If he pushes it down, then draw hard on the whole instrument equally, until it comes loose.  
de la sansue de la gorge	of the bloodletting of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Sometimes medicine is without effect, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines. 
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	And when this does not profit, then look in the throat of the sick person to the sun, after which you press their tongue with the instrument that I have told you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sinus, if it has all little hooks, or use fine tweezers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a pointed cane, and put it into the patient's throat, then push or drive the end of the cane with a hot iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And let the patient hold sharp water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	Then take a full draught of sharp cold water, and work the mouth open, and have it swallowed down, and move it in their hand often. 
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And as soon as the sickness feels the sharpness, it will cease. 
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not cease as we have said, then fumigate the sick person with asafetida, at the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the grape.  
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	Do this many times, for it will fall away without delay. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are hot coals, and it be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and in that hole be placed the head of the instrument. 
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then he inhales the fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but comes to the sinuses; 
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	And the sinuses will now fall, and if they do not fall, you begin the fumigation many times; 
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient suffers thirst, and eats salty things and such, and does not drink water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it is necessary that they go out by this treatment.  
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the sinuses, is, when one can see it, like tongs bent to enter the throat; 
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and has the appearance of a bird's beak, and it has the roughness of a file, so that whatever it takes, it cannot let go;  
et vez ci la forme:	and see here the form: 
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what memory brings here after one and the other in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size; 
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two manners, one of which is in its appearance itself, and from the moisture it holds.  
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the ulcers when they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the buttocks, and abscesses in fleshy areas are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if abscesses one should not pierce, as long as the belly is healed according to its fulfillment; 
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their fulfillment, as abscesses which are near joints. 
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints and it is left until it is ripe around, by chance they may corrupt the ligament and nerve of the joint, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Where the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal limb; 
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or where it is near the fundament, if one pierces it even when it is ripe;  
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	And it is not right that you pierce an abscess which is hard without complete digestion, except for the one which is near the fundament, lest it rot thoroughly, and be drawn out inside, and a fistula form; 
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and it may not heal in a long time. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And you must know the hour of the perforation of the abscess which is dead according to its ripening, and it is when the pain is eased, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the softening and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; 
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and you must make the perforation sit where there is the most dependent part of the abscess, and where it appears to be moving; 
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and let the perforation be along the length of the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and near nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no weeping. 
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In cases where they bend, according to the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in fleshy place, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed to be digested completely, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before this, its body will be lengthened by the venom within it, and it is full of much filth. 
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	And perchance the lips harden and the depth of it. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess which is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you administer small abscesses, small perforations; 
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many fissures according to the appearance of the size of the abscess;  
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to sever the core, and cover; 
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	When it has become as yellow as drapery, and is dead, then it is necessary to do as one does with boils:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if there are such that are split into three angles, and if there are such that one cuts as the leaf of myrtle, as abscesses of anger; 
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if it has such things where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuts. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who do not have a head, such as a superficial abscess, it is fitting that you pierce them completely;  
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is fitting when the abscess is large and has collected a great deal of pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour but draw out a portion; 
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then open the abscess until the next day, then draw nothing further.  
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this many times in succession, until all the pus drains out. 
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	In the same way if the patient is of weak constitution, or a woman carrying [a child], or small children, or old men debilitated. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes leaps with the exit of the bowels, which by chance kills the patient, and you do not notice it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound clean, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a clean wound, apply bandages of linen or fine cotton. 
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess and there are many openings, you must put a bandage in each one so that they come together. 
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have covered a part of the skin in the abscess and have sewn it around, you must fill it with old cotton or linen tow without moisture and bind it until the third day. 
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the bone will heal, and the ointment dressing will continue until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold and fresh water, moisten a cloth, and place it on the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the discharge of blood persists, apply dressings and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book to the area, and if it is a time of winter, and the wound or abscess is very sensitive, you must put on bandages and cloths soaked in warm wine and oil; 
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in summer, and the flesh is fleshy, it behoves that you put wet cloths on it with vinegar and oil, or with wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said; 
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then untie the abscess and wipe it and heal it, as is fitting, until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And this is universally known in the treatment of abscesses: 
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see this chapter.  
des soros	of the shoulders
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the head of the shoulder comes small abscesses, and are manners of us that are in webs, just as the jeweler's file of a ring, and many are like it.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fatty and others that have moisture as well as pus; 
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if there are such that are hard and stony at the waist, and there is no doubt that the artery does not oppose it. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the hip are such that you should try all instruments called "dilator," of which the form comes after this, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, so let it pass over for a long time.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is drained, if you scald without leaving the skin that contains it, because it returns immediately when you leave nothing; 
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; 
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; 
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and do what remains of the night.  
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then begin again with cotton as before on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain for a night; 
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if an abscess is full of thick pus, treat it according to this form for a long time;  
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and apply your ointments and scrape it from all sides, and put all your treatment of milk where it lies; 
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery opposes you, do as I told you afterward. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do for an abscess if it is pierced, and of the waist and of the cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the abscess softens and the moisture, it is lighter for they are drops of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if some of these abscesses or head where there is no moisture, and of these were I abscesses that I copied or the head of an old woman; 
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	And I found the abscess just like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break it; 
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if one had done so, they would have done just as well to make a wound from a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming on the head, those which come on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be in the lowest part, so that the pus can flow out; 
et les cure si com il covient.	and the cure should be done as is appropriate. 
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess occurs at the neck and below the armpits, and in the angles, and sometimes it comes to other parts of the body, and they are very painful and intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly within its rib, just like the nodule and the abscess on the head, as we have said; 
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And the appearances of these scrofula are many. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are such things that contain moisture, and some that are so bad they will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	In the one then that you see of good disposition to touch, and it seems like the color of the body, and moves from each part and is not near the nerves of the neck nor at the artery nor at the duct, and is not deep; 
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	it is fitting that you cut it above, and scrape it from each part, and extend the two edges of the heart to ointments, if you need them, as we have said in abscesses of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and treat it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, and let the scalpel not be too sharp nor cutting, so the hand does not slip, and do not go too far ahead lest you cut what you should not.  
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut a vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put into the wound powdered vitriol, or some powders that staunch blood, and draw out the wound; 
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And let it remain until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to fester. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood has been drawn off, you may return to your work until you have completed it; 
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Then you must be sure with your index finger whether there remain any small scrofulous ulcers, and if so, clean them. 
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if it has in the root of the scrofulous ulcer a large vein, you must not cut that scrofulous ulcer at its root, but tie it with a strong doubled thread and let it fall off by itself without harm. 
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then dress the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then bandage it. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you scrape away the whole scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them now, since there is no longer any excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary that you know how to cut the root of it, and draw firmly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofulous ulcers which retain superfluity, pierce them where it appears dead;  
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce them as the one previously mentioned, hanging down, then apply tents with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleansed, apply an ointment promoting healing flesh until it is healed. 
de squinance	Of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; 
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their words. 
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have strabismus, it is necessary that the cleft of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be cut out; 
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and one should not help him by this means, for all the veins and the throat of the sick person are affected in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the throat, it is fitting to lift the epiglottis to avoid the peril that comes from choking.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below III or IV circles a small incision across, between the II circles or according to the quantity of the incision of the pharynx, not in the cartilage; 
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And those are suitable for cutting the epiglottis because there is no cartilage and the vessels are long. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to all the edges, then splits the heart until it reaches the sternum. 
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the symphysis, as we have said; 
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm from the sternum which flows out through the place that is broken, and by the loss of voice. 
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open a while. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed in which we doubt strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the heart, and sew it all alone without the cartilage. 
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then administer medicines that produce flesh, until it is healed. 
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	 Albucasim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely torn open and the patient is judged to be dead, and the defect is apparent.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient can breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; 
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And because the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and clean it, until it was cleansed; 
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I have seen. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young woman took a knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe; 
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and I found her as dead as can be. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found the blood which had flowed out of it, and although it had not opened a vein nor run any further than the throat, the veins were ruptured by the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and cleansed it until it was healed;  
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it did not happen to the damsel that she was red of voice, and she returned afterward to her disposition; 
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for this reason I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there should be no fear. 
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large abscess in the color of a yellow hue, and it is very common in women; 
et est selonc II manieres:	and it occurs in two ways: 
naturez, et accidens;	by nature, and by accident;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	where the natural one has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental one occurs in two ways, of which one is similar to thick phlegm, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from our arteries; 
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there should be fear, and it is not fitting to work with fire except in those that are small, and prove and search all the way through: 
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it as we found ours, and it cannot be opened to any vein, then cut it, just as one cuts the nails, and treat the hair with all its down, if there is any. 
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And enclose it well from the beginning, and care for it as is fitting until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of warts
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways known to us, of which I will speak of all the resemblances; 
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is fitting that I say all the difference that is between nail and issue.  
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that an issue is hot and feverish, as long as the boiling is not passed, and the corruption is completed. 
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Then the fever and heat subside. 
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With a nail there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains the pus, which is its own bag and is according to the color of the body, and it begins just as a pimple, and grows large. 
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to two appearances, either greasy or moist, and their color is as I have said in the division. 
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of a new wound, that you examine and inquire first with all the instrument which is called "introductory" according to what its form will be or the chapter which is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses of us is that you take the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the center, then according to the size of the abscess.  
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then extract the intruder, and take care in case it springs out. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs, whatever color it may have, do as I have said for the other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the intruder no moisture comes, know that it is greasy, so do it then in a cross shape and take it with pincers, and lightly scratch it on each side and watch the coat where it lies so you draw it out cleanly with the new. 
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out whole, do so piece by piece so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, the pain will return many times. 
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if a small piece remains and does not bother him, apply the wound with some strong corrosive powders, cleanse the wound, and put soothing things on the hot abscess, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed. 
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the pain is great, sew the two edges of the wound together and treat it with what promotes flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	And if the pulsating vein is against you or something else hastens you, apply powdered vitriol to the place and leave it for two or three days until the wound rots, and relieves the boiling of blood. 
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	Then return to cauterize what remains in the pain.  
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of instruments for insertion, and they are of three kinds: 
grans et moien et petit;	large and medium and small; 
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three square ones which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and there are three kinds: 
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which one sews charms, and they are made of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and those which are yellow are worth more, and are better proven for black lead to encircle the curves of fistula; 
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings. 
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the lancets are very similar as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, medium, and small; 
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if it has two curves in three ways also; 
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if it has three curves, and are also of three ways;  
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if it has two curves, and those with one curve only, and are of three ways; 
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all this is necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these are what they do with sharpening, and some of those that cut only from one side are used for scraping, so that we don't cut the vein or nerve. 
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these instruments are the lancets set in handles, so that the patient doesn't feel it when opening abscesses. 
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three ways:  
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	Great, small, and medium, as you see; 
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And do not use any but in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and angles, and similar places; 
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And never make another instrument small, resembling the husks of walnuts, according to this form, with which one staunchs blood: 
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it back in place which heals by cutting veins and arteries
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes men's breasts swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much that they appear like women's breasts; 
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and those who wish to cure them, if it is necessary, should proceed according to this form from line .b. to line .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape off the fat and fill the wound with medicine mixed with charcoal, then bring together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; 
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if her breast hangs down, and is softened by its size as it often happens to women, then make two cuts on the breastbone, through two similar incisions. 
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is joined to the other at the end of one and the beginning of the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; 
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then flay the skin between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about suturing and powders, and what is necessary for healing, until it is healed; 
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made because the patient does not want to rest, or because of bleeding, then you should fill the wound with softened cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; 
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it until it softens the remainder and the fat, then heal it until it is healthy. 
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come below the armpits are hard kinds of scrofula where there are ribs and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore those containing moisture must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
