Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then apply the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day. Then remove all the cotton and treat it with an ointment suitable for this until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, then make it like we have said in making incisions for scrofula, and if the wound goes inward, apply a cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the breaking of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut and the skin above it is sewn, many times abscesses occur, and the same thing happens to the swollen vein and abscess. 
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if the one who knows cuts when it is for the artery, the abscesses are long and perfect. 
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it with your fingers, you sense the separation.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is for a vein, the bones are seen to be further apart. 
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cut this abscess, and especially when it is under the armpits and at the angles and neck and many other places, and it is very large.  
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to avoid the cure with iron, and he who is in charge must also avoid it, and on the one who has a swelling from an artery running under the skin for a long time. 
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then work the incision as directed with one-inch marks, and cleanly separate the artery from the surrounding tissues until it is exposed. 
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then insert a needle beneath it and pass it through to the other side, and extract the artery with a doubled thread in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples. 
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then cauterize the area between the two ligatures with an intro Mitter until all the blood has been released and the abscess is drained. 
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply a bandage that promotes healing, as long as the ligatures hold.  
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then dress this with an appropriate ointment until it is healed. 
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	And if the abscess is at the size of the vein, it is necessary that you hold onto what you can grasp from the abscess to all the surrounding skin, then insert a needle beneath the area that you are holding and pass it through, using a doubled thread so that you draw it out on the other side.  
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then tie the abscess, as I told you, with a thread from one of its two sides to the other.  
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	And if you doubt that the thread will come loose, put another needle through all of the thread under the whole abscess at the incision of the first needle, and pull out the threads in four parts. 
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut the excess of the heart and leave that which is tied. 
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put a cloth softened in wine and oil on top, then give him care of bandages and ointments until he is healed.  
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in arteries and veins, abscesses also come to nerves when they are overworked, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens most often in the shoulders and arms and in all their places where there are joints, and it is a grievous abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in several conditions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is removed formed, the patient feels pain, and it is not perfectly matched to the body, but below the heart. 
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	And it moves well in all directions and does not go forward nor backward, nor below nor above; and the one that is in the joints should not be covered by iron. 
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	For fear it might contract.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And if it is on the head or forehead, cut the skin with a scalpel.  
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscesses are small, take some tweezers and grasp them at their root. 
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, suspend it to the lancet and flay it, then the surgeon and bind the wound with stitches, and cure it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	of large bogeys hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Sometimes it happens in the bowels and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its appearance like mushrooms, and it has subtle roots, and thick heads. 
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	And there are small ones and very large ones. 
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw a man who had two in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and they had small roots, and they were easily cut, and moisture continually flowed from them. 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I weighed them and found that one weighed eighteen ounces, and the other six.  And when performing surgery, if you see that the patient is moist, and the color of the joint is white and moist and has fine roots; 
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if the incision is made wide, and there are fire cauteries present.  
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For at the hip there often comes excessive bleeding, and if the blood goes too fast, then hurry and cauterize it. 
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	And if you see the patient fainting and fearful of the incision with iron, then take a well-made linen thread, and bind the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then restrain it, and do not cease to pull the thread of linen until it catches the artery, and flows through by its labor. 
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	And if the roots are thick, it is feared to cut them immediately because of the belly, but you can well cut half of it and then cauterize it so that it does not grow back. 
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then dress the wound, and be careful not to cut the tendon which is of a fox color, poor in feeling, and milk-like in appearance.  
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an inflamed abscess, and I will come to the treatment of chancre later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the arm is strong
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of a boil comes from cautery of a wound or a fissure in the flesh, and is on the belly and in some of the bowels, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is present, or from windiness; 
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is by the rupture of the flesh and by the issue of the bowels, then the color of the abscess appears like the color of the body, and it is a light matter without pain, and it opens from different issues. 
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse; and when one presses on its sides it springs back, and then returns, and by chance if it is tightened, it greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and through hard labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, but do not constrict it. 
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to blood, it opens with these signs: large and hard abscesses, and fixed according to a certain quantity. 
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work is such that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from an artery or vein, or windiness. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is fitting that you leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or bowels, it is fitting that you instruct the patient to hold his breath and be stretched out straight, then grasp all around the elbow. 
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then command him to grasp often between your hands, then go around the place that you have grasped with all of the spatula, then extend half of the abscess above to the whole large one. 
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then bind it around with a strong thread, or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let the knot be loose. 
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then work on half of the abscess extended above the ligature, and push your index finger in and grab the intestines; 
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it caught by the ligature, loosen it and push the intestine out of the belly;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find pus, grasp it with forceps and cut away the excess. 
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if an artery or vein opposes you, bind it well then return to your work and take two needles, thread them with strong thread, and push the two needles around what you have already done so that they pierce through. 
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then stretch the abscess in four directions over the needles, and if you see pus, remove the needles and leave the ligatures until they rot and let the dead flesh come off by itself. 
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	when you cut it when it is thin and rotten, then the care of what suits it, and open the abscess as we have said; 
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the area with what suits it, and suture the area. 
dou chancre	about a sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have said in the division the likenesses of a chancre, and how one should work with medicines, and how one should avoid the treatment of iron; 
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and say that the chancre spreads into the marrow, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and they said the ancients that when a chancre is in a place where it can be scraped, such as a chancre which is on the breasts, and on the thighs, and in similar places, it should all be removed when it is in the beginning;
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, it is not suitable that you approach it, for I can never cure any. 
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	No one has ever healed without me before. 
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the works, when it is in place or can be removed, as we have said, are that you purge the patient of black bile once; 
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	Then make him fast if he has manifest repletion, then put the patient in a good place to do the work; 
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	Then gather your ointments or poultices, and hair from all sides, and bone from all sides without leaving anything out;
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And let the blood run freely, and wipe the area with your hand or some other thing, and if the flow of blood prevents you from cutting the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is stemmed. 
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it with another cure until it is healed. 
de ydropisie	Of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have already said in the division the resemblances of dropsy, and in what manner the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron:
si est eclites soulement;	if it is only cracked; 
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one should not touch it with iron in these two cases: 
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	that is to say, tympanites and ileus, for it is a deadly thing; 
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	Therefore when you treat this kind of dropsy which is called "cracked" with medicine and the treatment does not help, consider whether the patient is weak or if he has another disease than dropsy, such as cough and loosening of the bowels and similar things; 
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	do not touch it with iron, for there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient is of strong constitution and he has only dropsy and is not too young nor too old, then you must proceed as follows: 
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	lay the patient straight on your hands, and have the attendants press the belly by pushing the point at the lowest part below the hip, then take the sharp pointed spatula in this manner:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cut in two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	At a point, and however it is not so deep that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and it cannot be broken. 
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	Then look if dropsy is drawn towards the intestines: 
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	If it is necessary that you cleave within the bowels, three fingers breadth below on the left side of the buttock.
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	And if dropsy is due to liver disease, then your incision should be on the left side of the bowels, three fingers breadth below. 
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	And if it is due to the spleen, then it should be on the right side, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie on the incision so that the superfluities do not flow into that weak spot.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	Then pierce all the skin with the instrument and push it in, and lift your hand on the whole length between the skin and the fascia as far as when scraping to the quantity of a nail or so.
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Then pierce the thighbone until the spatula arrives at the eighth place, and this is the place of the needle, then pull hard, and push this instrument which has this shape: 
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it resembles a subtle silver cane, and is made of iron or brass light, and has at the bottom part a small hole. 
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	And on one side, there are three holes. 
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	And two on the other side, and one on the other.  
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And the head is shaped like a pen, and this is the shape of the incision which scribes use to cut their pens. 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	At the top there is a handle, so that when the instrument arrives at the point, it now rests on the instrument.  
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	Then empty out half or a third part, because if you empty more than is fitting at that time, the patient might die due to the resolution of his spirit from the limb, or his head might become numb, or he might approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but according to its quantity of virtue, and according to what the patient's disposition signifies in relation to virtue; and his pulse; 
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	Then treat the instrument and hold the point, and it is now held by the heart which pierces the opening that is on the syfac, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; 
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	Then restart the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and treat the point with a small quantity; 
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Do this every day, and be careful not to press as long as it remains but a prick of a point.  
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt the patient, and leave much of a point there, if the treatment involves burial or hot sand, and through much sweating or bathing and in the sun, and if he drinks; 
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and the cure of drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the point, as I have said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	of the suppression of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without a hole in their penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, as soon as he has not pierced all the spatula very subtly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then put or make a small subtle plug of wool, and bind it and hold it thus for III days or IV and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug so that he may urinate, and then replace it; 
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and by chance it is not necessary, for the urine which comes will not allow it to be closed. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose opening is small, if it is treated with a clove of garlic, as we have said, it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the opening in its place are unfortunate, for no one is born with the opening at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before lifting their penis upward; 
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot copulate because the matter cannot come up to the bladder, and it is a bad disease. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the work is such that the patient lies often on his back, then they extend the head of the penis and the cap as the size of a quill, so that the urethra hole is in the middle, as it should be; 
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And beware of the discharge of blood that often comes, and if it happens, let the one who stops blood stop it, and treat the wound until it is healed. 
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Often these boils come on the penis, and they are an unsightly appearance of flesh;
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; 
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	it is necessary that you take them with a subtle lancet, and cut and cleanse all of them, then put moistened cotton with Egyptian ointment on top;
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with diachylon ointment until it is healed. 
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the wound is malignant, of a foul color and discharging, then it is fitting that you apply a cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have caught it, and if the foreskin is partly on the penis and partly inside the skin, then you must remove the part that is inside first. 
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	And when it is joined together, the treatment is outside. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you treat it all together, unless the head of the penis is surely secured so that it is not pierced, blackness and decay will come to the penis and the groin. 
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to remove everything that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from pomegranate bark and vinegar, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a flow of blood comes, apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	Cauteries assist in two ways together: 
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	that is to say, in the stopping of blood, and in counteracting corruption.
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the penis is corrupt and retracted, it is necessary that you draw or insert a cane of lead into the penis and have the patient urinate. 
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the hairs grow around the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, whether it is due to a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scorch it with a sharp instrument, until the bonds are loosened and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides. 
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if this is a difficult thing to do, it is necessary that you scorch it with a spatula at several points around the head of the penis and the skin. 
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	Then carefully separate them, and apply a thin linen cloth soaked in cold water so that it does not burn again. 
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not a loosening of continuity like other wounds; 
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Whenever we perform this work of our own volition, and especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best work, and the lightest for their safety. 
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have nothing more than what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I want the greater part of the masters and surgeons who performed circumcisions used to do it with a sharp knife, with force, and with all their might. 
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	This would split the heart because there are two membranes, and by chance if one cuts this one above it remains below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Here it is necessary to cut, and the pain is doubled, and at the cleansing which is of the two membranes, the point of the member is not reliably secure.
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	And at the cleansing of the one membrane, by chance the iron slips, and ruins the work, and many times they are born so that they do not need cleansing and I want it so. 
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	About the modification which is made to all the strength of the thread I have found the goodness of experience for the strengths cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if you cut equally in I all at once; 
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but let the threads be well twisted around the leather;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only doing it to tie the thread around his penis, and then comfort him in all ways that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	Then make it come out straight between your hands, and put the force between your hands or below your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; 
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	Then put your hand on the penis and blow where the heart is, and pull it up until the head of the penis is in; 
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then cleanse it well from the filth that has gathered there, then tie the place with a doubled thread, then tie it below the other ligature; 
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold it with the second ligature to the scrotum and index finger, and grasp between the two ligatures, then lift the heart quickly above it and pull the head of the penis; 
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood run drop by drop, for that is the cure; 
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on top and on the powder lay a cloth soaked in half an egg yolk cooked with rose water, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure it with other cures until it is healed. 
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of forces for purification is this: 
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	Let the two blades be held and sharp, and let the blades also be as large as the handle equally:  
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The error of purification is when the heart flees within the incision; 
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	Therefore it is fitting that you extend it to your fingernail, just as the sharp face of an abscess does:  
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	And the cup equally, and if you cannot hold it to your fingernail, then hold it with tongs, and then hold the cup. 
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they pass three days, and that which is under the foreskin is swollen, then leave it until the abscess below is appeased, and scrape it lightly; 
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If the cup moves as you can, and beware of the part of the foreskin, for it will not harm anything.  
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Therefore cure the place of things within a wound with powder as we have said in our treatise on powders and if one sews too much and it goes above it will not hurt. 
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore cure it as we have said until it is healed.  
dou retenement de l’urine	regarding retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is from obstruction by stone or congealed blood, or bowel, or flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the division. 
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	And if the urine is not released and you see that the retention is due to a stone at the neck of the bladder, it is fitting that the patient be bent on his knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	And let his feet be placed on his back and extend his belly above the back, and restrain the patient as much as he can. 
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	And then the neck of the bladder is constricted to expel the stone above so the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer an extraction with any instrument called a "syringe," which has this form: 
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it should be of fine silver, light and thin, like the feather of a bird; 
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and the tube should be one and a half palms long, and be fine at the head. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	The method for draining urine is such that you take a doubled thread and tie a piece of wool or cotton to the head, and insert the head of the thread into the syringe; 
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut off the excess wool and insert it up to the head of the syringe, then grease the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a stool, and anoint the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and lukewarm water; 
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	Then gently place the syringe into the penis, as far as it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis over towards the buttocks. 
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then push the syringe forward until it reaches the bladder, and let the patient feel it coming up to the empty place, and this is not done according to this order unless the one who guides it where it goes is crooked.  
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then stretch the thread all along the wool bit by bit, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out and let the urine flow. 
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And repeat with the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and align the patient.  
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorches or blood comes into the bladder, or putrefaction is gathered there, and you see sharp waters and medicines distilled, then make with all the instrument which is called "clepsedre," and it is of this form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if it has 3 openings: 
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	Two on one side and one on the other, as you see. 
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	And the veins are cut so that the medicinal court is such that it cauterizes the penis well without additional pain, if one can draw out the moisture and inject when necessary.  
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see your medicines settle in the bladder, put the head of the cautery into the moisture and draw it out with the instrument that is within. 
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	if you draw the moisture to the cautery, and then pull strongly on the instrument within;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	the moisture will enter within and come to the bladder immediately so that the patient will feel it. 
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of the subtle enema with which we enema the bladder
si est ci:	this is it: 
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is made of silver or boxwood, and the head is higher;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and below at its side where the linens are tied; 
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture that you see used to enema the bladder in it, then tie it between the two sides with a good strong thread doubled, and heat the tip of this moisture over the fire. 
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	Then put the head of the syringe into the penis, then hold your hand over the bladder so that all moisture comes out, until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder. 
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	And if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment and make a circle out of it, and pierce it round about. 
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	Then put a strong thread through these holes, then assemble the circle like one assembles a bowl, and put in it what you see of oil and moisture and vinegar, and tie it to the instrument. 
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And do as you did with the bladder, press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder. 
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have already said in the division the ways of stone and its extraction along with medicine. 
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	And we have said the difference between a stone embedded in the reins and all the signs, and which stones one should operate on. 
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	And I will tell you openly and briefly. 
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone that is lodged in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that the sharp point of the stone resembles a sharp point in its subtlety; 
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and it opens the urethra and scratches the patient's penis, and bends it many times, and then stiffens; 
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and many of these points dissolve.  
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	And the healing is light for children until they are four years old, and it is very grievous in the elderly, and it is in the middle for those who are between adolescence and old age; 
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.  
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient by enema, to draw out all the phlegm that is in the bowels.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it hinders sometimes to seek the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet and push them down so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes it comes out from there. 
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	Then make him sit between your hands evenly balanced, and let his hands be below his thighs so that his bladder is entirely inclined downwards. 
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	Then grasp it and press it inside. 
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	If you feel the stone in the space, hurry now and cut above the stone.  
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not budge at all when touched, moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand if the patient is a woman, or your middle finger if the patient is a young man who is fully grown. 
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	Insert it into its base and grasp the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, bind it at the neck of the bladder. 
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	Then press on top of your finger, and insert it at the opening where you see you must cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand and command him to extend his right hand upward with the testicles, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the testicles in the area where you are making the incision.
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then he inserts the spatula, cutting, with this form: 
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And he makes an incision between the buttocks and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left buttock; 
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and it shall be straight upon the stone, and your two hands shall be right there by the fundament, and the waist shall be made so that it is wide outside, and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; 
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	by chance the press with the hands which are by the fundament shall jump out without work;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and know that there are some stones which have angles and margins: 
si est griés a issir;	if it is grated to come out;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there are some which are underneath, resembling a lentil, and round, from which the issue is easy. 
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	Therefore when there are angles and edges, make the incision larger; 
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	And if it does not come out, you must pull it out with tongs that are like a file at the head, to extract the stone so that it does not escape. 
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	Or you insert a subtle instrument bent at the head;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	And if you cannot bring it out this way, widen the hole a bit, and if the sinew is cut, remove it with vitriol. 
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And if there are more than one stones, insert the largest one first into the neck of the bladder, then those above it, and treat them forcefully; then the smaller ones afterwards if there are several.  
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be sewn, and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the patient: 
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	Either he dies, or his urine comes out immediately because the veins cannot bind. 
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but nevertheless force yourself to pull it out, or to break it up with pincers, so that you pull it out piece by piece. 
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	And when you have completed your work, apply the wound with frankincense and aloes and dragon's blood, and extract it, and put on top a cloth moistened in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; 
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Then bind the patient under his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, if it rises very well in the place of oil and water, then cure it with ointment diafynacon and ointment basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if abscesses come in the wound and corrosions, and blood clots in the bladder, and urine is retained by it, which is known in part that without straining with the urine: 
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Therefore apply a poultice to the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and rot it; 
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then raise the wound with a needle and thread, and help it in all ways that you know until it is healed. 
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And it is necessary that every hour that you treat it, you bind his two thighs together and apply the medicines on the site. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small and it is lodged in the urethra and stuck so that urine cannot pass;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	if the cure I have just described is performed many times, one can be excused from cutting due to this treatment. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tried this way.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this shape and fix it at three angles in the fire:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone so that it cannot go back into the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then carefully insert the borer into the penis until it reaches the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the borer in your hand against the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone through to the other side;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	If urine comes soon, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it is soon broken, and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is healed; 
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot do this for anything that prevents it, tie one thread under the stone and the other above, then cut the penis where the stone is between the two threads, then extract it, untie the thread, and clean the frozen blood that is in the wound; 
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	from the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It can happen that a stone is lodged in women, and if it happens sometimes, the treatment is difficult, and it is forbidden for three things: 
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a woman who is well-informed and who will reveal herself to the doctor, even when she is chaste. 
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third manner is such that by chance one cannot find a woman well-knowing in this art of hands; 
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	And the fourth manner is such that the stone of the woman is more deeply embedded than the stone of the man, for which it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear. And if necessity compels you to this, it behoves you to take a midwife well-knowing, and with difficulty one finds her, and if you do not find her, then you should use a sharp, subtle knife; 
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and present a midwife well-versed in the lives of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command her regarding the inquiry into the stone; 
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look very closely whether the woman is a virgin: 
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it behoves you to put your finger or thumb on her fundament and seek the stone;  
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, she should constrain it below her finger, and instruct her to push her finger where the patient is, and want and press her left hand on the bladder. 
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she finds it, it is necessary that she moves it quickly from the entrance of the bladder down below, as far as it reaches the root of the thigh; 
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then put it on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the buttock, where it is moved together, and feel the stone in that part; 
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move her finger above the stone or below, and let the size be small at first;  
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then put the knife in the incision, if you feel the stone, enlarge the wound as much as the stone can come out forcefully, and know that there are many kinds of stones: 
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	These are to know, small and large, sharp and dull, long and round, and those that have barbs. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the arrowhead remains, put ground vitriol on it and hold it for an hour until the arrowhead is extinguished; 
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	Then return to your work, as long as the stone is strong, and have instruments that I told you in the extraction of the stone from men to help you in your work; 
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	And if the arrowhead remains and it is from an artery that has been cut, put powder on the site and bind it with tents and bandages, and do not touch it anymore, leave the stone and do not pull it out, lest the patient should die by chance. 
puis cure la plaie.	Then treat the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the flesh tightens, then return to your work, as long as the stone remains hard.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	The watery substance is nothing other than an accumulation of moisture or white phlegm, which is below the heart of the testicles, and which contains the seed.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	And it is called "syfac", and never properly in the web of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg. 
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	And it is the skin from which the white syfac comes as we have said. 
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	And this did not happen by chance. 
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this branch is so weak that it comes to the joints, and it spreads that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And never does it come from striking the testicles, and this moisture has many colors:  
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	it is yellowish, or without red, or black, or white watery, and more happens. 
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is white syfac as we have said, it is the boil of the testicles; the pain lasts as long as the shape of an egg and does not open the testicles because it has moisture all around. 
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if it has moisture in the web itself, it is a boil of the testicles with part of the egg, and therefore one thinks it is another egg. 
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white sinew, then he will feel it well. 
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	Therefore, when you see the color of the moisture, test all the instruments which are used for insertion beforehand, as its shape was before.  
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this which comes after the introducer, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we treat it with iron, it is fitting that the patient be cleansed according to our ability and the repletion of his body; 
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then lay him on his back, upon something a bit high, and put a lot of cloths under him;  
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left, and command the assistant to sit on his right, and extend the instrument toward one of the two ribs near the heart of the testicles; 
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the sharp spatula and cut the skin of the testicles along their length down to the pointy end, and make your incision perfectly straight by dividing the skin of the testicles up to the white sinew, and delicately scrape it according to your ability; 
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the syfac full of sharp points at a large hole, and extract all the sharp points, and then put your ointments, and extend the syfac upwards; 
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the heart of the cones, but only the syfac alone; 
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Cut all or by pieces immediately the side of it subtly, that if you do not cut it wisely, it will return sharp. 
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	And if the egg leaps from your work, so reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the syfac; 
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then join the two leaves of the heart of the cones with a stitch, then heal it as the other wounds, until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the egg corrupted by another illness, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, in doubting the outflow of blood. 
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	Then cut the scrotum with all its suspensory ligament, and extract the testicle, and treat it as we have said. 
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if the pointed object is assembled in two parts together, know that they are two branches;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	If you cut the other part as you have done the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and place in the wound linen soaked in rose oil; 
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And place another linen soaked in wine and oil, and put it on the two testicles, and put double cloths on top, and tie it all with a bandage according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths and fill them with shredded linen according to this appearance and let them be assembled by stitching in the throat of the breeches, and one side takes on the fundament up to the back, and the other at the part of the groin; 
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two chiefs on the two angles, and let all the assembly be gathered in the loop of the arm; 
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And it is never medicine this branch of cautery in place of iron cutting, and it is that you take the cautery knife subtle, and peel the skin of the testicles, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white fascia containing the sharp point is uncovered; 
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that fascia with it, and scald it with this subtle hot cautery:  
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And the peel in all the ways that you can, as long as you uproot everything; 
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and be careful that the fire does not touch the testicle; 
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	And know that this work is safer;  
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and watch out for the outflow of blood, and it is better than the works of cutting. 
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if anything opposes you, whether an abscess, discharge of blood, or something else, treat what opposes you, according to what has been said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this work because of its horror, then administer a perforation as I tell you, and know that when you are well-assured by the signs we have mentioned that the watery humor is there, then make the patient sit on a raised seat; 
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	then pierce the abscess at the bottom part, as wide as a span, and make the perforation as long as the body; 
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and let the opening be wide so that all the pus can flow out;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then place cotton on the spot and bind it, and let it stay to drain the remaining pus, then treat it until the wound is healed; 
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white cloth does not let the humor escape into the mouth of the wound, then you must put a feather or the instrument with which one treats the humor of dropsy in it, its form being as shown before; 
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and enlarge the wound a bit, and know that the humor will return and gather again after six months or so, and when it gathers as before, then the patient will spend his days like that. 
de l’aposteme des coions	from a boil on the buttocks
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this branch, fear has many dispositions, for which it seems to me better to leave it. 
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	And I will tell you the work and the resemblances of an abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say therefore that many abscesses come on the body, and likewise on the testicles;
et c’est par mout de cas.	and it is by many causes.  
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is to know by excessive sourness and sharpness, which is spread to the joints, or from percussion. 
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	And the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; 
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And find no pain, and it is an abscess of sorrow. 
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And by chance there are abscesses grievously porous and pierced, and of a dark color, and sometimes it comes from the new growth of an artery, or swelling of a vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from the new growth of an artery, it is known by the hot disposition of the abscess when you press it with your fingers. 
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	And it is not fitting that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	That which is made from swelling of the vein is known by its disposition at the touch of the fingers, and one can well make an incision on this type, and on the other types.  
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	And it is that you cut the heart of the testicles, then lift up the egg, and pull out the cord from white fat, and deliver the suspensory ligament from all sides of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already dried with these fresh charcoals, then it is fitting that you pull out the egg and cut it. 
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is adhered to the fat, or in that which is within the vessels, then it is fitting that you deliver all of that tendon, and cut it roundly. 
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is behind or further back, it is fitting that you cut it all, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, apply the wound with wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	from a boil on the buttocks
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess wrapped in an envelope resembling a burr, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient groans when he goes. 
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	And the treatment for this disease is as dangerous and difficult as this one before it, nevertheless we will tell you its work according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is fitting that you make the patient sit on a raised seat, then you put the suspensory of the testicles down to your thighs, to all the vessels that are near the penis, and bind them tightly, and extend them. 
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	Then cut with a sharp scalpel in a wide place so that the vessels are exposed, and then flay on each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries which are in the temples; 
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then insert a needle with a doubled thread and tie it at the first place where the vein appeared and tie it securely to the other end.  
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then cut them straight down the middle according to the length of the body, and extract the corrupted humors.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then dress the wound as other wounds where one injures bowels so that no vessel bleeds which nourishes one of the testicles. 
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for through this there comes no harm, and if all the vessels are seen, then it is fitting to draw the veins of all the vessels; 
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the bone does not lose its nourishment through the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be helped. 
de la routure dou syfac	Of the fracture of the bone
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The occurrence of this branch is through the section that comes or arises, or the extension on the belly in the part of the intestines, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the veins; 
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this rupture is either at the symphysis or from the extension of it, and these two manners come from much of the same causes: 
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	either by percussion, or by a jump, or by a struggle, or by lifting something too heavy, and by similar things; 
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is from the extension of the symphysis are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; 
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	And the abscesses are equalized until towards the end, so that the pus hastens the intestines. 
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.
