And the signs are when it is of the section of the gut, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and there are various abscesses appearing underneath the skin nearby, and this is due to the exit of the intestine and the body being outside the gut.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never pull out the intestines with the hernia, and it is held back there, and causes great pain to the patient, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments, because of fear, one should avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the manner of the work is such that you instruct the patient to knead the intestines with his hand inside the wound if he can enter. 
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	Then let it be rubbed on his neck between your hands and lift the thighs.  
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	Then stretch the heart above and cover all the skin of the testicles from length. 
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then put inside the folds of the waist a knife according to what you need to open the wound, and let it be such that the bones can come out.  
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then flay the pus that is under the skin of the testicles until the white pus hard is uncovered from all sides. 
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	Then put your index finger in that which follows the testicle, in that which is between the white pus that is under the skin of the egg, and between the second pus, and part that which is behind the egg, and between the second pus.  
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and then place your right hand inside the patient's buttocks
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and instruct the minister to extend the egg upward, and untie what is aired behind the ligature; 
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and inquire at your leisure if there is any intestine wrapped around or white sinew hard, and if you find nothing, put the end in the belly below; 
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	then take a needle with a large thread made of ten threads, and put it in the back part near the sinew, which is after the skin of the testicles; 
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	after the waistline, then cut the flesh that appears from the threads, as long as there are four threads;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	then assemble them one upon the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the sinew, of which we have said is below the skin of the testicles, with a strong ligature of two parts; 
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the flesh around the threads and tie them in two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish it can enter within, so that no abscess may come there. 
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and put a second bandage over the first, twice as long as it, and after these two bandages leave two fingers' breadth below the heart of the groin. 
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	and then all the rest according to the roundness that the egg carries.  
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	Then bind in the part which is below the skin of the groin as long as the sinews and bowels are bound, as we have said before. 
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Then apply wool softened in oil to the wounds and bind it with the bandage we have described.  
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never are the white sinews cauterized as we have said, after the incision, for fear of stopping the flow of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	For this happens often and leave the bandage on until it oozes through it; 
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if it is slow to drain, raise it with hot water and place it on top of what we have said until it drains. 
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then treat the wound with another dressing until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I never saw anyone who dared to make the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made like a branch which is together with the screw, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after the incision on the thigh slightly below. 
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	Then sew it to me, and heal the abscess of he who works, as long as the vessels weep;  
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heal it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	Sometimes rupture comes in anger, as we have said, and open the veins;  
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and do not draw out any of the intestines like onions, and if some are drawn out, it is bad, and repair every hour; 
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and nevertheless if it remains too long in this place, the wound or fistula grows, until the intestines are drawn out; 
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens because of the extension of the fistula which is at the anger, as we have said, for it is extended, then softened and swells the veins and opens them; 
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	and its treatment is by cautery, as we have said before; 
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and it is sometimes cured with iron in this manner: 
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	and the patient lies frequently on his back between your hands, then cover the place of the rupture swollen about three widths; 
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then pull out the sinew which is below the skin than usual, then take a red-hot iron and place it on the exposed sinew spot; 
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press down to the deepest part of the belly, then cauter the two spots exposed by the sinew on the top of the iron and cauter one and the other; 
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then remove the top of the iron, and do not cover the sinew nor extend the wound or anything else, as I have shown you in the cure of a rupture of the intestines; 
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Then cure it with the cure of wounds. 
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, let the patient cleanse and care for the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sinew is constricted, and has no appearance in the fracture, and the cauteries are milder in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in some men because the flesh that is inside is softened, and it is made to be seen. 
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	And it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back and cuts away the softened skin onto the natural skin.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	Then bring the two edges together with one stitch, and if you see, sew the excess of the softened skin at three or four stitches firmly.
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Then cut between the stitches and cure it like the other wounds until it is healed, and remove the thread. 
dou chastrement	Through chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Know that castration is forbidden in our law, and for this reason it would please me not to speak of it in this book. 
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and it is necessary only in two ways: 
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one of which is that the patient in his reason responds when asked, and knows the treatment; 
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often need to castrate some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say therefore that castration is done according to two methods:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	either by attraction or by incision. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In that which we do by attraction, we make the beast sit in hot water, until the testicles are softened and hanging; 
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then take them with your hand, until they are withdrawn and you no longer feel them. 
Du chastrement de taille:	Of castration of the tail:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	it is necessary that you hold the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut above each testicle one cut, when you have well skinned them;
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	And he leaves no mark or subtle mark which is on the vessels; 
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	And this manner of castration is better than that which is done by attraction, because in attraction there may remain by chance some parts of the testicles, by which the beast desires lust. 
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then heal the wound until it is healed.  
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphroditism occurs in two ways for men: 
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	One is that between the two testicles there appears also a shape like that of a woman's nature, or it may have hair, and sometimes urine flows into it.  
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is for women, and it has on the belly like a rod and two horns.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the treatment for both men and women is that you cut off all the added parts and treat them like other wounds; 
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	In the second manner, of men whose urine flows through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.  
de la tentigene	Of the tendon
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	A splint is a piece of wood added to the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; 
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	And some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure. 
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It is necessary that you hold the excess of the splint in your hand or at your elbows, and bind it lightly; 
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not bind too tightly, so that blood does not flow, then treat with another treatment until it is healed; 
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and to another splint that grows at the mouth of the marrow and the bone, and by chance jumps out, and according to its appearance it is like a cow, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow disease". 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you cupping it as we have said the tenting, and heal it until it is healed.
de erratique	Of wandering
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	It is erratic if the nature of the woman is not perceived, or if the opening is small; 
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	And it is natural by birth, or accidental through illness that it has come. 
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	Or it is by chariot added, or through subtle force or hope, and it is made perfect in the marrow, or in the ribs, or below, or wherever it may be. 
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	And they differ in conception, and childbirth, and by chance having flowers.  
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	And the knowledge of these is through the gaze of the bailiff. 
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the splinters are near and visible, whether on the left or right.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is through subtle force, and it is close to two leaves, if you hurry, they will come thus. 
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	Put your two index fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, spreading her legs;
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	then extend the two leaves until the subtle force is gone, and the swellings are over. 
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	Then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on the spot, and let the woman stay at home each day so that she cannot solder. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the synovial membrane is hard and thick, it behoves you to cut it with a scalpel resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the splinter is of oak wood, then suspend it at the onion and the copper. 
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	And have the medicines steeped in blood, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, all together with egg yolk. 
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	Then apply a leaden cane wide enough so that the wound cannot close up. 
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	And thus for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen.  
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then it should be cured with other remedies until it is healed. 
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a boil comes with flesh, if it suits to cover according to this manner, except for ulcerated abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an inflamed abscess in the marrow, one must not use fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which do not usually bleed, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hard. 
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	And we have said in the division the resemblances of others, and the signs, and I will say here those which receive cure. 
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and fissures when they are completely embedded in the anus, and do not appear to the touch, unless they are cauterized by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the ulcer, one can feel, are those one can cleanse.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	Therefore it is necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then extend the hemorrhoid with tongs and copper on its roots, then sprinkle powder of blood-stopping medicines such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; 
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	Then put its feet to the wall for an hour, then put it in cold water. 
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	And if blood flow comes, then place it in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and gall nuts and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make a plaster on its back. 
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it goes out, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If not, apply cupping to its back and breasts without injury. 
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	Then take wool, soak it in plantain juice or hawthorn juice with old wine, and apply it to the area. 
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointment until it is healed;
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	and the one called "albathir" is red and resembles a rough head, so cover it as I said for the thelul. 
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then cure it until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the sea
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come in the sea, such as ulcers and piercing abscesses and herpes and swellings and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	It is therefore necessary that I say in this treatise about the hot abscess which comes to the marrow, which is not among the abscesses which they call boils; 
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you wish to know the work of iron, see if the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.  
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Then do not hurry to pierce it, but let it mature until the pain is eased; 
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then have the patient sit on a stool, and have two small stools where he can lean, and support himself on his back and bring together his feet at the farthest part from the leg; 
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and let his thighs be spread apart, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; 
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	Then suck the jawbone towards the left side, and bring the instrument with which one operates the mouth of the wound, from which the form will then come.  
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	And it is necessary that when you see this instrument administered, you insert the point first to know the depth of the wound, so that what enters the instrument does not go any deeper than it should and does not injure the patient. 
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	And if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the wound with cloths so that the instrument does not injure it. 
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	And it is necessary that he put the funnel of the instrument above and hold the instrument.  
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscess opens, and one makes it with the hand soft, then if it is necessary to cover it at the head, at the spatula left.
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	and when the bowel is emptied, it is fitting that you put into the wound tents softened in oil of roses, or in oil of green vitriol. 
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and put the tent firmly from the wound to the edge of the marrow, and put by outside on the marrow and on the point wool clean softened in water where agrimony or mullein are cooked; 
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure afterwards every two days with ointment suitable to this, until it is healed;
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and at no time raise the marrow and the wound by an enema of water and honey, and then of water or long roots of lily and birthwort are cooked; 
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	then return to the ointment. 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healed in the marsh, it is necessary that you refrain from using a hot iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the form of natural childbirth, and the signs if it be so when you see the woman press down below, and desire to smell vinegar: 
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	Then hasten to let the child's breath out; 
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	Then know that such a birth is according to natural form, and the issue is below its head, and the second twin with it; 
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	And when you see these signs, it is fitting to press its belly lightly so that the child issues quickly;
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	For when it descends upon its head, then the second twin comes with it, and the mother is delivered of her superfluities by good purification; 
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	And this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.  
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it sometimes comes upon its feet, and the body or the head and hands come first, or it comes upon its belly, or often, and is turned by chance out of its neck, and by other bad figures;  
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these matters, and to beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should help her. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the child comes out on its own through natural birth, and the woman gives birth easily, and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a saddle where women hold her. 
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	And let oil or fenugreek be cooked according to its nature, and then put the ball between her thighs the small spatula of which is this shape: 
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	And split the second fingernail, and scrape at its corner until the moisture that is within runs out;  
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and press the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must give the woman a clyster of fenugreek mush with sesame oil; 
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	then have her take and sneeze repeatedly, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour:
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	If the child is now delivered. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if the two hands come out fully, then you must reset them lightly bit by bit; 
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a seat and raise her feet. 
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	Then raise the seat from the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall when it is raised. 
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if her hands cannot enter and the child is dead, cut her hands with a knife that has been placed beforehand and extract the child and reset it equally. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child upon its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes onto its feet, it must be pushed upward; 
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it back and forth until it is equal.
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	Then take it by the feet and extend it back and forth. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	If it jumps up to its thighs, command it to grasp and make it sneeze from being restrained. 
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps further, may God will it. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, turn it little by little until it is according to its natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is light.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it does not come strong as we have said, take a mixture of hawkweed, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and crush everything in a mortar. 
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	And put it on the nature of the woman inside and heat this ointment, then have her sit in hot water up to below the ribs. 
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	And when she is softened underneath, make a plaster of myrrh for her and put it underneath, and leave it for an hour. 
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	Then have her sit on a stool, then make her sneeze and pull out her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, for the infant will now leap. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the infant comes in this form, if he puts his hands on it bit by bit;  
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then be careful and hang him by his neck, and let his feet dangle down, and let him lie on the bed. 
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and fold her hands little by little, then take her hands upon the belly, and remove the cushions underneath, until she is exposed below; 
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if her child does not jump, then he takes her feet and moves them upwards, then he moves the belly up, then he puts his hands in; 
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and draws out the child little by little;  
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and instructs the woman to hold still until her child emerges. 
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the delivery of a child who comes forth with one hand extended
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	It is necessary to engineer to return the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot return it, then make the woman stand up and walk; 
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, then make her sit on the bed, and unbend her legs upwards;  
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then apply the poultice that I have described; 
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a chair, and then study to return the hand;  
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	And take the child according to its natural form and make it sneeze, and command her to hold herself as long as the child remains still. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the delivery of the child upon its neck, and has spread its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	It is fitting that the healer has their hand, then turns it a little at a time, and takes it lightly;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is equal, put on the natural muscle oil and oil, as we have said, then command her to move a little at a time; 
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, make her sit on a seat, and command her to hold herself; 
et la fai esternuer.	and make her sneeze. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner for all the second
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes strong in this manner throughout the entire second joint, grasp the second joint with your fingernail, as long as the moisture is drained; 
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child can lean on its face and neck, grasp it from below, so that it is not held back, and the child dies;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	Then put the child inside as long as you have placed it as it should be, and instruct the woman not to move at all: 
adonques si istra legierement.	then if she moves slightly. 
de l’issue des gemelz	from the removal of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born: 
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	and this is not a strange thing, and it does happen.  
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are a strange thing and do not live if they are named: 
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they be multiplied and are delivered by the suture which divides them, which is tied to the belly button: 
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they are also born naturally as one under all, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they are born in a difficult way, the care is as we have said, and let the midwife be subtle, and do quickly and lightly what she does: 
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do so as it is necessary for salvation. 
de plusors enfans	of several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	Sometimes they are formed in the marrow I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or several up to XV, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the glorious sage, and it is fitting that the bailiff knows all this, for by chance similar things may happen; 
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	if you do according to what is necessary. 
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman for a dead child in the womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to work with your hands; 
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is fitting that you know whether the woman is of sound constitution, and does not have an accident or fear of death; 
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is fitting that the woman be placed on her back, with her shoulders inclined downward, and her legs raised;
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the midwife takes hold of it in two parts, where it is tied to the bed so that it is not treated until the child is delivered; 
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the womb with wet oils mixed with marshmallow and fenugreek seed and linseed, then anoint her hands with these oils and these mixtures; 
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	then gently insert them into the womb, then wants the place where she inserts the fingers to be convenient for this, and take care that if the infant is attached it descends on its head; 
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	if she inserts her fingers into its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or into the nape of the neck or near the ribs, and if the descent is on its feet, she inserts them at the hip and middle ribs;  
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that she holds the finger in her right hand, and puts the curve between her fingers of the left hand, and inserts it with all her hand gently, and inserts the finger into any of these places we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty thing; 
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the lancet: 
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then insert against the other lancet, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal.
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then extend them equally by moving back and forth, to make it come out, and let the lancets have teeth to hold it, as the shape is like this: 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if a part remains, anoint the base with some of its oil, and put them in that part, and draw out the other part. 
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if none remains, put this lancet or higher up, and do this until it all comes out. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes forward over the other and it cannot be brought back by tightening, then it is fitting that you wrap a cloth around it until it all rises.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	Then apply the cup to the joint of the foot or at the knife's edge, and so you must do with the other hand, and for both feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the child's head is large and it is stuck at birth, or if it has a sharp point assembled, you must put the splintered spatula between your fingers and cut the point and extract it. 
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you will return it to the instrument which is called "almidach," of which the form comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one.  
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	And in the same way do so if the infant has a large head naturally; 
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then draw the bones with tongs, and if the head jumps out and is extracted forcefully, it should be split, so much that the moisture which is in the bad delivery is removed. 
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot come out, cut it into pieces as small as you can. 
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, it must be pierced so that the moisture runs out. 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the infant is on its feet, the attraction is light, and the straightening at the mouth of the uterus is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is embedded in the belly or the breast, it must be extracted wrapped in a cloth upon the hand; 
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and pierce the belly or the breast, so that the moisture within runs out; 
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if the other members are removed and the head remains, put the hand of the patient into a pot of warm water, and pull it up to the mouth of the pot. 
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	Then put in one or two ounces, and boil it hard; 
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the pot is constricted due to a hot boil that has come, then it is not right to work on it, but rather administer moist and fatty things.
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And let the dispenser apply plasters, which are soothing and moistening. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the infant is on its side, and you can put it straight, apply what we have said in the living child; 
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and if there is no way, cut the flesh into pieces and leave nothing of the afterbirth.  
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, apply what we have said for abscesses that come in the marsh; 
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if bleeding occurs, apply a strong astringent bandage and administer other remedies.  
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb a child had been dead, then she conceived another upon that one, and the other was also dead.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, a boil came on his arm, and it swelled so much that it burst, and began with great discharge.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to heal, and I thought for a long time, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and one bone came out, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvelled greatly, because it has no bones in its belly.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I treated the wound and set the bones until the woman was better; 
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and I kept the woman like this for a long time, so that there would be just a little swelling in its place;  
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have only recorded this chapter so that when the masters encounter a strange thing they know what to do. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring back the marrow to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	Here follows the form of the presser, with which one presses the books. 
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and at two turnings are the heads of the two linen cloths.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nevertheless, the horns should be more slender than those of the restrictor, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; 
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and the mouth of the spindle should be two fingers wide, and the margin of the trees one finger, and a length of a palm and a half;  
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and between the two linen cloths there should be two adjustments of this same spindle, which are fastened on one side and the other, a half palm in length or a finger more. 
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	And these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the press to open when one turns the two horns.  
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more slender and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood spindle, according to the appearance of tongs.
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and it has two arms for adjustments, as you see, one palm long and two palms wide. 
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	And when you see the vulva open to all instruments, have the woman sit on the bed with her feet dangling and legs open, then insert both arms fitted together into the vulva, and hold the head of the instrument beneath between her thighs. 
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Then work your hand on the whole instrument as you did with the forceps equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the vulva, so that the woman does what she wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	These instruments are all assembled and are multiplied in their likenesses. 
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	And when she sees them matched, the work is all the more hasty, and higher are men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despair of the instrument until you have prepared it, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze deliberately, and remove your hands from her mouth and nose; 
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if it comes out that way, all is well.  
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If not, take a pot and make a hole or lid in it, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia lignea and centaury; 
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in a pot with water over the fire; 
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	then put a cane or tube in the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the womb, and let it steam until the vapors enter the womb; 
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	then make her sneeze, as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second bone leaps quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not strong, command the patient to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or mallow poultice, and then plunge it into the wound, and hold it there for a while. 
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	And when she has found it, grasp and extend it little by little straight, so that the marrow does not break during extraction. 
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	But you must move it slightly to the right and left, and then draw it out.
si venra et se desaerdra.	It will come and loosen. 
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the opening of the marrow is constricted, we have said the cure is sneezing and fumigation with herbs. 
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	And if it is not from all of this which we have said, be careful that you do not pull against the grain.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	But it is fitting that what is at the opening of the marrow, you tie it to the thigh of the woman, then apply an enema with tetrapharmac ointment.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if he carries it and puts it back, and will come strong; 
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but all the same, when it is carried so it comes with bad smell to the stomach and head, and harms the patient. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	So therefore proper fumigations are needed for this:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	None of the ancients have proven fumigation of watercress and dried figs. 
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates a woman to retain her flowers and her secundines is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it seems like a reed, and one puts the subtle head in its nature, and the heads wide on the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigations be on the coals, and the scab as long as it is gone, and start another.  
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but rather have a subtle tool: 
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	so it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that tool with her finger, and not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and guard against touching the opening.  
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put it on linen soaked in wine and oil, then treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will stay in place, insert or put a cane of wood and leave it for three days, and let it be removed when the child wants to go into its chamber.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And sometimes this inflammation comes from the suppuration of a wound or abscess; 
si covient coper celui soudement:	if it is necessary to cover that suppuration: 
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	If it is healed as we have said of the cane of a plum tree. 
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that come below the buttocks are nodules and swellings that come from beneath the buttocks or in the space between the two parts, whether it is one fistula or several; 
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	And when that nodule is old, if it works and still gives off white or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; 
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	And they are known by the fact that there is either discharge or flatulence when the patient has a bowel movement, and perhaps one jumps out. 
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if there are fistulas that extend to the bladder, and to half of the penis; 
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and they reach the junction of the thigh, and to the knee. 
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one recognizes a fistula penetrating the fundament, and not penetrating.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And it is that you stick your index finger or the fundament, and insert a fine needle of steel or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is tortuosity, then you insert a tent of fine silk thread, or a horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair with your finger. 
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	And if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge of pus, flatulence, or worms as we have said. 
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	Know that it does not penetrate.
si te haste dou curer.	if you hasten to cure 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula extends as far as the bladder or as far as the urine channel, then if the urine escapes and cannot be stopped by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced as far as the joint of the thigh, so the attempt comes as far as the place. 
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If there is no crookedness and the invention of pain turns inward, so it is that he will go there now, and no medicine or ointment by application is worth.  
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these persistent fistulas there is no cure except toil, and vanity of foolish sights that interpose themselves. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In that which is not persistent and is not ancient, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back. 
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	And he lifts his legs up to his thighs, and puts his thighs inclined toward his belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then put in a tent of iron, or lead if there is crookedness, as far as you know where the tent comes. 
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels it around the base, it is fitting that you put your index finger there, and if you then feel that the tendon has been pierced; 
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and whether it is uncovered or you feel between your finger the sinew or flesh, then know that it has been pierced. 
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If there is no work to be done on it, it cannot be healed.  
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is said that one can heal anyone well, but this happens rarely 
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help that is done, if it is heated according to the width of the fistula as it has been said before. 
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	And put the whole hot cautery into the fistula, as long as it comes out at the base;
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this two or three times until you know that these faulty flesh are burned, which resemble a bird's feather. 
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	And then the cure of softened tents with butter until that which burns is extinguished, then the cure of ointment spreading and healing. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is healed like this, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it cannot otherwise be healed; 
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	And if the tent enters and does not pierce through to the bone which is at its foundation, and between your finger and the tent there is a thick covering of flesh or sinew, and you see the fistula under that which covers the core;  
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	If the opening of the beginning of the fistula is found and pushed forward before the tent, then apply the cautery afterwards until it reaches the head of the tent;  
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	And the tent will be delivered and will fall away. 
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	Then cleanse those charred parts which resemble a bird's feather and leave none remaining. 
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood comes, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For fire cautery accomplishes two things: 
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	This is to know, the cautery of these added meats, and the suppression of blood and the drying of moisture. 
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	Then the treatment of softened tents in butter or in crushed hazelnuts, as long as the embers burn well, and it becomes stronger when the meats are burned in the bowels. 
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then treat the wound with ointments of boiled dried herbs.  
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way to the foundation and is far from the body, it should be treated with a poultice or foundation, and inquire about this.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the tent and between II is the cloth or the silk or meat, where it is about to pierce, if there are no other ways of faith and hope except through the administration of one of the III manners: 
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put tents and treat them as first.  
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	And do not go too deep so that you do not cut the ligament that holds the foundation, and the evacuations come through the intentional sense. 
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then the cure, as we have said; 
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and cleanse it once it is cut away from the base, either by hand or by another pointed instrument; 
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then cleanse that corrupted flesh which is in the wound, as much as you can;  
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part behind the base: 
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it were a lighter thing for the patient. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And fistulas are never made in this manner: 
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and when you put the tent into the fistula, and it is near or touches the base under the skin above, then take a tent pierced at its head according to this form:  
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I bend the thread twice, and put the tent on all the thread into the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is passed through the edge of the base inside, then pull out the thread from that pierced spot, so that you put your finger or thumb in the base; 
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and treat the head of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and separate one from the other, and leave it for one or two days; 
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it several times, until the thread catches these bars that are between the two, and they click; 
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then treat the wound until it is closed and healed. 
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, make it pierce through all the ways that you can, as long as it is not too constricted.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to treat for placement or covering with a bandage so perfectly, and then cure as we have said, until it be healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the pointed spatula with which you make a fistula must be very sharp on one side and cutting;  
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other side not sharp, so that you don't cut what you shouldn't cut, as you see here: 
des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Hemorrhoids are according to two ways: 
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	where they are inside the buttocks, like grains of rosin, and there are small ones and large ones, and they often bleed, and there is one or several, and they protrude from the buttocks and at the top of the buttocks;
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	But those that are heated have a little moisture, and still again or a little bit of sharp citrus or a little bit of blood, and they have the color of the body. 
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	And the treatment for those who have them in the foundation, it is as if you instruct the patient to stretch himself out so as to go into chambers until the foundations dry up and the threads appear; 
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	If you hurry, and can grasp it with tweezers, or hold it with your fingernail, then cut it at its roots.  
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	And if the tweezers cannot hold them due to their moisture, take them with linen, or cotton, or a piece of chamois. 
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	And pull them out at your leisure, then cut them off and sprinkle some hot powders that are in place of a cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	Or cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then treat them with other remedies until he is healed. 
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot come out, then give the patient a harsh and pungent enema to cleanse what is in the foundation so that it may come out openly. 
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	and if the patient can be pressed, and if the threads are strong from the foundation, then the treatment is easy.  
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and you take them with your fingernail or forceps and cut them off, then treat it as we have said until it is healed, and he fears the incision by iron.  
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	If it is necessary that you administer a suture according to this manner: 
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take a twisted thread and put it in a needle, and then pull the thread over and make the needle pierce through the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and it should be wide. 
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	Pull the thread tight, then tie a knot in the thread and remove the needle, and do the same for all the others, and leave one to drain off excess blood.  
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	Then put on the bandage softened in rose oil or cerate, and put it on the bandage, and instruct the patient to rest. 
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then leave it until it heals, and when they are healed, apply ointment and other treatments until it is healed. 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	for the drying of wounds or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there occurs drying up of the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you hold the tip of a spatula or your fingernail on top of it so as not to let it get wet. 
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	Then treat it until it is healed as needed. 
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	And if it cannot heal, shave it again more forcefully than before until it heals completely and is scraped. 
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed. 
dou fremit	Where it trembles
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A boil is a small faulty appearance near the body, and it spreads quickly.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes you find the cold there, and one feels it also like a deathly shiver, and it comes throughout the body, and most of all in the hands than anywhere else. 
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the remedy is that you take a cane from a goose feather or a strong vulture feather, and place that cane upon the shiver, until the circles completely encircle the shiver; 
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand all the way around the cane until you encompass the whole shiver, and put it in perfectly, and pull the shiver out from its roots.  
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make one of a chain of iron or according to this form, and let it be subtle below and sharp above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	Do not pierce, but hold on to the pain, and press. 
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see it, cauterize the shiver, as it is described in the chapter on cautery.  
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Sometimes one makes an enema of silver or artichoke, or melted iron or malleable iron; 
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	And at no time are these instruments made small or large, according to those to whom they are administered. 
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then who minister to children in their care and are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large enema is wide on top, where the belly is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	And if there is a separation where the stomach is tied as you see it and the flesh is pierced inside.  
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	And there are two holes on one of the sides and one on the other. 
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And the stomach where one puts medicines is made from a beast's bladder or parchment and pierced all around with small holes, with one finger's width of space between each hole, then threaded through these holes with a thick thread, twisted in an X shape or round about, and the belly is assembled like a goat. 
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	And when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread in front, then administer an enema.  
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And this is the shape of the circle: 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or yolk of egg, or something similar, then insert it gently. 
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	Then he presses the ministers with his two hands together, until it is all full, then extracts the clyster, and lifts the patient's legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him hold it as long as he can; 
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And if he sleeps a whole night like that, it is of greater help.  
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize it for a disease of intestinal flux, and the medicine hastens to enter, then resume until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are on the fundament or an abscess, let the clyster be as subtle as for a child; 
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle clyster where the skin is drawn out:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; 
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We will tell you the cures of hands and of medicine, according to accomplishment. 
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the striking of stone, and the cutting of sword and knife, or of spear or of gun or of arrow, or of similar things;
