ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or they are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; 
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and begin with the wounds of the head that are simple, for the remembrance will come in its chapter. 
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that it is from the striking of stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt a hot abscess: 
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	If it bleeds readily from the cephalic vein itself, and only a little blood comes from the wound, and the bleeding is on the opposite side of the injured part; 
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and have the patient abstain from wine and rich foods. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if it does not bleed, reduce their food intake, do not let them drink wine, nor eat meat. 
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	And place on the wound, if an abscess begins to form, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in astringent wine. 
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	And if there is no heat in the abscess, apply to the wound, if it is fresh and bleeding freely, and not moved by air, a powder which I will mention a little later. 
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has been disturbed, apply ointments until it is healed.  
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together with sutures, as I will say for wounds in the belly, about suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is uncovered from the bone, and can move, and only holds by a point, then cut it. 
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Then dress the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as testicles and cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rotten skin, and it does not reach the bone, cut out all the rot thoroughly, and pour strong water over it, then dress it. 
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if it has an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped without cutting, and it cannot be staunching by medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it loose, tie it with a thread. 
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does no good, then cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the dressing is light.
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And put this powder on it so that it welds just as if the fire had moved it. 
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the manner of the powder is:  
pren encens une partie;	Take incense one part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	Dragon's blood two parts; 
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	Live lime three parts, and powder it subtly, and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly, until it burns well and joins with all its blood; 
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	And then bind it well, and leave it unbound, if it does not swell; 
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	For one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.  
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never is this done with chalk alone, when one does not have incense nor the blood of a dragon, but that the fire has heated the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the fire has moved the wound, put this powder on it immediately; 
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	But put some digested ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it runs clear;  
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let him be treated with other treatments until he is healed. 
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, extract it with fine forceps;  
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about skull fractures later. 
de la plaie dou col	from the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, it has no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is nerves, there is nothing else to do but leave the treatment alone and not put anything binding on it, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract; 
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of nerves is cold, and their connection with the brain, which is the highest member, 
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be under it, such as chamomile steeped in warm water and mixed with rose oil, and chamomile washed also in warm water, and other mine stones according to this manner, and moist ointments. 
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is covered and full of pus, then pierce it lower. 
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut and blood flows, then loosen it, tie it off, and cautery is necessary. 
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	And if the spine of the throat is cut or the heart and the conduit that carries the flesh are preserved, then sew the heart onto the bone of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back into its natural shape. 
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then carefully remove it and leave it for a few days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed. 
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	And if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then scrape it. 
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	And if there are bone fragments, remove them all if you can, and if you cannot obtain them, leave them until the wound festers and is cleansed, aligning the opening. 
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wound is fresh, put powder on the powder that I have said. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of the wound of lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a cut from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, look to see if the wound has a foul odor that makes the patient faint: 
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	Then you know the wound is mortal. 
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	And if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put any powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it because the blood will not flow freely and return to the heart, and kill the patient. 
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	But apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day. 
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	And if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb excess moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	if there will come no spasm, nor bad trembling of heart nor strangeness from elsewhere; 
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good signs, know that the wound is saved. 
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat it then with bandages and other treatments, until it is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, and works, then know that there is a fistula; 
si la cure si com on doit.	if the treatment is as it should be.  
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from an incision of a sword or knife, and it is simple, whether on the leg or the back, treat it like those that are in front.  
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	If it is large, stitch it; 
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, with powder, and if it is embedded in the bone and has broken into pieces, clean the wound, and treat the foreign bodies if they are loose; 
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not weaned, leave the wound to fester, which will lighten the extraction. 
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And for other wounds on other limbs, judgment is as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	of rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great, medium and small; 
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the great wound sometimes the intestines or nerves of the intestines protrude, by which the introduction of others;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one because they put the intestines back in more carefully, if they do not put them back hot against hot;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines swell quickly when they feel cold, and enter more carefully, and for this reason, the medium wound is better because they put back the intestine in its place more easily than the others. 
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that a rupture of the belly is according to four manners: 
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the suture of other wounds of the body and two other proper sutures are common to other wounds. 
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And nevertheless they are more appropriate with the suture of the belly, and I will say each one and declare it.  
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine is outside, and easy things are put back in place, this is done in one of two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold. 
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in two ways:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in warm water only, or you boil in hot water squill and cypress and saffron, and rub the intestine until the swelling is gone
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And at no time make this wine restraining, and it is better to have only for drawing out swelling. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestines with hot or lukewarm water, for by this is opened up the entry to little things; 
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small cut in the wound with an instrument used to cut hemorrhoids
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is better than cutting, that no one should cut except in great necessity nor if there is not.  
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	And these are the instruments for splitting it: 
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	If you cut inside the curve and remove nothing, and see this form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines protrude, if you return them to their natural form in their proper place, if you have the power, for this is worth more.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part below the belly, it behoves you to have the patient lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head; 
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the part below the belly, then put the head and breast higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture from the belly is in one of the two parts, then put your mind to this that the injured part be higher than the other. 
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in large and small wounds.  
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	In small wounds put what appears to you, then have between your hands one who has all the rupture in his hand, and bring together the lips; 
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common way of stitching, and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound a finger's space, and put in a needle where there is a good strong thread;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the sinew, which is under the skin inside, so that you make it pierce from that part, and bring together the two edges of the sinew and the four together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then strain a doubled thread onto the needle in two parts, then bring together the two sides of the wound evenly, and then leave one finger's breadth of space, and insert another needle. 
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then tie on the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to how many needles you need, until the whole wound is restrained. 
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And let the needles be medium-sized, between thin and thick, for thin needles pierce all the flesh, and those too thick cannot enter well.  
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	Therefore it is fitting that they should be medium-sized. 
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	And it is not fitting to drive the needles too far beyond the flesh and leather so that they pierce and open the wound before the suture. 
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	And then bind the sides of the needles so that they do not bother the patient while sleeping, and put bandages or cloths on the sides of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed. 
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	And this manner of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it requires only one needle or two. 
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second suture is common, and it consists of bringing together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the sinew together on one needle with a strong medium thread.  
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	And when you have pierced all four edges together, pull the needle back to where you started, in the manner that one sews clothes. 
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	And leave a space between each stitch the thickness of two grains of barley. 
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This suture heals a man well and I sewed up a wound on a man's stomach or belly, which was cut by a knife and the wound was more than a handspan in size, and the intestines protruded for two handspans, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I put the intestine back in after it had been out for 24 hours and the wound healed up to 15 days, and I treated it, and it was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And those who saw him thought he would die, and it was a miracle. 
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	And I did not treat him with any ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine.  
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And I put nothing more on the wound than old cotton twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Here I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:  
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and thread it from the outer part to the inner.   
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	When it has pierced the center straight through, take the thread from the tip of the needle, and make it pierce from the inner part to the outer.  
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	The understanding of this stitching is that you sew just as furriers do with furs, and you leave the thread once on one side, and take it up again on the other, until the stitching is all complete.   
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second way of sewing, which Galien properly calls, is as some do, who join the two parts together naturally, and apply one of the heads of the suture to the other head, in this manner: 
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Insert a needle or the head of the silk thread nearby, and make it pierce that place only, and leave the two heads of the suture; 
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside part to that inside one, along with the two heads of the suture; 
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then make one and the other pierce from the outside part to that inside one, in two other heads of silk thread that are on the other side; 
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the gentler way of sewing and the most common. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galien said these words, and some testify to it, that one must sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each; 
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one must put one needle from one side, and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew straps. 
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more grievous than those in other places of the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, so that the fire has not moved it, then put the intestines back in place, and the seam.  
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	Then put charred charcoal powder on top, and if the fire has moved it, put any ointment that is present on it, until the wound swells. 
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	And stitch the thread, and let the sinews and the muscles be joined.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed. 
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you have no medicines, put on it as soon as it begins to boil over old cotton, and stir it twice a day until it is healed 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need other medicine for several positions unless the wounds are simple 
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound will cause commonality with the principal members, it is fitting that you moisten linen lightly in tempered oil, or in rose oil, and place it around the wounds, and under the armpits; 
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if he feels pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which often happens, then enemas of warm red wine, and likewise if the putrefaction comes up to the intestines; 
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is due to the fineness of the veins that are there, and the subtlety of the whole body, and its resemblance in nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the splinter jumps from the wound, put it back as you would the intestines, while it is fresh. 
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	And if it is old and has become green or black, you must bind the place that is black so that blood does not flow into it, for there are veins and arteries. 
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	Then cut what is between the ligature, and place the two ends hanging down from the part below the wound until it loosens for easier extraction when the splinter comes out, and the wound gapes. 
de la routure dou boueil	from the breaking of the eye
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are round, and the wound is small, some men can restore it, for I have seen a man who was wounded in the belly by a spear. 
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	And the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and from it issued excrement and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I have put it to care according to what I could, and did not cease to refine until it was healed, and the wounds joined. 
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it joined, I doubted that the patient might have pain in his belly. 
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	And he had no pain, but remained in better condition, and ate and drank;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in a certain way: 
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	Take bristles at large heads, then bring the lips of the wound together, and when the bristles have opened their mouth, put them on the two lips so that they squeeze their mouths shut;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then he cuts off the head, and this remains so that it cannot be untied, then put another bristle afterward in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed;  
et cout la plaie.	And sew the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If those hairs burn in the intestine and cause no harm to the patient, one can tie the intestine with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way: 
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the head of this intestine thread that is well stripped and then tie to the head of this thread a fine linen thread twisted together. Then thread it through a needle and sew the intestine, and smooth it at the break.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	And this manner of sewing is only according to the way of trust and hope. 
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestinal folds, there is nothing but subtlety. 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it grows old, is called universally "fistula," and the same when it is healed and bows inward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to its greenness, a hard and white knot where there is no pain, and it is also raised like the feather of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	And sometimes the bowel is clear and sometimes thick 
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	Sometimes spotted, and sometimes enough; 
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	And as I have spoken of it in the section on wounds, any wound that is not healing and there is no flesh, it is only due to one of nine causes:  
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, by the smallness of blood or flesh; 
ou por sa malice;	or its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside and on the lips, that does not allow new flesh to grow; 
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much bowel;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the veins are spoiled and the matter is of bad quality; 
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a type of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	where by its nature, digestion is slow in the region, and feeling is slow, and it swells naturally; 
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones: 
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicine in the division. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is fitting for me to make you aware of the treatment of fistula which is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula occurs in all the members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or in the bladder, or to the intestines, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; 
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the nature of the principal member, and similar things.  
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas that are in this manner are due to poor healing, and there is nothing but labor, and ignorance; 
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is a fistula that does not come to the place I have said, and you are confident of the cure and have seen it, then take a tent of linen or iron, if the fistula is straight. 
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is crooked, then use a subtle tent of lead, for the lead bends easily around the curvature. 
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well encircle it with tents, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for the moisture will travel from one opening to another and cleanse it. 
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then have it bleed freely as much as you are able, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and it is well cleansed beforehand, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it. 
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then treat it according to what I have told you, and remove the corruption and corrupted humors that are within; 
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	And then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep and straight, it is necessary that you cut deeply as much as you can, then put softened tents soaked in medicinal water, and push them up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; 
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then put ointments that promote healthy flesh, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it. 
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not trouble your principal limbs as we have said; 
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, then clean out all the corruption as much as possible, and then treat it with things that promote healing until it is healed. 
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	And if it is not healed and returns as before, know that you have not gone far enough. 
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	Expose and scrape out as much as you are at the bottom and remove all the corruption, then restore the place. 
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it is healed in this way, it is good.  
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach. 
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	There is nothing else to do but leave it to nature.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	And if there is a small corrupted bone and you can remove it with forceps, extract it with an instrument suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, treat them all and leave none behind. 
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut both moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put something promoting decay on the wound, and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then you will remove the bones more easily; 
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, only promote decay until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound; 
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part that has decayed and reaches as far as the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	you must sew and cut everything until the decay, and then treat it until it is healed; 
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take example from it and help in your work. 
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	There was a young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the materials came to the leg, and it swelled with a large abscess, and he had no reason to open it. 
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	But his doctors in their folly worked so much on it that they opened the abscess and corrupted many materials, and it became a fistula, and there came many openings that all flowed with pus and moisture from the body. 
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And many doctors treated him for two years, and there was no one skilled in the art of hands, until I was called to him, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating it, and what flowed from the openings into a large container. 
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And the young man's body was turning red, and he had a citron color. 
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I put a tent in one of those holes, and then I examined all the holes, and I found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I hastened therefore and probed into one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came as far as the bone inside. 
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw what appeared to me of the corrupted bone and thought that there was no other corruption except for that which I removed. 
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	And I began to restore the wound with hot medicines for a long time and could not solder it. 
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	And then I began again and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing into the bone, and I saw it and removed it, and I tried to solder the place.  
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	But I could not do so until I probed around a palm's length of the bone and cut it away entirely, then I restored it with medicines.  
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	And it was healed and soldered quickly, and there was no need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had of him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation often bled, but it was healed completely, and in place of the bone a hard flesh grew, and was of good disposition and had neither harm nor any contrary at all, either coming or going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any place in the body, then it must be treated in this manner: 
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take a ligature and bind it to the head of the bone that appears, and instruct someone to extend it upwards; 
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and place another ligature of wool larger than the first ligature, and tie it upon the flesh that is below the bone, and extend the head, so that you draw down the corrupted flesh, and expose the flesh on the spot where you wish to sew, so that the silk does not stain the flesh; 
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a coal or a board below the bone to move aside the corrupted flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And it is necessary to treat as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and to treat again another time. 
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and does not appear, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all the flesh. 
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then put a coal underneath, and then treat from one part to the other the corruption, and let the treatment be as long as the corruption is a finger's breadth, as we have said. 
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint and treat the bone where it contains from the other side. 
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other remedy than to cut.  
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	And if the corruption is or in a point of the hand, or or in a point of the foot, then it is very serious, but nevertheless you must inquire into that corruption, how it appears to you. 
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all ways that you can, but let the vein or nerve not oppose you. 
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And know that the incisors and saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the setting of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and smallness, and their hardness. 
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And for this reason, it is necessary to equip each kind of work with its instrument.  
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And know that the work will show you the instrument you will need, according to the knowledge of this art and the testimony of the manners of diseases. 
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	So prepare the instrument you need according to what is fitting.  
dou feu	fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder may dislocate inward or outward. 
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have medicine that corrodes it through the treatment of medicines, and it profits nothing, then it is necessary to cut that member up to the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater malice, which is worse than the loss of the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	And the signs are that the limb becomes black, as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackness, then comes the corruption of member to member, and takes hold throughout the body. 
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If it is from a bite of copper, and if it is by the sting of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar creatures, if the corruption is at the head of the toe, cauterize it, and do not give it space to come up to the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, cauterize it at the joint so that the corruption does not come up to the arm; 
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, cauterize it at the elbow;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the elbow, death is certain, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of its virtue; 
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and do the same when the gangrene comes or foot: 
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes in the first joint, then cut off the limb after the other joint; 
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then cut off the whole foot; 
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises in the leg, then cut it at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die; 
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the manner of cutting or sewing the limb is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister's ties downward, and another minister's ties upward, and you sever the flesh that is between the two ties at a spatula's width, until the bone is exposed; 
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cut or sew, and put on each side a sheet of linen, so that the sew does not touch the healthy place, and bring to the patient other wounds and abscesses. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if a flow of blood comes when you are working, quickly cauterize the area, or put on some restraining powders. 
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed. 
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	And I will tell you what happened to a man in his own foot: 
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	He had a blackening that looked like a burn from fire, and this corruption first came in the back of his foot, until it spread throughout the whole foot.  
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the man saw the corruption, he quickly covered the foot and it was healed. 
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And a long time afterward the corruption returned to the back of his hand, and he came to me, and I put things that repel on it after cleaning the body, and I could not stop the corruption.  
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And he said that I should hold his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of recovering the matter. 
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	And I also doubted that if I cut his hand, he would not die, because the strength of the man was weak. 
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And he despaired altogether and returned to his land, and hastened to hold his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I only tell this story because one might do the same thing if there is need. 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes in fleshy areas and remains so long that it forms a large collection of pus. 
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then it bursts and discharges the pus, and the wound remains open, like some vessels.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And the skin above it is as delicate as a thin cloth and does not extend down to the bone or to the nerve; such an illness is called "healthy" and is not called "fistula." 
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so elongated that it reaches the bone completely, it is called a "fistula"; 
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cook is such that you cut around that skin, and just the same when it is subtle, like a cloth; 
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not spoil because of its corruption. 
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you believe that the skin will burn, and the corruption is not completely gone, and the skin is thick like leather, then treat it with an enema like this: 
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	look to see if the breasts are large, and the bowels that come from it have a foul smell, then give an enema of Egyptian medicine which is made like this:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take alum, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put them in a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take of this according to your need, and make it with vinegar and honey, and in an enema put it into the breast, and draw out the fistula; 
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine remain for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; 
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breast is softened and the pus is removed;  
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and sometimes put in an enema of vinegar ash, when this medicine is not present, and take ashes from vine wood, and pour vinegar over it, then strain it, and use as an enema, until you know that the breast is well cleansed. 
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot tolerate it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the vinegar ash, then use an enema of vinegar and honey or add a pinch of powdered litharge. 
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	where you cleanse it with honey and mead wine, so that the honey has the property of purifying and cleansing, and the wine makes the body breathe. 
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And when you have done this and are confident that the breast is well purified, then cleanse it with something that produces flesh in it, and take a diaphoretic plaster and make it with rose oil and wine; 
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cleanse it with certain medicines and ointments, whose properties I have described or will treat in the discussion of ointments; 
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And if the opening of the breast is small and the nozzle of the clyster cannot enter, enlarge it a little with an iron instrument and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment or basil ointment until it is enlarged. 
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if the wound is too large, sew it up so that only the place where the clyster can enter remains open; and if the opening that leads to the bowels is above, sew it lower than where it is. 
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the belly is in perfect condition, do not allow flesh to grow. 
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cover the breast below as you see it, arrange it in such a way that the belly runs to the lowest place where it is; for when the belly is perfect, do not allow flesh to grow and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see it, arrange it in this way.  
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	Let the belly run slightly downward and do not leave anything of the belly. 
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	And take consolidating medicines to put over the breast, and spread them on a linen cloth that covers the whole breast.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	Then cover the sore place on the breast as forcefully as possible making the hole larger than the first, then spread ointment often on the other cloth according to the size of the hole, and put it on the sore place on the breast to align the belly, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and he who is outside the belly from the breastbone, often removes it to remove the bowels, and know what flows from the bowels, whether it's poison or pus or enough, digested, or undigested. 
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take care whether the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread halfway and you see the nature that leaps up on the breastbone, know that the breasts are already healing, and approaching health. 
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	And then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, if you change another bandage, and renew the ointment. 
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts swell with undigested food after many days, know that the breasts do not air out.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come after a long time, do not despair at all of health, for healing approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men whose wounds heal slowly, and some who do the opposite; 
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested bowels leap from the breast after many days, know that the breasts are not healing;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breasts are slow to heal and are inflamed, apply drying medicines that are moist in substance and dry in effect, such as diachylon ointment, for it contains a large portion of vitriol, and this is the last resort medicine; 
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take diachylon ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the rose of old wine equal in substance; 
puis le confit et en use;	then cook it down and use it; 
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and the same made with honey makes it thicker, when diachylon ointment is not present, or you can take myrrh and aloes and frankincense, grind them, and sprinkle the powder on the honey when it has been taken off the fire; 
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	then make it into a paste and spread it over the breast, and administer twice daily aristolochia longa and roots of orchis, which are also like flour of vetch and centaury; 
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and in the use of simples or compounds: 
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	crush them, and make a powder, and put it on the honey that I have said, and use it; 
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the sore is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment, then know that the corruption is fully embedded, and makes an impression on the bone, or hard limbs, or limbs;  
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure of the fistula, as we have said before. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	A felon is an abscess that arises under the nail of the hand or foot, or perhaps arises in other places;  
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is inflamed and no heed is paid to it, then it becomes a large abscess, running and oozing pus so much that it runs to the root of the nail, and perhaps runs all through; 
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And corruption comes to the bone, until there is a foul-smelling pain, and the flesh around it becomes wide, and the color is dark. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not profit, then it is necessary that you cut out all the superfluity which has remained from the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cauterization is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy; 
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail presses on the flesh and begins to grow in, and the sore starts, then you should put a wedge under the nail that points at the flesh, lift it up, and cut away this thin flesh subtly and lightly. Then put burning and corrosive medicines on the remaining flesh to remove it all; 
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.  
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it out and treat it forcefully, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; 
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the pain corrupting it, so that the wound is shaped like an I as mentioned before, then treat it until it is healed; 
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed and swollen, and it causes great pain, then you must first heal it; 
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the inflamed area with a sharp scalpel, slicing across it, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the inflamed area, for the patient would feel too much pain; 
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, apply something soothing on top of it.  
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain from the deafness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two nails that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is sinew where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or its birth is in some parts of us.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who are born with no pain in any part of the body do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the body may possibly move.  
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The cut of one who is fleshy should be light, in a measured way: 
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a wide scalpel. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Those who are born at the root of the joint are hard to cure. 
si te tien dou coper.	If you hold them tight.  
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For one who is born or about to be born soon, it is fitting that you first shave the flesh roundly down to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable size for this, and then heal it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The solderings that come to two bones together come by birth, or by soldering of a wound, or by burning of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is fitting that you bind that wound so that it may heal according to its natural shape. 
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place it between two soft cloths soaked in rose oil, so that it does not stick together.  
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or you may place it between two thin pieces of lead, until its flesh is healed, as it should be.  
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If soldering comes to any of his joints with the palm, then bind that soldering as it is fitting.
des vils	of old men
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large vessels filled with superfluous melancholies that come from various parts of the body. 
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And it occurs more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others.  
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary that you administer to him purging with colocynth, and then apply basil to him.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The treatment with iron is done in two ways: 
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One is to bind them and strongly draw out the black blood.  
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other way is that you lift the vein, and treat it completely strongly. 
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The incision is according to this manner: 
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First raise the leg with very hot water so much that the flesh becomes softened, then strain the leg of the patient from above the thigh to the part below the knee; 
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein in one place, or two or three, with a wide incision, then loosen and strongly treat the black blood with your hand from one side to the other, as much flesh is released as the strength of the patient can endure. 
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then tie it, and order him to abstain from meat containing black bile;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, and benefit the patient. 
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The lifting of the limb is according to this manner: 
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Place the leg of the sick person, if there is much hair, then put it in a bath and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red and swells the veins. 
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you do not have a bath, heat it by fire and then cauterize the place near the vein along the length of the knee or in the part below the ankle. 
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then cut the skin with an awl and flay the vein from each side until it appears when touched. 
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it also appears like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	Then put the tip underneath, as long as it is raised from the skin and then gently cut it with an awl and cauterize it in another place above the three toes. 
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then flay the skin above the vein until it appears, then ligate it with a ray, just as you have done, and bind it to another hook, just as you have done first. 
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then cut another incision, or several if you need them, then ligate it, and bind it to the second toe, then draw and ligate it up to the second incision. 
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then extract it from incision to incision until it comes out entirely, then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot draw and lift it, insert a needle through the whole thread doubled, tie it and draw it up, then insert it under the ray and turn your hand on one side and the other until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And be careful that it does not cut, for if it cuts, you cannot draw or lift it, and the patient will be harmed.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And when you have treated it all, put on the wound a cloth soaked in wine and rose oil. 
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And dress it until it is healed. 
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the sinew is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly but do not cut it. 
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the sinew is curved and does not cut except it cuts a vein.  
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And it is of a large curve, for if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the shape: 
de la voinne civile	from the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is embedded in the legs, in hot places where neither herbs nor trees grow, and in earth where there is no moisture. 
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And by chance it arises elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the rot that comes under the skin, as it comes into the body snakes and worms, inject between skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a very large inflammation comes in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to come out, just like the root of a plant.
