Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the shoulder is open, it is fitting that you wrap around a piece of linen from three and a half to two and a half fingers, and tie it, and leave the linen hanging on the leg, and every time it begins to come undone, wrap it again around the linen and tie it.  
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root, as long as it is all coming out. 
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and rot or pus and bad sickness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For this reason, it is fitting that it should be treated bit by bit until the end, and nothing remain in the body.  
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and there are times when this vein, when treated, is X palms long, or even more, and one man came to me whose was X palms long, and when you cut it, if it bursts into I rays or holes, and pierce it to the bottom so that everything comes out;  
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and let the matter inside be emptied, and apply to the place medicines that prevent putrefaction at any time, then treat it as you would an abscess. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes this vein has few rays, and even when it opens at the joint of the foot or the ankle, and many holes come out and it spurts rays;  
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	then treat it as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This ailment is called in our land "the ox disease," because it often occurs in oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body ascending and descending, and the man feels it well from limb to limb, as long as it runs under the skin where it goes, and jumps strongly;  
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And it is caused by putrefaction of certain humors, such as worms and serpents and lampreys or ascaris in the belly. 
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	And one doubts its wickedness, for when it goes through the body and rises to the head, and comes to the eye, it may perchance enter and destroy the eye. 
et ceu avient maintes fois.	And this happens many times. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it healing and draining, one cannot know for sure that it is gone except when it goes: 
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	Therefore it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong tight ligature, then cut above it and drain it well, and if the worm is completely embedded in the flesh and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies.  
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm that it does is that it can corrupt the eye, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or the head near the eye, remove the eyebrow below it, then cover above and treat strongly; 
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary for the patient to cleanse the body with dissolving medicines for corrupt humors, and avoid meats that cause putrefaction. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This illness is called "shaking" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then can move from limb to limb; 
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I have seen what I tell you.  
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she revealed her arm to me, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; 
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and soon after, I saw it rise as quickly as a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, like living silver when it cuts from one place to another; 
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain departs from that place, and goes into the shoulder, and then a little while after it spreads throughout the body, until it reaches the other arm. 
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then she told me that it turned back around the body, just as I saw it. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how it moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I had seen many who well believed they could move pain from one place to another, but I had not seen it myself as I did in this woman. 
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And I thought it was because the woman had a dry body and exposed veins, and that is why this constrained windiness appeared. 
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And it does not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate and have moist bodies and full veins. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see this illness being cured, and the patient feels the pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then apply a poultice above and below quickly, and then cup upon it until this constrained windiness at that place is gone. 
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the place; 
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it in your eyes, then the cure of those who expel windiness, such as foul-smelling pills, and serpent pills, and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the bodies where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of theirs is that there are some which have large points, and small ones, and hairy ones, and smooth ones; 
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some which have two angles, and those which have tongues, and those where it has parts; 
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and the one which falls in any limb falls according to two manners: 
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	where in a principal member it falls, such as brain, heart, liver, lung, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you here afterward, appear to you: 
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	So it is necessary that you are wary of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterward in many situations; 
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this bad sign does not appear to you and the arrow is not completely embedded, then treat it and care for the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	The sign of the brain when an arrow penetrates and pierces the bone, and leaps the dura mater which is on top of the brain, is when there is darkness and drowsiness and greenness and redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; 
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps it is without force from the nostrils or ears; 
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps loses speech and voice; 
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the wound there appears white moisture resembling pus, and leaps also like burning charcoal;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if these signs appear to you, take care of the treatment, and treat the arrow if it is not embedded. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of an arrow when it has lodged or entered are that it is near the left nipple, and also it feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not hollow. 
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the arrow also moves like a pulse, and in its course black blood comes forth, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting. 
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Know then without doubt that death approaches. 
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that has not been removed is that without any foam it leaps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs deeply and desires cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow has lodged in the covering of the hip, it is near the ribs; 
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and there is great groaning and great pain and sighing.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And all the limbs of the shoulders are moved. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow sticks or lodges in the stomach, it may happen that something of the undigested flesh leaps from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes the gut or stomach, and it passes through the intestines without touching any fiber, there is no hope for a cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow has lodged in the bladder, and the urine leaps forth and flows out, and the patient feels great pain: 
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Know that the wound is mortal. 
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the armpit and the spine of the back and the forearm and the thigh and the legs, and similar members, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous as I will tell you so that you may do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow fell or lodged in the root of his nose: 
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and drew it out from the other side below the fat of the ear, and it was healed without pain. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I drew out an arrow from a young man that had lodged in the fat of his eye below the eyelid, and the arrow was embedded, and one could only reach the point towards the fletching, and the arrow was large like that of a Turkish bow, all iron light without ears; 
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The young man was healed, and no bad accident befell him. 
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears:  
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I shaved the beard and worked subtly until I drew it out, and the Christian was healed. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And draw an arrow from a man who had it stuck in his belly, and thought he would die. 
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	And then after thirty days, his condition did not change.  
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow and pulled it out forcefully and there was no bad outcome. 
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man to whom an arrow has fallen in the back, and the wound is sealed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change his natural state, nor does he find any harm in any of his natural functions. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you see another man to whom an arrow has fallen in his face, and the wound is sealed over;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and it remains thus without him suffering great pain; 
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar cases. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And I drew an arrow from a man of the prince, the king, that was stuck halfway through his nose, and there was a slight slant to the right side. 
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	And the arrow was all embedded. 
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat her three days after she fell. 
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I find the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried every subtle remedy on her, and did not feel her at all; 
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and she felt numbness and pain below her right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the point of the arrow. I put an atractive and digestive plaster on the wound so that the pus would not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the pus from the arrow appeared to me. 
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I kept the plaster on for three days, and sutured the wound deeply, and kept the patient a long time until he felt the arrow one day deep within his flesh;
et il le me dist.	and he told me so. 
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put a strongly corrosive medicinal liquid on the wound for three days until it was open, and I probed it, and felt the head of the arrow lift up in its place. 
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then apply in the opening of the wound that medicine sharp, until the head of the arrow appears visibly to me; 
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and pierce well the edges around four months, and then enlarge if the wound so that I could put in the forceps, and the muscles from one side and the other, and it could not come out; 
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then I did not cease to refine and engineer various instruments until I took it one day with forceps well made, according to the form that will come at the end of this chapter, so that I could draw it out, and restore the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the wise judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn, and the patient was entirely healed. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your care on what I do not say, for the books cannot contain everything; 
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But the wise masters compare very little, and on that which is present and lacking, they find nine works, and nine instruments, for the removal of foreign things which happen in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not come out of limbs where they are stuck except according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the place where they enter, or through another part; 
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which comes out through the place where it enters is an arrow entering their flesh, and that rarely happens now. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the flesh is rotted around it, and the exit is widened. 
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for several days, and move it every day. 
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps, and if it does not jump, pierce around with a very fine instrument until the wound is enlarged, and then treat it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the accidents I have mentioned appear to the patient: 
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	Do not treat it at all, but leave it as it is until it is equal after several days, for if the arrow comes as far as theCSF  that means death. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not fixed in more than the bone alone, and does not reach as far as the sinew, and the patient remains for some days without any bad incident, then draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very deeply lodged and cannot be removed by force, then administer poultices around it as I have told you; 
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the area until it is healthy. 
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is embedded in a part of the body where it cannot be seen, then search for it all over; 
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, treat it with any suitable instrument; 
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then enlarge it until the wound is large;  
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears by which it is held, remove the flesh that is stuck in two parts as much as you can, then break or bend the ears of the arrow until you can draw it out; 
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the arrow, lest you draw it out more grievously. 
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then leave it until the surrounding flesh has rotted, then treat it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood opposes you, then apply what we have said about treating it in its chapter;  
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of cutting a nerve or vein, and place something as you can so that you can draw the arrow out without danger, whether quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; 
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and put the patient in the form he was when the arrow fell on him for it is the greatest help that there is and if you cannot then put him according to what the signs show you 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, where it appears nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in a place if one sees or feels it apparently 
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	cut therefore above as much as the forceps can grasp and then extract it 
si saut fuer maintenant.	if a jump is now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand around until it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out leave it still and then begin the extraction again as much as it comes out; 
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there were a part of the arrow  push it all the way in;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if there were a point and you see it administering thrusting, if it administers the instrument with its head so that the point of the arrow enters into the head of the instrument 
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And then put force, and if the arrow is feathered, put the instrument with a pointed end inside, to make extraction easier. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, it is fitting that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as is fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow lodges in the flesh or the belly or the bladder or the side and it is nearby and you can cut on top of it, cut. 
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And beware of cutting a vein and a nerve, and then extract it, and then stitch the wound if needed. 
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And treat it until it is healed. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps with which one treats arrows is like a bird's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways to do this:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow. 
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the end of the arrow is like the feather of a bird, for piercing at the point of the arrow, as it is shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the forceps for pushing and pulling is this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are XXXI veins from which one heals, of which there are XVI leaders, namely:  
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two temples that are after the ears, called the two "herbechs"; 
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are apparent in the two temples 
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins which are in the two corners of the eyes, which are called "aspirers" 
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is below the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the top of the nose; 
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two cords which are at the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above the lips, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are below the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm: 
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; 
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "fascia," and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; 
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilica is either on the right or left side; and the common people call it "vein of the belly"; and it is above the fossa; and it is that one from which we bleed, which opens clearly above the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the salvation vein is the vein which is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; 
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot there are three veins: 
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is below the curve of the pouch on the left side, and the second saphena which is at the ankle on the right side; 
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein which is called "nurse," which is at the ankle of the other side;  
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	Bleeding from the veins that are behind the ears helps with old catarrhs, and migraines; 
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of the bloodletting, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a coarse cloth; 
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then tighten the patient's neck with a screw, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two hanging strands from the head: 
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	where the thumb is at your own pulse, and wherever you feel the pulse below your thumb, that's where to cut in. 
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet and insert it below the vein to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire vein upwards, cut through both the skin and the vein well with two strokes, and let the blood flow out as much as you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strain and tie it, until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already said incision and cautery in the first book. 
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The cutting of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for ancient migraines, habitual and customary ophthalmia, and for the body’s watery tears. 
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the quality of the bloodletting is as I say: 
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	And it is that the patient tightens their neck, so that the two veins appear openly;  
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And they feel the thumb under your hand, and then you make a sign with the knife. 
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then lift the knife onto the vein above at your index finger, and put the lancet underneath, and lift the vein above and cut it, just as you did in the two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need. 
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then loosen the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then form a bandage, and leave it until it is healed. 
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And we have spoken of them and their treatment and extraction, which begins at the start of the book.  
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding of a vein in the forehead is worth as much as the bleeding of the cephalic for old diseases of the face, and for migraines, and for redness.  
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is such that the patient tightens their neck by twisting, as long as the vein appears; 
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called a "burin," of which here is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press down with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you see. 
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then untie the patient's neck and bind the vein until it is healed and never do the work with a wide flame.  
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	In any case, it is not right for the flames to be too strong; 
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the angle should not be skewed, because the bone is close and might break by the flames when they are subtle. 
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The vein of the two tears that are in the two eyes helps with these things, and with inflammation, and redness, and the boil in the eye, and diseases of the face; 
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their vein is such that the patient tightens his neck by twisting some cord, as before; 
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the vein, and it should be a long vein, a small cut for a single flame a wide one
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are subtle, they might break; 
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then let the blood run, as much as you need, and then tie it with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The vein that runs from the nose is good for water, and for strong thirst, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, even when it is old; 
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	And the quality of the vein is such that the patient squeezes his neck, then pulls his nose with your left hand, and takes a thin flame long, and puts it in the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well otherwise, and the blood will now begin to flow; 
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go too far into the lip, and make the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for one night, because it is quickly restored; 
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the shape of the flame: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The vein of the two temples helps with the tightness of the groin, and the beginning of measles, and many diseases, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and erysipelas; 
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of the treatment is such that the patient must pull his collar down on both sides, as we have said. 
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	And let the master be standing above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a stool, then cut the vein along its length widely, then draw out the blood temperately, or as much as is needed; 
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then do the same in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and draw out all the veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	And leave him until morning, so that the wound is healed. 
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sinews of the veins above the lips help to hold together the mouth and are corrupted by gums, fissures of the lips, and teeth and gums.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the treatment is to make the patient sit in front of you and pull down his collar as I have said. 
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn back the lip and look at the two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by their blackness and because they have small black veins around them. 
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Therefore do one and the other, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, then cut the largest of each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health below the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bleeding of the veins that are below the tongue helps after the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and for eye diseases, and for mouth diseases. 
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of the bleeder is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts their tongue, and looks underneath on each side for a black vein: 
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Bleed one and the other, and do not go too deep, for underneath are the arteries. 
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the arm from which one commonly bleeds are bled according to two manners:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	When you prick with all the flame, myrtle strong, or olive subtle as cutting trenches, and it is called "anesil"; 
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	And they are large and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame myrtle is very renowned, and it is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins raised full of thick blood evident, and that contain thick and troubled blood; 
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive flame: 
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more subtle pointed, and it is for severing small veins, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilisk, which is one of those veins, helps with illnesses that are below the throat, and on the neck, and on the chest, and on the belly; 
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the healer that he bleeds it, and that he guards himself from the artery which is below.  
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, then it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said; 
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame must not be piercing, but cutting like a knife. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilisk does not open manifestly, it is fitting that you extract it and change for another. 
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	Or if you want no vein from it, or you heal in its place the vein within the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens manifestly; 
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the cautery knife to the flame, as we have said.  
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the place of the sinew, it is fitting that you extract the arm so that you touch the place until you know the pulse; 
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place of incision, and then bind the arm, and apply the vein to the cautery knife flame.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	And be careful not to wound the artery when you see the swollen place, for it is of the artery:
eschui la donques.	Avoid that then. 
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protrude upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from an artery. 
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and put your thumb on the length of it, then remove your thumb if the blood stops flowing, which often happens. 
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	If it bleeds again, bind the arm, leave it like that, and tell the patient not to move it;  
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be on your guard, and do not move it until it is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the blood does not stop flowing and it is coming out at you, and medicine is not present to you, then grasp the artery if it appears, for the head of it retracts;
et estainche li sans.	and stop the bleeding.  
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of ivy root, and cut it, and take one of the halves and bind it on well until the next day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if his blood is staunch, it is good; 
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, he should be treated as we have said with powders that staunch blood; 
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the staunching is not hindered in several positions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the bandage on the arm. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein in the middle helps as it draws blood from above the head and below the body because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said; 
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is fitting for the phlebotomist to be careful of the nerve that is below, and if he pierces too deeply and finds the nerve, it will swell and the bleeding will be hindered, and perhaps it cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve appears many times, and if it does not appear in some men due to its subtlety, then you should draw the blood with a blunt instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And carefully excise the nerve according to your ability. 
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then make the incision long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The artery of the head helps by drawing blood from the head and helping these ones. 
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is best to bleed by cauterizing with olive oil flame or myrtle flame, for this is the safest of all veins, as there are no nerves nor arteries beneath it. 
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, it is best to seek the lightest place and do not grieve if one misses the first time, and try again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance some men's veins swell when it is missed the first time, but do not worry. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the lancing is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing that you must know about bleeding is that it is only administered to preserve health and to ward off diseases to come.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	And let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins which are as follows:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	These are known as cephalic, facial, and basilic. 
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And one should bleed at the beginning of spring in young people, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear. 
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	And bleeding should be done on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day. 
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	Bleeding administered for illnesses has no set time, but is done when needed, day or night, at all hours and in all times. 
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not fitting to bleed children until fourteen years old, nor women carrying a child from the fourth month until the seventh. 
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Old men who have passed sixty years should not be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wishes to be bled, in any manner, it is fitting that they cleanse their bowels with a mild clyster if they have retained much phlegm so that the veins do not draw harmful impurities from the intestines to the principal members. 
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Nor does he who is too full of meat heal well, nor he who is drunk until he is overcome, nor those with dropsy. 
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And he worsens from sickness after colic attacks, vomiting, discharge of the bowels, and multiplication of childbirth for women, and from labor, staying awake, and fasting, and from whatever drains strength, whether by weapon or by the body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then subtly thin the humors if they are too thick, by meats and drinks and by medicines if you have the skill. 
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then bathe him if nothing forbids it, to thin the blood, and bleed from a vein near the wrist on the third day as we have said. 
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And keep him from work, exertion, and lust, and similar things that day.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And be careful and joyful, and let the tourniquet be higher than the one being bled, and rub his arm two or three times, then tighten the bandage moderately for the blood will not run if it is too tight or loose. 
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt. 
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then moisten the linen with a drop of old oil, then place your left-hand thumb on that vein below the place where you want to bleed, so that the vein does not escape and fail when cut. 
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee as swiftly as cords upon linen, and if one has such veins full of windiness, so that when the flame is placed upon it, it shrinks from the flame and cannot open the vein, then one is among these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if he opens the vein, but the wound is too narrow, for this reason it is necessary that the linen-handler be knowledgeable in these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If not, start again a little lower than that place or higher if the limb is not swollen. 
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen and the patient is afraid, leave it for one or two days and do not bind the arm. 
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	Perhaps some boils will form. 
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Do not bathe afterwards and then begin the setting again if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the puncture is small, or you cut the sinew subtly and doubt that as much blood as you see will not come out, then pierce in that puncture itself all the way through. 
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	And work quickly so that the limb is swollen.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	For this often happens when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, do not begin the setting again and put a bit of linseed oil on it, because it draws the blood from the body and is gentler in that place than the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer a ligature of oil into each vein that you open, to staunch the flow of blood. 
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	And this same thing does act as a tourniquet and bandage when applied.  
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If it is too thin, the blood will seep through; if it is too thick, it will impede circulation. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there develops a large abscess, which often happens even when the vein has only been opened a few times, or when the opening of the vein is small, if you hurry and apply a moistened sponge in warm water and salt to the area for an hour; 
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary to do this after the blood has flowed from the vein, and if it remains in place for a few days without any blackness or greenness, it will not harm him.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see it, put some aloe or myrrh mixed with calamint juice, monsterwort, or something similar. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often abscesses and appearances occur at the site of the basilic vein:  
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	So put your hand on it, and if you find the area soft when pressed by your hand, then that appearance is bad. 
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Therefore beware that you do not put any of what we have said on it, for fear of cutting an artery; 
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but apply a dry plaster to harden the area, then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.  
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it is red; 
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it thick, let it flow out until it is thinned;  
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down. 
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is fitting for one who is ill and strong, and needs bloodletting, that they be made a wider wound, and the incision be wide. 
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for one who is weak, do the opposite, and they should be bled little and often, and one should bleed them by cutting across, not by pricking. 
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of bleeding saves from the running of blood and the cutting of nerves, and is worth more than bleeding that is long or wide. 
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for one whose body lacks for bloodletting, it is fitting to give them softened bread in pomegranate juice;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	if they are feverish, bleed them three or four times; and if they are of cold complexion, give them before the bleeding softened bread in thick syrup, or in honey syrup flavored with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chicory, and a fragrant syrup.  
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after the issuing of much blood, it is fitting that he inhale broth of flesh and subtle aromatic syrup, and use other things as we have said in the division or chapter on syncope for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to increase his arm strength, and bleed again, it is fitting that when it is weakened by a great bloodletting, that he bleeds a little at a time, according to the amount of his continuing strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to drain his arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong flesh, then bleed him seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to heal from another location, it must be healed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For it has much blood within the body which is already heated, and brings fever; 
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	so it is necessary to draw a great quantity, and widen the opening as much as it will allow. 
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	Then when you have observed all the conditions of health, and place your hand upon his pulse while he is recovering, so that death does not come instead of recovery, for this happens many times when the healer is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not fitting when you see the arm loosen and make blood come out a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly upon it. 
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it is bent, let him straighten his arm quickly, for this would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but leave it until it recovers a second time; 
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or apply the point of a flame, as long as the blood which is frozen at the opening of the vein comes out freely, and put upon it a piece of linen moistened in vinegar, and press lightly upon it.  
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, then do so in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein under the arm is cut near the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of the cautery is such that the patient plunges their hand into hot water, until the wrist is red; 
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then it is loosely bandaged, so that the vein appears well, then the cautery is now applied crosswise, not wide nor long; 
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And the opening should be wide, and it should be cauterized very close to the joint of the hand, and if none can escape, then put the hand back into hot water, and let the blood run into the water, until you have enough; 
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is summer, do not put the hand back into hot water, for it is put in more in winter than in summer; 
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the cautery of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the salvation of the right hand is worth for all liver diseases, and this is the manner: 
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand, and put it in hot water, so much that the vein swells, if you see it. 
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the vein is sideways, and if you cut it all around, it does not hurt anything.  
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	And do not go too deep, because the nerves are underneath all naked of flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot come out. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as needed, put oil and silk on the vein to heal quickly, and do the same for every vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein in the left hand is worth as much for the disease of the mouse, and do everything just as I told you on the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The cautery of the sophene is worth against all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of fluids, and disease of the reins, and of the thighs and legs old, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of this vein is that the sick person puts their bare foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it breaks, and ties above the joint of the foot. 
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there go many veins.  
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Heal then the bone or larger sinew, or at the ankle, that moves worthily. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you heal it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are underneath, and heal it by passing through as in cutting. 
et soit li flaimes anesil.	And let the flame be numbed. 
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, put the foot in hot water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the healing fails the first time, start the second time a little higher up, for the flesh is salty. 
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt about the nerve as we have said, and do the same to the sophene of the other foot equally.  
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle strong, and its bleeding is worth the pain of the hip, when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of this healing is that the patient enters a bath and squeezes above the ankle four times by twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open. 
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it opens, heal it in all ways that you can, and by crossing.  
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is worth noting that you must copy it, for the flesh is safe, and it is very full of hands. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then any vein that appears or back of the foot, and towards the small toe, and beware of the nerves; 
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and let as much blood flow as you see, and then untie the ligature, and put cotton on top and remove it; 
ele est maintenant sanee.	It is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	of cups of cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or of glass, or of wood; 
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And cupping is done in two ways: 
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cupping that is done without cutting is according to two methods: 
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is with fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	And bloodletting, which is done by striking and extracting blood, is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is all over the head. 
et li autres est emmi le col;	And the others are along the neck; 
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others on both sides of the neck; 
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the cupping glass below the chin; 
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the cupping glasses on both shoulders; 
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping glass above the buttocks;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the cupping glasses along both arms;  
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the cupping glasses on both legs; 
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the cupping glasses on both ankles; 
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and bloodletting does not draw any blood, except for a few small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it weakens no one, as one does when drawing blood from a vein. 
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it is not fitting that it should be administered, neither with all fire nor without fire, in any illness which comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of illnesses it is fitting to cup, or for customs, we shall administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every time. 
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are some who, when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And there are some who find repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darkness as well.  
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And there are some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and spit blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are some who think, and see by night blood and wounds and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is less than a month old, we order him to be cupped after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The sinew of the thigh helps in the treatment of the head wound ... that comes to it, and it is not right that this be done after the evacuation of all the body. 
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And this cupping is in place of the sinew of the cephalic, and it is not right that those who are of cold complexion use it, or who have diarrhea, for it does them great harm. 
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And therefore it is not right that the elderly use it, nor those who have or head colds.  
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal themselves often become stiff, and for this reason it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the doubt of stiffness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	Cupping on the neck is in place of the sinew of the head and the basilica, and therefore it is good for the constriction of the breast, and for the fissure of the canal of the lung, and for all, and for repletion.  
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to push a little, for if it holds too tightly, it will cause obstruction or blockage in the stomach and heart. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	Cupping applied to the two ribs near the neck is good for headaches, ophthalmia, migraine, strangulation, and pain in the roots of teeth, and it is placed where the basil vein is located; 
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and you must instruct the patient to hold their hand while applying it, so that they do not press on an artery and cause blood to flow. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	Cupping below the chin is good for mouth diseases, gum disease, and similar ailments that occur in the mouth; 
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is placed where the veins of the two lips are located. 
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Cupping of the shoulders is good for illnesses that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	Cupping on the elbows is as effective as three veins in the arm, because it draws blood from those large veins; 
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the patient not to thrust too deeply, for the flesh is thin of skin, and beneath are nerves and arteries. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping glass that is on the buttock is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for illnesses below, and it should be large, and made of horn, so that it can draw well. 
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if it were thin, it would break;  
et i fai grans plaies.	and it would make large wounds. 
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	Cupping glasses on the legs draw abundantly, for they pull blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the limbs, and of the bladder, and soften swellings. 
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are placed at the two thighs, and the two ankles, and nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and cause emaciation in many constitutions. 
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply a cupping glass is such that you put it first empty, and suck moderately, and place it quickly, and move it equally, and do not cease doing this, until you see the place red and swollen, and appear the redness of blood. 
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then take it off, and put the cupping glasses back on, and be careful in the disposition of bodies, for there are some who have thick flesh, and clear pores. 
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	If it is fitting to strike only once, and it is fitting to make wide wounds, and a deep prick. 
et suce legierement.	And suck lightly.  
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the flesh is thick, it is fitting to strike twice. 
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to make subtle the way of thick blood.
