Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the flesh is very thick, it is fitting to strike a third time. 
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we want to draw out blood little by little, we should only prick once. 
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want a lot of blood, we should start again often. 
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the blood is thick, pierce deeply enough so that the points are felt and the ends should be such that the hearts are pierced only a little, and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have few pores, that you anoint the place of the cupping glass with stimulating and dissolving oil: 
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is summer, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;  
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is winter, use watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one. 
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, then take oil of marjoram, or balsam, or oil of anise, and such like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one whom one is treating has tender flesh and large pores, it does not suit to put any oil on, but it must be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture should rise with bay leaf, or myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have excess weight should rise with old wine, or vinegar water, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar ones.  
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And it is not advisable to apply a cupping glass before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two. 
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And do not sleep after cupping, and it is fitting that he wash himself, when he is about to be cupped and when he has been cupped. 
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are being treated who are choleric, and if the flesh is too painful and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	it is fitting that they take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce in season, and similar things; 
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat little, and meat from castrated animals, and moist meats.  
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion, let them take syrup of honey and moderately spiced wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat little and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day he will purge himself, he should drink more than eat; 
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is advisable to give some men three anise seeds or musk before the purging, or after, to strengthen the main limbs; 
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the wine be subtle, but it should not be drunk by those who are hot.  
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	Cupping glasses that are placed without cutting are those placed on the liver, and on the mice, and gout, and on the belly, the buttock, the kidneys, and the hip bone, because these limbs do not suffer from being cut, and we only do it to draw blood from one limb to another, as we put them on the breasts when they bleed. 
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we put cupping glasses on the belly and on the buttock to weaken the limb. 
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is an obstruction or stone, it removes by its attractive virtue perchance the obstruction, or dislodges the stone from its place. 
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and it does so likewise when placed on the liver and on the breast when there is retained windiness, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only. 
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of hot water, as in pleurisy diseases, and in this manner one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs suitable for this have been boiled. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	It should be two handbreadths wide and half a palm long, and it has a small hole near the middle, as for putting in a needle, and it is made of horn, smooth in front so that it does not hurt the patient when put on the limb. 
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and have in the middle a rod of ash or iron, to put a chain on it, and they are large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them. 
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For children's cupping glasses are different from those of old people, and those of thin people are different from those of fat people. 
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must thus put this cupping glass upon the limb: 
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Take the chain of wax or linen, and put it through the cupping glass via the rod which is in the cupping glass, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the cupping glass so that it does not burn the patient; 
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then put it on the limb, and your hands must be over the opening that we have mentioned, so that when you want to, the vapor goes out, and one removes the cupping glass. 
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the bandage as before, and often start again, if you need to. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass which is administered for pleurisy, and sharp pain, it has neither stem nor hole, and is not administered except when full of water, and is placed upon the member only; 
et c’est li forme:	and this is its form:  
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Cupping glasses are administered only in members where one cannot put cupping glasses because of their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places; 
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on those devoid of flesh, such as bone or veins, and others similar; 
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the quality of the user is that when you find cupping glasses which are in sweet, clear water without putrefaction, then take them;  
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them for a night in sweet water, until they are familiar and have nothing in their bellies; 
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then let it be bled by vein and cupping, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on bandages. 
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are full and have shrunk, if it is a place where one can put a cupping glass, then put it on, for that is worth much afterward. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the place a little, and then sharply, very well, and then press it out.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the bandages are too tight after the body of the bandages, then wet a linen cloth in cold water and put it on top, until the bandage is softened. 
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if there are many bandages, then put crushed vitriol or alum and similar things on top until it is softened. 
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or you can put half of peeled beans on the place and leave them there until they burn at the spot so that it stops now. 
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other ones. 
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the lancets do not want to be taken, rub the place with fresh blood, or stick a needle there until the blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will burn. 
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are falling, sprinkle powder on a piece of aloe and salt mashed up, or ashes, then they will come off now. 
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know ye, son of thread, that the things we are telling in this chapter were never seen by anyone in old books, nor read in any letter.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, the science is strange in our land, for I never found anyone good at it. 
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I do not know anything else, except through the science of the old books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life. 
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in these two previous chapters. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary therefore that we say or prologue of this book the sums of speech and the chapters where wise men put their understanding, and remain upon virtue, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is fitting that you hasten to heal the sick person on one side and the other, unless something prevents you, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age; 
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the weather is very bad, or too cold; 
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and eat cold meats, that is to say, cold dishes, and broth of fowl and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty broths, and do not fill yourself too much with meats which fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess, nor spreading of matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient returns to his first government which he has used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is fitting that one nourishes the patient with meats that promote fattening, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in broth, rice, and pies, and cow's udder, eggs, fresh fish, and red wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For indeed without nourishment muscles are replenished more quickly than a fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of the old and infirm cannot be well set or fused according to their nature because of the dryness of the members, nor can those which are too tender, such as the bones of small children. 
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	But have no fear, set the broken bone with large splints that hold and join the limb together, as much as you can strengthen it as it was before. 
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And do not delay his work, and for this reason he must be fed large meats, as we have said.  
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a skull fracture is different than a fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manners of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes to the bone, and another by sharpening, as the point of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture at all a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in every manner, let him have his engine and his proper instrument in restoration, according to what his memory comes back to its place. 
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And a broken bone is known because the flesh is twisted and clearly visible from afar, and it sounds when pressed by the hand. 
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no crookedness or sound upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture. 
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it may well have crookedness, or a crack, or a small fracture. 
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not fitting that you move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come afterwards, and then extract it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture which goes awry, and whose two parts are separated, it is necessary now to put them back together equally, just as abscesses come to life. 
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if a hot abscess comes, leave it alone for a few days until the abscess is calmed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	Then put it back together gently and wisely, and know that the restoration of it is lighter than the restorations of those where there are pieces. 
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then remove it, as it should be done afterwards. 
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the broken bone is in two parts, whether it's a hand or foot, or a small limb, or two strings, or one string and a hand. 
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And place the limb according to its natural form, so that when the broken parts of the limb are freed, you reset them by all means possible into their places as you can, and be careful that your work does not cause the patient injury or pain. 
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And adjust well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms. 
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: 
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If it is set beautifully, and do not constrain it too much, nor press as those who by their work cause abscesses, heat and contraction in the limb, as we have often seen. 
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is set properly, admonish the patient well that he does not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and guard well that the limbs are so secured that he does not feel any pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, unless it is slight, and it is necessary to put him in a position where he feels no pain. 
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And be careful that he is placed straight, so that twisting does not occur when he is restored.  
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and largeness and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and hands and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	it is necessary to wrap them in soft and delicate linen cloths. 
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	And those that are large, such as thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and strong bandage, for wide bandages embrace the whole large limb and restrain it equally on all sides, so that there is no dislocation. 
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then bind it with light bandages, three or four turns depending on the limb, and pull your hand away a little from all the binding, then go above the fracture and pull less, so that the fracture can move away a little. 
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And loosen the bandage little by little until you grasp a large part of the healthy area, then take the other bandage and wind it back over the fractured area. 
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then go back to the part below the fracture and pull it moderately, not too hard nor too gently, as we said in the first lesson above. 
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place linen cloths or rags between the bandages so that they are all equal, and then bind everything over with bandages, and then apply your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put on something soothing that heats the abscess and removes the swelling, and leave it like that for several days; 
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then stretch them on your steles, and they should be half the width of a reed, or wood from which clefts are made, or palm fronds, and they should be according to this figure: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the stele which is placed on the fracture be a little larger and wider than the others; 
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And it should also be as long as is fitting for the limb, whether small or large; 
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then stretch them on the steles as you did in the first instance, then tie a thread tightly over them, as in the first instance over the fracture; 
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	Tighter above, looser below. 
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is fitting that the threads be moderate, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen; 
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their ligatures with twisted linen cords, and this is a great error, because the ligature cannot be even if it is too fine, and it is not fitting that there be less than two fingerbreadths of space between each stitch. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sore from the heads of the bones after being bound in their bandages, then place under them cloths of flax, or scraps of wool, so that they do not bruise.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the heart is broken, I will say the cure hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not right to set all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, it is not fitting to place stitches closer than after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your judgment of the heat and swelling that arises from the abscess; 
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and see here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsion:  
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg yolks, and make this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, and use it; this is the common way of making a plaster that restores fractures in many positions, and for women and small children as well, because it is neither too hot nor too cold. 
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another way of plaster to restore a fracture and a dislocation and a twist. 
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take three drams of saffron and of leadwort and of euphrasy and of asafetida and of gum arabic and of frankincense, each one. 
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Myrrh and aloe, each five drams. 
alechil VIIII З.;	Elecampane nine drams.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	And make powder of them, and mix them with the white of an egg.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the complexion of the man is hot, then use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth more than many men. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another way of plaster that is good for a twist: 
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take frankincense and mallow, each ten drams. 
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Myrrh and aloe, each nine drams.  
acaice VI З.;	Here is the sixth chapter. 
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Boil Armenian bole X, and grind it well, and mix with sharp vinegar or plenty of egg white, and administer it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way to make a plaster for joints and bones that have been torn from their places, and soothes the pain arising, and the size breaks down the bone, and the fracture. 
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take new wool, and soak it in lye and boiled oil, and put it on the place.  
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for calming a hot abscess and properly removes pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to make a plaster that restores broken bones: 
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and terrestrial poppy leaves, and grind together, and make a plaster. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to plaster for the restoration of a bone fracture and for softening the discharge of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take mallow root, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, of each one part; 
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	And grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander vinegar, or vinegar, and use it.  
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner of plaster stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of marshmallow, and seed of flax, balm, melilot, and sanicle, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all an equal part; 
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	And grind them, and boil with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb to restore it except cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else besides, and he says that it should be between hard and soft.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says that one must put on the broken limb, to restore it, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way of plaster that is worth for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take mugwort and horsehair stripped, or feathers of birds, and marshmallow, and weigh them equally, and grind them, and make plaster and bind it.  
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then untie it a little while after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor that the bone has moved from its place; 
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if not untie it by hand for several days. 
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, lack of rest or swelling, then hurry and untie it, and remove the plaster now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and dip it in water, and lift it up to the place, until the itching stops, and the pain is eased. 
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry linen soaked in water or rose oil on it, and bind it with a bandage, until you are sure of a hot abscess. 
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and reduce the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then begin a delicate binding again, and apply a plaster, and do not bind it as tightly as before.  
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And gently continue until it is healed. 
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess boils and reddens and has pain and swelling are gone completely, and you need plaster and bandage, if it starts again, as you did first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing comes to the limb of what we have said, do not untie it for more than three days or four or five or seven.  
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And never leave it for twenty days, according to what we see, until the fracture heals and approaches the adjustment of the flesh upon it.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then restrain it more than at first, and thicken its flesh, as I have said before; 
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the place drying out more than is needed, know that nourishment cannot come there; 
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	raise then a poultice of hot water, every time you loosen it, and this should be done every third day, and leave one spot dry.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	through this work then nourish the limb, and quickly amend that which the foolish mirror does, which leaves the limb twisted: 
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it is bad, and if it is work that frightens, I do not see anything else but to leave it and work straight. 
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of fractures, and various shapes, and the causes are destined; 
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures that are made by the impact of a sword, and the neck breaks all the bone down to the sinew that is below the bone, as a hatchet or axe does;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason this manner of fracture is called "haichure". 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Where the sword cuts the bone above without piercing, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute.
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And the wound of these two fractures is large or small. 
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded percussion, or fissure, or chips of stone, or falling onto stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture that reaches the membrane below the bone, or above it, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound that is joined to the bone is as subtle as a hair and the fissure is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary." 
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound is made by a blow of stone or by falling or by something similar and drives the piece of bone inward, and the bones are close together like when smiths hammer on anvils 
si entre li piere dedens.	if the stone enters inside 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to those who have or heads with wet bones, such as children's heads.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it happens in all these ways of fracture that small pieces are detached, like splinters. 
et je em parlerai en son leu.	And I will speak about them in their place. 
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the traction on them, and the inquisition with probing, and by the corrupted flesh which is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	Similar hairiness is known by this, that when one has uncovered the bone, and rubs quickly upon it, if it appears black breakage.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, take care of the patient’s accidents, and if you see any evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, and emission of understanding, and stretching, and trembling, and fever ague, and the eyes coming out and reddening, and other similar things in several dispositions, then it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a hopeless situation, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the navel cord first comes to you, and it is winter, then it is fitting to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the latest that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the cloth under the bone is corrupted, and the accidents come that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary that you split open the fractured part thus: 
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and take the head of the patient gently, and uncover upon the bone in all the ways that you can, and upon the shape of the wound more often than you can, and if discharge of blood comes to uncovering the bone, or abscess rises, help him with what is necessary, and fill the place with cloths softened in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the abscesses that rise are appeased, and be sure of the discharge of blood; 
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then begin by taking out the bone around it, and this is done according to two working methods: 
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One method is if you cut a narrow opening in front, and this is the form: 
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he inserts another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is if you have several cuts of different sizes, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed and made of tempered iron;  
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and in operation lightly so that you do not bruise the head. 
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is fitting that you pierce around it, so that you administer cuts with augers, taking care that they do not pierce beyond the bone into the flesh, and it must have above the point a flange or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you must have several of them, so that each one comes in its place according to the type of bone, so that you have augers for all flesh;  
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and these are the three forms of cauteries: 
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing through broken bone is that you put the cautery on the bone and turn it back and forth until you know the bone is pierced; 
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then put the cautery elsewhere a little after, and thus do all around, then cut with a knife the space of bone that is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments you have such as tongs, pincers; 
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and be careful not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.  
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone and drawn it out, it is necessary that you use an instrument that remains from the bone for all other instruments similar to a knife, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other knife; 
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if any small bones or scales remain, remove them lightly with instruments. 
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with bandages and dressings as we have described. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another way of working is that which Galien describes, which is safer. 
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and he praises it highly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will put underneath the head of this lenticular scalpel, of which this is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, but divide the part in two directions, so that the incision is towards the bone. 
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then strike with a small mallet on top, so that you gently chip away the bone all around, and be very careful of the cloth underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is attached to the bone, remove the bone lightly, for one can remove it well without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not extend to the cloth, and the bone is cut only on the surface, and there are small pieces, then you must file down that roughness and remove the scales with a subtle razor which you should have in various quantities, so as to administer the most suitable one in each place, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you shave before large razors, and afterwards with more subtle ones, and do not cease doing so until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other fine cuttings and subtle fractures, you must treat according to its location.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and it is something that is not answered to one who has put his study into this art 
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is uncovered, it is fitting that you take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it upon the wound 
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it upon the first cloth; 
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as lightly as you can so that you do not burden the wound, then administer another bandage over it, and do not bind it too tightly just so that it holds the wound only 
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it like this for one or two days, until the abscess is calmed, then unbind it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, vetch flour, frankincense powder, birthwort, and similar things 
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and of these things make powder, and put on the wound, and administer immediately worldly medicines without biting; 
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and be careful that the wound is immediately clean, so that you do not leave any ointment there, nor allow any pus to gather, for when pus gathers on the cloth of the brain, it runs and spreads, and causes great harm to the patient; 
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one puts a mordant thing on the sore, it irritates above it. 
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if any bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not come except for the medicine that one has put on it, so that it has some virtue, then it is fitting that you take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and in glue one drape, and put it on the sore; 
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure in ways that are fitting, until it is healed.  
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes both parts of the nose above are broken, or one by itself, for there are two bones; 
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and that below is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it is forced to bend or twist, and then heals. 
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you insert your little finger or thumb into the nostril and place the broken part inside your index finger, and push it through a pouch, until the nose returns to its natural shape. 
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.  
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the knee, and the bone cannot come back into place, then you must put it equal to the head of a nail with a large hole.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, you must do it otherwise, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; 
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling has subsided, then insert at the top of the nose strips of linen cloth, if the break is in one part. 
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	If you put pressure on it from another side, if there is a fracture. 
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	And the tendons are so thick that they fill the holes of the nose. 
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some healers say one should soften the bandages with butter and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem right to me, but it is necessary that they be softened in a mixture of egg yolk and mill dust; 
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the tendon, as long as the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.  
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes goose feathers are put in place of the tendons, and if it is wrapped with linen cloth, and it holds the fracture together, and breathes for the patient. 
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Or do what you see fit. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to a head while you are working on it, put cerate or moistened cotton in rose oil, or in a drop of diascordium.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if boils do not come, apply a plaster made from sesame flour and frankincense powder mixed with egg yolk, then put light cloths on top and do not tie the nose. 
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the fracture of the bone is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract them with suitable instruments, then sew up the wound, and treat things that promote healing, and join together, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this. 
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the bone, then treat it with bandages, and put splints of plank, until it is healed. 
de la routure de la mandibule	of the breaking of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is knocked down below, and there is no wound showing, and the break is only outward, and it is not broken in two but merely pushed in, so a knowledgeable person can tell easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, that you put your index finger in the patient's mouth; 
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is in the left jawbone, then put your index finger of your right hand and gently push the fracture inward, and adjust it with your other hand by force, and make it equal. 
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is broken in two, it is necessary that you administer extension in two parts, so that it be equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the movement of teeth occurs, or a break, then bind them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put cerate on the broken jawbone and put a double bandage on it. 
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And put on the cloth a large star well-made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width according to the jawbone, and tie it up on the cheekbones that you can reach, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light meats. 
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the shape changes, untie it on the third day, and then put back what has been changed. 
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And apply plaster on it, made from powder from the mill with plenty of egg or rye flour, after you have removed the wax. 
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And put light wool on top of the plaster, and if the plasters dry out and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times it is healed in three weeks. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, treat it as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, see if any piece of bone has been removed. 
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If subtle of the bone to remove suitable instruments. 
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, if the wound is large, sew it, and put suitable plasters on it, to promote flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the strong one
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The collarbone breaks several times forward, towards the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways:  
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	Where it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; 
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Or there is a fracture with a wound.  
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the works are so when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the collarbone is broken; 
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the side;  
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Then put the fracture equal to your two hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor indentation.  
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend more, place under the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, and make it large according to your need;  
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and extend and lift the force, and extract the spear with your hand, so that you put the fracture equal, as it should be. 
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the humerus out backward because it is embedded deep, then it befits that the patient lies often on his back, and put under the shoulder a half pillow, and push the ministers the shoulder down, so much as the bone of the humerus is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then straighten the fracture to your liking, and if you find it shattered, it is necessary that you split it up; 
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and treat the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join because of any swelling, cut it with one of the incisors that you have; 
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but put this instrument under the splint to keep the fracture in place.  
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it resembles a spoon and is not notched, and it should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; 
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it has two heads, as you see, one wide and the other narrow, according to the shape of the wound that you have made when treating the bones.  
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure of the hot abscess, if it burns the wound, and the rupture is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, apply the wound with cloths and bandages, according to its quantity. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if boils come, moisten a cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The setting of the bone, when it is without wounds and without incision, is that you put on the bone a plaster of flour from the mill and egg yolk, and put light wadding on top, and put a splint under the armpit, if you need it; 
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very large bandage a palm wide, then put two cloths on top of the wadding and the plaster; 
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a thin splint three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the ends of the bandage hang down; 
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And put the splint on the fracture, and turn the bandage up the neck, and under the healthy armpit, and under the sick armpit;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and the resetting of each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the bone fragment does not move on the broken bone, then reward it each day, and when the ligaments are slack, then loosen the restraint; 
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie on his back, and put under his armpit when he sleeps a small pillow, to lift the shoulder up; 
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	then the fracture will be relieved of its weight by the elevation of the shoulder, or you tie his arm to his neck, and do not untie it until twenty days have passed so that no bad accident occurs; 
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then begin the plaster again if you see he needs it, and remove it and leave it like this until it is restored; 
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored at most in twenty-eight days, and less for some men. 
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It sometimes happens that the shoulder breaks or is dislocated out of place, and it is not healed except by touch. 
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	If you fit the apparatus according to the shape of the break and reset it according to its natural form in all the ways that you can.  
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then put on the place powder from the mill with plenty of egg whites and light bandages, and put a double cloth over it. 
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then put a wide and thin splint on it, a bit wider than the shoulder, and if below the splint any hair is found in any place of the shoulder, use linen bandages so that the splint lies evenly. 
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then bind it all with a large bandage firmly so that the splint does not move from its place and examine the binding every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And whenever it swells, bind it again and put the splint back in place if it has moved and have the patient lie on their side. 
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or in 25. 
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is fulfilled, if it dislocates, be sure, for it is not a bone that is put back lightly. 
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out in front, and not below the heart, then do this: lift it up, set the bone, and do what we have said about the breaking of a bone to soothe a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this rarely happens;  
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the end. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken below, it descends, and the patient feels great pain, and a lack of breath, and all at once, and by chance vomits blood, and opens the hair in the broken bone, and he feels it well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back, and puts a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of the two sides with his hands, and subtly sets them equal in all the ways he can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; 
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then put on plasters and bandages over the thin layer of salt, or other light herb, and wraps it in a cloth, and ties it over the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the ligature round to the back, and remove it carefully, and observe the bandage every hour, and if it softens, remove it; 
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it becomes necessary to untie it due to corrosion or itching that occurs at the site, or pain or abscess, then hurry and untie it, scrape off the plaster, and treat what has come about in a suitable manner. 
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then soften the plaster and remove it until it is healed. 
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that a broken rib occurs only in the thick ones after the back, and chiefly inwards, and they do not break except because they are slippery; 
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and one can feel it well upon inquiry, as is due.  
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you put the break back equal, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply a plaster, and remove it with a spatula if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the rib fracture is sloping inwards, the patient feels great pain and stabbing, as in pleurisy, because the bone pierces the lining; 
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and a sharp pain, and everything vomits much blood, and it is a grievous illness, and the ancients have put great effort into it. 
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer meats that swell the belly, to push the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, that hot abscesses will come, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, so be it healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they said that one puts cupping glasses on the place to suck out the form, and it seems reasonable. 
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, there is doubt that the cupping glass does not attract superfluities to the place due to weakness.  
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should cover the place with linen soaked in hot oil, and put wads between the ribs to hold the bandage evenly, then it is cured by a cure of pleurisy, of meat and of medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot suffer because of the bone pointing through the flesh, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put an instrument under it to hold up the skin. 
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one should cut the bone, and pull lightly, and then stitch the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with poultices until it heals. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if boils come, put them on cloths softened in rose oil, and place them on the sore. 
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat while the place of this which suits a boil, and lies often on the side where it should be, until it is healed. 
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a fracture comes to the bones in the neck, and it happens that he cries;  
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also at the spine of the back. 
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know whether he will be healed or not, if you take care that if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is deadly in several positions, and if he moves them and feels well when they are removed and not strained, know that the junction of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if care is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you see whether it will heal or not, if take heed whether his limbs are softened, and whether accidents are in hands, and on the back there is windiness and discharge without wanting;  
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when he is turned on his belly, there is discharge without wanting. 
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and wants to raise himself up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is mortal:  
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if he does not labor in his treatment 
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that you warm it if there is a hot abscess, and put on the spine rose oil or egg yolk oil, until it is appeased; 
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; 
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed. 
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bones are broken, it is necessary to cover over the heart;  
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with stitches, then treat it with an anointing poultice, until it is healed; 
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the “head of the cow,” put a pouch from your left hand, and place it equal to the other hand in your power, then apply the plaster and splint on top, if you need it.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then he extracts it, and if there are broken bones, he sets them, and dresses the wound until it is healed. 
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the hip
