Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It may happen that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it does, there should be only a small reduction at the head. 
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	And setting it straight for a long time, and lowering it to its place, the patient will feel pain at the site, numbness, and swelling where the break is. 
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And for the setting, you extend your hand above it as long as you are on the break.
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	And recognize what the fracture is and its shape. 
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And if the fracture is only at the head, you set that fracture equally until it is in its natural shape.  
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it slopes inwards, make the patient lie on his stomach until the restoration of that fracture appears to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it equally, put a plaster on it. Then put a splint of wood or horn on top and immobilize the fracture so that it does not move
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And apply the place below the ribs, as long as the ligature is equal. 
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if an abscess comes, do not touch it, until the abscess is appeased, and put on what we have previously said. 
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	And then return to the restoration, and remove it as is fitting, if there is no bad accident;  
et c’est li maniere.	and this is the manner. 
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the breaking of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder joint is that which is between the elbow and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two manners. 
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	One of which is that you take a splint of moderate thickness, according to this form:  
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two ends with two ligatures, and bend them upwards, and place the patient on a seat. 
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Then the patient's arm is broken above the elbow, until it reaches the armpit, and one puts a bend in a stick, then leans on any heavy thing or a servant extends it down; 
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then put the hands together at the break so that the break returns as it should. 
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one lifts the patient onto his backside, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two assistants that one holds what is on the fracture with his hands, and the other holds below all the limb, and each extends to his part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, extract the ligature below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the assistants to their respective parts.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, you must put one tie below the armpit, and the other toward the elbow, below the break; 
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the break is towards the elbow, it is fitting to put a tie lightly, without strain, so that the break is aligned on the arm and on the elbow; 
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	then align the break as it should be, and restrain it, if abscesses do not come.  
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess comes, do not extract it until seven days, and put on moistened linen in wine and rose oil, until the abscess is calmed.  
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then extract it, and the way to extract it is that you put the plaster on the break, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; 
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put the cloth, and extract on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place of stars, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved. 
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone moves, use splints, and put on the break a splint larger and stronger than the others, and have between each splint two fingers of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes the break three fingers on each side; 
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then pull upwards on the splints, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter about fractures, pulling harder and less apart. 
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the seating of the splints and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you are setting the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, then leave it tied until the seventh day, as we have said; 
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then look at the bandage every three days, so that it does not itch or swell, or that swelling does not come to the place where the bandages are too tight.  
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is dislocated, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if none of these accidents occur, do not untie it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put a cushion of wool evenly under the shoulder and look every hour during the day or night that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or that the bandages are not loosened; 
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if he heals by virtue of medicine, and gives him the meat we have put before in such a way that the meat is first subtle; 
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it begins to recover, it should be thick.  
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be recovered in 40 days altogether; 
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must unbind it and administer baths and ointments for healing the place.  
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is ugly and obstructed, it will remain tied up for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	Of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "two humerus," one of which is small and is that which enters the shoulder pouch. 
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	And the other is large and is that which is below towards the little finger.  
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	Perhaps only the large humerus breaks, or only the small one, or perhaps both together. 
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small humerus is broken, restoration is easy and healing is quick.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large ones are broken, so is the healing bad, and more grievous than when they are broken together. 
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only a small bone that is broken, then it is necessary to extend it lightly and set it straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the large bone, then it is necessary to bind more strongly; 
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it on a cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small ones lower than the other bones, and let the patient be crossed upon himself, and the cushion in front of him higher up so that the patient does not suffer any hardship.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then extend the ministers' arms below his hand or at the elbow, and another minister above. 
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the sights equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is none detached that you can grasp by the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, do so with a bone saw, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a singular chapter; 
si pren la cure.	then take care of it. 
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if at the beginning of the restoration boils should arise, then apply a plaster of cerate made of rose oil and white wax, that it is neither too hard nor too soft; 
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and I lay a cloth over it subtly, until the abscess is calmed down. 
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then I remove the wax, and I put a plaster made from mill flour with plenty of egg yolks, and then I place bandages, and let the bandage from the break be stronger now, and a little wider than the others; 
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that it must have six bandages or arms in several positions: 
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the break is in one of the bones, or in two; 
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and apply more pressure above the break than anywhere else, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; 
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the cloths above the break be soft and moist, and not hard or rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread with which it is bound be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. 
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And inspect the limb and the bandage after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any bad accidents come to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must pour hot water on the limb until the itching is appeased. 
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And let the limb not be tightly confined. 
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again the tightening, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones loosened, and similar things, so be it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you are careful so that the nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little and leave it like that for a few days until the nourishment can flow and then remove it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things which we have said happen to the patient, then do not unbind him for 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	Or when he is in pain, then let him put his hands on his neck, and let his necks be equal, and beware of movement and shaking, and sleep on his back. 
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And know that this fracture is restored in 30 days or in 35, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the temperaments and complexions of the virtues.  
de la brisure de la main	of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and as we have two fingers there are often small fractures, and they only bring weeping many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the sole of the hand is broken or bent, it is fitting that the patient sit cross-legged, and sit straight in front of him equally. 
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then put his hand on the outstretched table, and extend the ministers the broken bones, and put them equal to the meridians, as long as they are well joined.  
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and put on a poultice and bandages, if no abscess forms, then he puts a splint according to the size of the place; 
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and it should be wrapped in a linen cloth. 
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is in the middle of the sole of the foot, he makes a splint of cloths, and instructs the patient to bind it to his broken sole; 
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then he binds it with a long cloth, and the splint should be as wide as the palm of the hand, and bind it as is appropriate.  
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the forearm, it is necessary that you put a splint on top and another underneath on the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie the whole hand around, and make the bandage tight between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture occurs in any of the bones of the fingers, if it is the thumb, he sets it straight, as is appropriate; 
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and binds it with the palm, and if you see fit, he puts a small straight splint to lift the fracture, so that it does not move;  
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	And if the fracture is on any other finger, such as the index finger or one of the others, set it equal and bind it with the healthy finger that follows. 
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	Or you tie them all together in a splint, which is worth more, or put them on a board, such as a pouch; 
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And take care in the restoration and arrangement of a hot abscess, and help those who come to it, as I have said. 
de la cuixe brisie	of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The thighbone is often broken, and one can see it well when it turns forward and backward; 
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	And the restoration consists in tying one splint above the fracture and the other below. 
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his bandage to his share equally; 
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.  
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, one of the ligatures should be towards the knee, and the other ligatures below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is near the knee, then let the bandage be below the knee, and let the extension be downwards. 
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Then place the splints so that the bone is equal to his two hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster and bandage, if abscesses do not appear there. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it cool down and then return to your work and treatment; 
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The bandage is made in this manner. 
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary that you wrap the bandage tightly doubled two or three times, and leave any excess, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the buttock, and pass a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the end of the thread above; 
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn up the leg and thigh the bandage, then place on the fracture splints, and put a splint on the bone of the leg. 
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then fill the space between the leg and thigh with soft cloths to make the constriction equal, then begin to bind with three or four turns on the fracture. 
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	And when you go further above the fracture, loosen the binding.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then take the two ends of the thread that you have placed between the leg and thigh, and bind three splints that are above them, then return below to the head of the thread, as far down as the foot.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And loosen it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, until no abscess, swelling or other such thing appears.  
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if one occurs, untie it and treat what has come as we have said many times. 
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	And if there are bone fragments that stick out, it is necessary to remove them, if possible.  
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	And if not, it is necessary to split the area and draw out the force. 
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And treat it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And whenever the thigh is broken, just as one puts splints in the shoulder and arm; 
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	In all cases, in such a restoration the patient does not falter.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in 10 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the varieties of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the hollow of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the passage of the knee, there is not often a break, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, unless it is just a crack or a hole, and occurs in all wounds, and open wounds, and this is felt well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is done so that what is crooked is aligned with its peers as much as possible.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then apply the plaster and a round splint if needed, and remove it as necessary. Then observe all the precautions that we have mentioned for other fractures, such as abscesses, cauterization, and other similar things.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it meets each situation, so that he may be healed. 
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that the leg has two bones, one of which is called "mustelz" and the other "foscile". 
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And there are all kinds of fractures as they occur in the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as that for the arm, and the work is the same. And if both bones are broken together, the leg turns in all directions. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bones are broken, so turn them forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and sees it well.
et torne desoz.	And it turns downwards. 
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then apply extension and set it equal, and bind the splints equally. 
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	But nevertheless, if the break is bad and there are several pieces, the extension should be smaller and lighter.
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and age according to your virtue. 
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two bandages of willow wood that can bind the leg on one side and the other, and let them be as long as the leg from the knee down; 
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap them twice both above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this binding the leg cannot decline to the right or left, and thus it is well; 
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and no one should administer sticks as long as the leg, and if it is of willow wood, put them on the leg to prevent movement, and properly make these in the fracture or where there is a wound; 
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move the leg every day to see if there is a hot abscess or another accident;  
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	until the cure so that it is healed. 
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the breaking of bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle does not suffer a fracture, but the bones of the foot sometimes break, and there are two ways this can happen.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if it happens that a bone in the foot is broken, and you see these bones rise up against each other, then have the patient put their foot on the ground as if they were about to walk, and then place your foot on theirs where the bones are raised, and then press until they return to their place. 
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then put on a plaster and bandages over it, and place under the belly of the foot a small board two finger widths thick, then straighten the foot carefully, and once you have wrapped it in cloths and other things that you need.  
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if any of the two bones are broken, set them as we have said for the bones of the hand. 
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then place a splint on the broken bone according to the length of the bone, and let it be a bit wider, then put under the foot that board which I have mentioned, and straighten it carefully. 
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, place on each bone two splints according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and remove the table from under the foot. 
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let it be standing on the head of the table beyond the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well. 
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is fitting that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said. 
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and treat each incident as appropriate.  
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the bone with a dagger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bones of a woman's nature are broken, make her sit wide, then incline her towards the back, and let her be held from behind. 
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	Then fill the vulva of the patient with cotton, and put in it as large a piece as a fist.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	Then untie the woman, and lift her back little by little, and then pull the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of the nature, and return the bone with the stock. 
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and do this for seven days or so. 
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	The fracture will be restored, and if you see it, take a bladder of a lamb, tie a cane to the opening, and insert the whole bladder into the nature. 
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	Then blow through the cane until the bladder is inflated inside.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	The body will set the fracture. 
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then fill it with cotton and leave it like that for several days until it is healed.  
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of a man or woman's shoulder is broken, restore it as we have said for the hip bone.
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And these fractures are not hidden from those who put their study and practice into it, and understand my book. 
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture indicates in several ways the right way to restore it. 
enten le donques.	Understand then. 
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	When a rod is broken, take a goose's throat and put the rod in it.  
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	Then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days or so, and it will heal quickly. 
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that he be poulticed now, so that the poultices that we have mentioned testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, and you have no other remedy, then restart to restore the fracture in the same hour, or that day, so that an abscess does not form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if boils come up, leave the restoration until a new day, as long as the boil is calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you will bring about evil accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent upon the chest uncovered, it behoves you to put it straight lightly with your hands, in small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension does not appear to you to be equal with your hands, then the surgeon has this instrument made of iron, which is seven or eight fingers long, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound. 
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	And it is necessary for him to soak it in three or four [of something unspecified], according to what he needs for each fracture treatment.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and it should be round and one large lump, so that it does not flatten under pressure on the limb during your work, and it should be sharp in front, and thick from the middle forward, thus: 
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called a "palainche," for which reason it is necessary that the curved head be placed on the head of the exposed bone; 
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and the end is brought down once, so that it returns and they are equal to one another. 
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, then it behooves you to cut off the head of the bone, so long as the instruments have power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, if the head of a suitable instrument for this, either an incisor or a saw, is at your disposal; 
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then remove that which remains in the bone of sharpness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is put back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	Do this so that it is in its place, then soak the bandage in black stiptic wine, and carefully if it is summer; 
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	And do not put any plaster or other thing on the wound where it has oil, lest it bring forth rot and corruption; 
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	Then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and bind a covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not strained with the fracture; 
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	And many times this foolish error has been made, and has brought death upon the patient or corrosion some time;  
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the constrictions be softer and gentler than other fractures. 
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil accidents may come, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it is not right to put splints on; 
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but bind around, instead of splints, hard cloths, and tie them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound has begun to swell, remove what you have put on it altogether and apply a healing ointment, such as tetrapharmacum ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be aligned in such a way that the bone runs down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day they pass through and it cannot be soldered but keeps coming back down, know that there are small pieces of bone; for which you must want the wound with a tent, and remove all these loose pieces which cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, it is fitting that you cure it according to what it says in its chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large bones, do not draw it out at all, for often death follows, but leave it until it rots; 
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	perhaps it will fall off by itself after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if you can. 
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if you cannot, leave it. 
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the boils which come from the solder
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	Many times after the healing of a fracture, especially when it is near a joint, it is a sorry sight to see the shape of the limb. 
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	And perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions. 
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take heed then if it is fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if you administer astringent medicines such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, so that you take any of these things or all together and mix them with astringent wine or with egg yolk or with oil; 
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and put them on a new bandage, and remove it well, and do not untie it for any day; 
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	And then dislocate it, and start another, until the nodules are removed;  
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you strain on a well-made plank; 
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of the plank is that it removes all swellings from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the nodule has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then put a cup on top of it, and make the superfluity appear;  
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you shave it with a razor until it is removed, and care for it until it is healed. 
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and the limbs remain weak and subtle afterwards, it happens for many reasons: 
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	For one reason it is because it was tied too tight, and it was not tied as it should have been. 
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	Or because there were too many bandages, and the nourishment could not reach the limb.
ou por multitude d’arosement;	Or because of a multitude of irritations. 
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	Or because of too large movements, not at its proper time. 
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	Or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.  
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and soften the body, until the blood is multiplied in him; 
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and give him baths, and give him joy and rest. 
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	Then apply pitch to the limb, so that the pitch attracts great nourishment, and often bathe it in warm water, until the nourishment runs to the limb. 
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and return to its natural shape. 
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bones are open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: 
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb anew, and many a fool has done this in our land; 
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this work is blamed, and it brings great evils, and perhaps death;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	nevertheless, if the dislocations and torments are fresh, it is fitting that they be raised with hot water, or softening herbs be cooked, such as leaves of mallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; 
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and make a softening plaster, such as diachylon well made, and you take the mucilage of mallow, and mix it with gelatine grease or sesame oil, and make a plaster upon it;  
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	Take fat figs and crush them with bran and similar medicines that reduce inflammation. 
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is dislocation removed by continuous and lengthy rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let movement be administered to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the tortuosity is old and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, then it must be cut up to the bone with a subtle and light incision.  
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And put cinders and plaster on the wound. 
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, so that it cannot move, and the limb is misaligned, and the patient feels great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, it is necessary now to bring it back without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, it swells up and by chance puts it back in place;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	Therefore, it should not be moved while it is swollen.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	Many times this brings on spasms and other pains. 
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	In all cases, when this occurs, make the patient healthy, then leave him alone until the abscess has been calmed.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then loosen it gently and treat each limb as the treatment comes to its place. 
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that both jaws are dislocated, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners. 
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	Either they are sometimes loosened from their places, and softened a little.
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Or they are entirely dislocated and hang toward the ground, cutting off saliva from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and envelops his tongue with speech. 
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by means of several arrangements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it quickly, and do not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	And in such a manner that the assistants hold the head of the patient, and put the tip of one of his fingers into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth if the dislocation is of two parts.  
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	And the other hand should be free to place it evenly. 
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to soften them, his jaws, and move them in all directions. 
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he looks at the eye equal, as long as it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if bringing them back is difficult, even when the two jaws are together, then apply a mixture of hot water and oil, until they soften slightly; 
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	do not try to force them back in place, as we have said. 
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without softening, then put soft cloths soaked in cerate made of rose oil and wax on them, and then bind them lightly with soft linen cloths. 
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on his back, with his head resting between two pillows so that he does not move it to the right or left, nor strain to chew, but take light food, until the pain is gone and the jaws are healed. 
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then chew lightly what he wants, and do not bother to open his mouth to eat and drink until the mandible is well joined and healed. 
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be put back in place within an hour and are not returned to their position, then fevers and accustomed sweats arise, and possibly a loosening of the bowels, and possibly vomiting of bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is lost; 
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times he who had it died in nine days.  
de la forcelle	from the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislocate within the sides of the continuation of the foot, and it is dislocated sometimes at a distance, and one can feel this well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back and extends his arms; 
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the place with your palm, and it will return;  
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put plaster on top and bandage it, and remove it; 
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the head which is toward the elbow cannot dislocate;  
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it does, and if it dislocates any time, reset it in its place as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then apply plaster and bandage it, remove it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed. 
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And in the same way, the head of the shoulder is reset when it is dislocated from its place. 
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only according to three ways: 
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	One of which is that it dislocates towards the part of the armpit below; 
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	And the second is towards the part of the buttock;  
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	And rarely it dislocates upwards, and this happens seldom. 
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	And it does not dislocate backwards for the shoulder, nor inwards for the nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	And often it dislocates below towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, for in them it happens quickly. 
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	To those who have enough flesh, it jumps out at the points, and goes back in at the points. 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And it sometimes happens to some men that they have a bruise or fracture, and their shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	Therefore you must try it until you are certain of it;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment. 
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that a dislocation occurs when it falls toward the armpit, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear distinction between them; 
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and below the armpit at the humerus, the head of the shoulder as if it were a bone; 
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring their hand back to its nest, nor move in any way;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated upward, unless it is hidden, because you will find it distinctly at the humerus; 
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this manner of dislocation is not very difficult to reset when it is new, or if the child is ill. 
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	The manner is that the attendants lift the patient's arm above, then place their fingers under the armpit, and lift the joint with force upward to its place; 
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the attendants lift the hand, and extend it upward, then put it below;
si venra hastanment.	it will come quickly. 
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said in the first days afterward, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; 
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the attendant apply a softening and soothing liniment, such as a decoction of altaea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and apply it;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then let the patient be laid on their back, and put under the armpit a cloth of wool equally thick, not too soft nor too hard, then place the patient's heel on the cloth, and lift the head of the shoulder virtuously, and pull the hand of the patient; 
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another minister hold the head of the patient so that it does not move downwards; 
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	this shoulder will now return to its place, and if you see the resetting according to this manner: 
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and that you have a man who is larger than the patient be present; 
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and stand straight towards the side, and put his shoulder under the armpit of the patient, and lift the armpit upwards so that the patient hangs on the arm; 
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another minister pulls the hand of the patient downwards towards the belly. 
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can hold something heavy with him, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And resetting can also be done in another way: 
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and that one sticks a long burning coal into the ground, whose head is as round as a pistol, and is neither too thick nor too thin; 
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it is placed under the patient, but let him have cloths soaked in vinegar above, and the patient is lying along the length of a log; 
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then let his hand be extended on the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly. 
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	And if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this treatment: 
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	Take a firebrand two arms long and four thumbs wide, which has a pointed head to enter perfectly under the armpit, according to this form: 
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	Then tie two cloths soaked in vinegar under the pointed end of the firebrand so that it does not burn the patient, then place it under the patient's armpit. 
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	Extend his arm up the length of the firebrand and tie the shoulder to the firebrand, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on a large ladder's rung, and let his hand hang down on the other side. 
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint must now be put back together. 
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, no matter how, it is fitting that you put under the armpit a sphere of wool equal in size, then apply a plaster prepared with powder from the mill, with incense and egg yolk, on all the shoulder and around it, then bind it under the armpit firmly, and return the bandage over the plaster, and embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he rest a bit, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; 
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then rest more afterwards for five or seven days, and move it; 
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is firm and not softened, then it is healed. 
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has been moved out of place due to moisture that has come upon it, or for another reason, it is fitting that you administer cauteries at three points, as it is laid down in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot raise his arm upward, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; 
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place. 
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	Dislocation which is towards the hip and breasts or behind, is done by force and extension of the hands and administered elsewhere; 
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal until it is healthy. 
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes stiffness in the limb, and slowness in movement, then let the patient bathe many times until that stiffness is relieved and it returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation one cuts
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the knife is dislocated at points, and at points it returns; 
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and if it is dislocated from all sides, and even in front and behind, the dislocation is not put back in place, for one can see it well and feel it well; 
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and it is dislocated according to each figure. 
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick cautery with the healthy one, if you can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is raised, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And you must reset it in the same way as abscesses should come, for if an abscess were to come, it would be harmful to reset it; 
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and by chance it cannot be put back in place entirely, even when it is at the back; 
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	it is worse than the other dislocations and causes greater pain, and by chance death comes. 
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is such that when it can be reset like this, you extend your hand with both hands.
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And let his arms be spread out, and his hands put in according to the angle of the knife, above and below, and push the joint towards his thumbs together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place. 
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and tightens from the root of the palm or the costal bone which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, apply strong extension;  
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and when the minister extends the arm and holds it so that it does not move during extension; 
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a long and wide double cloth around it;  
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the surgeon joins the joint to his hand, he should anoint it with oil to soften the joint, then push the joint together firmly until it returns; 
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, apply a dry plaster with egg yolk, bind it firmly and sling the arm to the patient's neck, and leave it for several days before releasing it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the ligature, and leave it. 
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	And if you see that the joint does not hold well, start over with the plaster and the ligature, and leave it like that for several days, until it is firmly in place. 
puis le deslie.	Then untie it. 
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels stiffness after the joint is reset and it moves, bathe it and rub it well, and press it until it is relieved. 
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	Or you put a greasy sheep's wool bandage on the joint, then leave it for one day and a night, then remove it, and let it enter the bath. 
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	And when he sweats, if he rubs the joint moderately, then put the bandage back on and then enter the bath. 
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And thus do it two or three times, until he is healed. 
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see it, put cow dung moistened with heated butter on it, and strain it. 
si revenra a sa disposition.	It will return to its proper place. 
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand dislocates and returns easily, more so than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to return it to its place quickly, in the same hour that it dislocates, so that the flesh does not swell, or an abscess comes hot. 
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the putting back in place is done as follows: you put the sick hand on a table and extend the patient's hand; look at it, and make sure it is straight so that they place their palm facing the appearance of the joint, and push until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	Nevertheless, you must look to see if it is well in place; 
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Then put the patient's back on a table for stretching and pulling. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient put the back of his hand on the table, and the doctor put his hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, that is good. 
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, apply poultices to soothe the abscess and leave it like that without restarting.  
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, the joint will remain crooked; 
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and do not harm the patient further than that, as long as his hand is weakened and he cannot grasp anything at all.  
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	Then know that the nerves are cut, or the artery. 
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If there is no other remedy except to pull it out with a cautery, and by chance nothing else will do.  
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for 5 days, then unbind it and leave it as is.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some pain, then apply warm water and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the shoulders of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the joints of the hand are dislocated at any point, sometimes on the back of the palm or in the hollow. 
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then apply force, and push the dislocation towards your thumbs until it returns, then hold the head of the joint, and bend it towards the side where it is separated; 
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for two days, and then set it equal that day; 
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	And at night the bandage, as we have said, and untie it during the day, and make it move, and re-bandage it at night; 
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated in the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; 
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do the same when it is dislocated elsewhere. 
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Concerning the loosening of the shoulder blade from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade of the back or neck is dislocated, if there are several dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the limbs jump with force involuntarily, and he cannot hold them, and often some limb is softened, either both thighs or both arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And many times the shinbone breaks into four parts; 
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	That which breaks in back is called "gilbositez." 
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The cure is that you set it if the "gilbositez" came from childhood: 
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there is neither cure nor healing at all. 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient manners of cures are said in many words, where there is not much profit in all; 
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.  
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the "gilbositez" which comes at the back of the foot, there is neither remedy nor healing; 
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes straight to the two sides, and one cannot cure except for that which properly comes to the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient be extended on his face in an equal place, and have a support below him so he does not become bruised. 
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then put one ember at the head in the earth formed, and the other at the feet, and tie a band under the armpits of the patient, and another at the thighs, and at the knees, and at the ankles; 
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two assistants hold the bands, one at the head and the others at the feet, between the two embers.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well closed, the ember as we have said, and the surgeon put his palms on the spine in a formed way, until it returns. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this treatment, then take a table of three arm's length, and place it below the wall, and let the patient be on his side, and put the head of the table below the wall, then put the middle of the table on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and put the patient's feet on the other end of the table, and press hard, until it returns to its place. 
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if you see it, do it with a wrench that turns in the hand.  
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And place two burning coals at the head of the patient's arm, and two others towards the feet, with a palm's length of space between each coal.
