et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	And make a hole in each coal, through which the wrench can pass, and set the coals firmly in the ground so they don't move. 
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And between each pair of coals place a turning coal, with which the wrench turns, and have two small coals of a palm's length in the two turnings to turn the wrench. 
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Then tie the string among the splints to the wrench at the head and the other string to the other wrench towards the feet, and each of the assistants turns his wrench along the entire string, and the master puts the spine straight as we have said. 
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when they are equal, put a drying plaster on them with plenty of egg white, and then bandages, and then the strip of a tablet three fingers long, which covers the place of the gibbosity and the part of the spine that is sound, then tie it with a ligature as we have said, and use the patient with subtle nourishment, until he is healed; 
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	and if anything comes at the end of health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the strip that we have said before; 
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	and never administer a piece of plum, and never does the appearance come in the back spine of the back, and we think that it is dislocation; 
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and it is the bone that appears, for which one should not have any presumption:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	By chance it might bring death. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come loose by dislocations, not like the other joints. 
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	And the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	inwards and outwards, and in front and behind. 
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	And more inwards than elsewhere, and rarely dislocated in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of this dislocation inwards is that when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick knee appears more open than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee at the fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And there is a swelling of a hot abscess, because the head of the thigh comes there. 
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one to whom it comes is death, if this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of the one who has it in front is that their leg is stretched according to its completion.
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	Everywhere, do not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants to make it go, it cannot before, and it retains its urine, and swells the groin, and when it goes, it passes over the heel. 
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who has it behind are that he cannot extend his knee or bend it, and the leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The reduction of this kind of dislocation is such that you recognize if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its arrangement, there is no cure; 
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and one should not presume. 
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways of dislocation, hasten that you return the joint, and extend it inside and out, and move it to the right and left. 
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	Perhaps it will return, and needs no other treatment.  
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this way, it is necessary that you prepare a strong minister, and extend the leg strongly with two hands, or with a bandage that is tied above the knee.  
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	And another minister extends his hand over it in such a way that he puts his hands under his armpits, then he binds it with a strong cord on the thigh; 
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	And another holds the head of the cord; 
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they stretch up and down all at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.  
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four resemblances, and if the dislocation returns as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If this does not work, it is necessary to apply a remedy according to its likeness. 
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is in the shoulder blade, it is necessary that you place the patient on his healthy side, then put the bandage at the root of the thigh and the place below the angle, then stretch the bandage upwards towards the angle and towards the armpit; 
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	then another minister takes his arms and embraces the thick part of the sick thigh and stretches it out in a straight form; 
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	if it will return to its place now; 
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot hold it in this manner as we have said, it is fitting that you bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong bandage above the two heels and above the two knees, and let the injured leg be extended two fists longer than the other;  
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then it should be hung on the top of a post, and be raised two arms' lengths above the ground; 
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then command a minister to embrace the top of the thigh, and let another minister hang with the patient who embraces the bottom of the thigh, for the joint will now return quickly.  
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at the hip, let the patient lie down as we have said for the one with sciatica, and tighten the bandage on the injured leg properly, and on the foot also; 
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put two embers, one at the head and the other at the feet, then insert one ember between the patient's thighs in the shape of a figure-eight. 
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And place cloths moistened with water around them so that they do not burn the patient, then extend each ember towards him and have the patient hold their dislocated limb equal to his hand. 
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put it on a table, and press it down as we have said in the treatment of dislocations, and lay the patient on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is in front, you must quickly extend the patient's injured leg according to what I have said. 
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And place the embers so that their heat is on the injured angle, then press with the other hand and extend it downwards towards the knee.  
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is in back, it is not right to extend the patient downwards or lift them up, but rather they should be as if their hip were dislocated in back, as we have said about lying on both hips. 
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	And let it be upon its face, and the bandage extended as we have said before, and one must press upon the joint at the table. 
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	It will be done when the patient extends his legs, and they will be equal.
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	Then adjust the thighs, and apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move. 
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	And let him rest for three or four days, then untie it, and apply plaster on top.
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	And if you see that they are equal, bind it as before, and leave it for three days. 
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	Then untie it, and let him walk gently, until the limb is strengthened.  
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The knee is dislocated according to three methods: 
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	That is to say, inwards and outwards, and behind.
et ne desalue point devant.	And do not dislocate it again. 
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you order the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not straighten at his thigh, know that it is dislocated; 
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; 
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take his knee in your palms, and draw it between your thighs, then bend the two sides that form the knee; 
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another minister extends his foot, as long as the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he straightens his leg at his thigh easily; 
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and put the plaster on it, and let the leg air at the thigh, and tie them together tightly for three days or four, then untie it; 
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And let the patient not move until their limb is comfortable. 
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The tendons are sometimes loosened, and sometimes completely dislocated, both within and without.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tense before the part where it is dislocated: 
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The resetting should be gentle, and one must extend the arm slightly with their hands when it is only bruised.  
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated altogether, you must make the patient sit upright and hold them firmly by the leg, above the ankle; 
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then draw the foot toward you with your right hand, and then to the left twice, then extend it upward and push the foot up well; 
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot;  
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	if it returns, it is good; 
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if not, start the work again, for it will return; 
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return this way, have the patient lay on their back on the ground, and fix a strong stick firmly into the ground between their thighs, and bind cloths around it so that it does not hurt the patient. 
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then have one assistant hold the thigh, and another assistant extend the foot to their hands or to a cord which they tie around the ankle. 
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then have each assistant extend evenly, and let the stick be now between the patient's thighs to hold them steady when they are being stretched. 
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then place your hands evenly on the dislocation and have another assistant hold the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly. 
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is back in place, put a poultice and bandages on top, and bind them firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and be careful of the nerves which are on the ankle behind so that the bandages are not too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	Then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligaments loosen, strain it. 
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	Then untie it on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient from moving for four days.  
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if he goes before that time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, it is necessary that you appease it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if it pleases them to stretch beautifully without exertion, and that is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or foot, it is fitting that you make the patient sit on a flat place or on a table perfectly straight, and put your foot on what appears of those joints, then press with your foot strongly, until it returns. 
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	And when it is equal and nothing appears, put under the sole of the foot a two-legged table, then strain it strongly and leave it for three days, then untie it. 
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let him rest until he is healed.  
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and of dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies. 
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you are not presumptuous in the cure, if you are wise in the art and have used it for a long time, and if you are pitiful and merciful and slow, do not be bold. 
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	And use at the beginning soothing things to calm the abscess down, and leave the patient in the hand of God if you do not see hope for health. 
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, now reset the limb in its place so that the abscess may drain.  
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is in place, administer soothing things to calm the abscess down and treat the wound as it should be with drying ointments. 
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if with the dislocation there is a break and small bones are detached, set the bones and do what we have said in simple ailments.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and guard yourself from entering the path of fear, according to what I have said, for this is worth more according to your Creator, and for the safety of your weapon and your body.
